Gen 1:1 In the beginning when God created the heavens and the earth, <br>		
Gen 1:2 the earth was still unformed and chaotic, <br>		with darkness on the surface of the abyss, <br>		and the spirit of God hovering over the waters. <br>		
Gen 1:3 God said, ‘Let there be light,’ and there was light. <br>		
Gen 1:4 God saw that the light was good. <br>		He separated the light from the darkness, <br>		
Gen 1:5 calling the light ’day’ and the darkness ’night’. <br>	There was an evening and a morning, making the first day. <br><br>	
Gen 1:6 Then God said, ‘Let there be a dome between the waters, <br>		and let it separate the waters from the waters.’ <br>		
Gen 1:7 So God made the dome to separate the waters below <br>		from the waters which were above it. <br>			It was so. <br>		
Gen 1:8 God called the dome the ’sky’. <br>	There was an evening and a morning, making the second day. <br><br>	
Gen 1:9 Then God said, ‘Let the waters under the sky be gathered together, <br>		and let the dry ground appear.’ <br>			It was so. <br>		
Gen 1:10 God called the dry ground ’land’ <br>		and he called the gathered waters ’seas’. <br>			God saw that it was good. <br><br>	
Gen 1:11 God said, ‘Let the earth put forth vegetation: <br>		Plants on the earth which yield their own kind of seed, <br>		and trees that bear fruits in which are their own seed.’ <br>			It was so. <br>		
Gen 1:12 The earth sprouted vegetation: <br>		seed-bearing plants, <br>		and trees with seed-bearing fruit. <br>			God saw that it was good. <br>	
Gen 1:13 There was an evening and a morning, making the third day. <br><br>	
Gen 1:14 Then God said, ‘Let there be lights in the dome of the sky <br>		to separate the night from the day. <br>		Let them be signs to mark the seasons, the days, and the years. <br>		
Gen 1:15 Let them be lights in the dome of the sky to light the earth.’ <br>			It was so. <br>		
Gen 1:16 So God made the two great lights: <br>		The greater to rule the day and the lesser to rule the night. <br><br>	God made the stars also. 
Gen 1:17 He placed all these lights in the dome of the sky <br>		to shed light upon the earth, <br>		
Gen 1:18 to rule over the day and over the night, <br>		and to separate light from darkness. <br>			God saw that it was good. <br>	
Gen 1:19 There was an evening and a morning, making the fourth day. <br><br>	
Gen 1:20 Then God said, ‘Let the waters teem with living creatures, <br>		and let birds fly over the earth in the open dome of the sky.’ <br>		
Gen 1:21 God created the great sea monsters, <br>		all kinds of living, moving creatures with which the waters teem, <br>		and all kinds of winged birds. <br>			God saw that it was good. <br>		
Gen 1:22 He blessed them, saying, ‘Be fruitful, <br>		increase, fill the oceans, <br>		and let the birds increase on the land.’ <br>	
Gen 1:23 There was an evening and a morning, making the fifth day. <br><br>	
Gen 1:24 Then God said, ‘Let the earth produce all kinds of living creatures: <br>		cattle and reptiles and wild beasts.’ <br>			It was so. <br>		
Gen 1:25 So God made all the different kinds of wild beasts, <br>		and the cattle, and everything that crawls upon the ground. <br>			God saw that it was good. <br><br>	
Gen 1:26 Then God said, ‘Let us make humans who are images of us, who are like us. <br>		Let them rule over the fish of the sea, <br>		the birds of the sky, the cattle, the wild beasts, <br>		and all the reptiles that crawl upon the ground.’ <br>		
Gen 1:27 So God created humans in his image, <br>			he created them in the image of God. <br>		He created them male and female. <br><br>	
Gen 1:28 Then God blessed them, and said to them: <br>		‘Be fruitful, grow in number, <br>		fill the earth and govern it; <br>		rule over the fish of the sea, the birds of the sky, <br>		and over every living thing that crawls on the ground,’ <br><br>	
Gen 1:29 God said, ‘I give you every seed-bearing plant <br>		throughout all the earth, <br>		and every tree that has seed-bearing fruit. <br>		They will be food for you, <br>		
Gen 1:30 and to every wild beast and to every bird of the sky, <br>		and to everything that crawls on the earth - <br>		everything with the breath of life in it, <br>		I give every green plant for food.’ <br>			It was so. <br>		
Gen 1:31 When God saw all that he had made, <br>		he perceived that it was very good. <br>	There was an evening and a morning, making the sixth day. <br><br>	
Gen 2:1 So the heavens and the earth were finished, and everything in them. <br>		
Gen 2:2 When on the seventh day God finished the work which he had done, <br>		he rested that day from all his work. <br>		
Gen 2:3 God blessed the seventh day and set it apart, <br>		for in it he rested from all the creative work which he had done.  ¶ 
Gen 2:4 This is the story of the heavens and earth when they were created. <br> ¶ At the time when the  <c>Lord</c> God made earth and heaven, 
Gen 2:5 there were not yet any plants on the earth, and no vegetation had sprung up; for the  <c>Lord</c> God had not sent rain upon the earth, and there was no one to till the soil. 
Gen 2:6 A mist used to rise from the earth and water all the surface of the ground.  ¶ 
Gen 2:7 Then the  <c>Lord</c> God moulded a human being out of dust taken from the ground and breathed into his nostrils the breath of life, and he became a living being. 
Gen 2:8 The  <c>Lord</c> God planted a garden in Eden, far in the East; and placed the human he had formed there. 
Gen 2:9 From the soil the  <c>Lord</c> God made grow all kinds of trees that are pleasant to look at and good for food, with the tree of life also in the middle of the garden and the tree that gives the knowledge of good and evil.  ¶ 
Gen 2:10 A river flowed out of Eden and watered the garden, and from there branched into four. 
Gen 2:11 The name of the first is Pishon, which flows round the whole land of Havilah, where there is gold. 
Gen 2:12 The gold of that land is pure and there is aromatic gum and the onyx stone. 
Gen 2:13 The name of the second river is Gihon, which flows round the whole land of Cush, 
Gen 2:14 and the name of the third river is the Tigris, which heads toward the east of Asshur. The fourth river is the Euphrates.  ¶ 
Gen 2:15 Then the  <c>Lord</c> God took the human and placed him in the garden of Eden to till it and to care for it. 
Gen 2:16 The  <c>Lord</c> God also gave the human this command: ‘You may freely eat from every tree of the garden, 
Gen 2:17 except from the tree that gives the knowledge of good and evil; from this you must not eat, for on the day that you eat from it you will surely die.’  ¶ 
Gen 2:18 Then the  <c>Lord</c> God said, ‘It is not good for the human to be alone; I will make a helper suited to him.’ 
Gen 2:19 So out of the ground the  <c>Lord</c> God formed all the wild beasts and birds, and made them come to the human to see what he would call them. Whatever he called each living creature, that was its name. 
Gen 2:20 So the human, Adam gave names to all cattle and all the wild birds and beasts. But there was no companion suitable for him.  ¶ 
Gen 2:21 Then the  <c>Lord</c> God caused the human to fall into a deep sleep, and while he slept, he took one of his ribs and closed up its place with flesh. 
Gen 2:22 With the rib which he had taken from the human, the  <c>Lord</c> built up a woman and brought her to the human. 
Gen 2:23 Then the human said, ‘This now is bone of my bone and flesh of my flesh. She will be called Woman, for from man she was taken.’ 
Gen 2:24 For this reason a man leaves his father and his mother and clings to his wife, and the two become one flesh.  ¶ 
Gen 2:25 The man and his wife were both naked, yet felt no shame.  ¶ 
Gen 3:1 Now the snake was craftier than any other wild beast that the  <c>Lord</c> God had made. It said to the woman, ‘Has God really said, “You must not eat from any tree of the garden”?’ 
Gen 3:2 The woman answered, ‘We are allowed to eat the fruit of all the trees of the garden; 
Gen 3:3 it is only about the fruit of the tree in the middle of the garden that God has said, “You must not eat from it, nor should you touch it, for if you do, you will die.”’ 
Gen 3:4 Then the snake said to the woman, ‘You will not die! 
Gen 3:5 God knows that on the day you eat some of it your eyes will be opened, and you will be like gods, knowing what is good and what is evil.’  ¶ 
Gen 3:6 When the woman saw that the tree was good for food, attractive to look at and desirable for acquiring wisdom, she took some of its fruit and ate. Then she gave some to her husband who was with her, and he ate.  ¶ 
Gen 3:7 Then the eyes of both of them were opened, and they  that they were naked, so they sewed fig-leaves together to cover themselves. 
Gen 3:8 But when they heard the sound of the  <c>Lord</c> God walking in the garden in the evening breeze, the man and his wife hid from him among the garden trees.  ¶ 
Gen 3:9 When the  <c>Lord</c> God called to the man, ‘Where are you?’ 
Gen 3:10 he replied, ‘I heard you in the garden and I was afraid, because I was naked, so I hid myself.’ 
Gen 3:11 The  <c>Lord</c> God said, ‘Who told you that you were naked? Did you eat from the tree from which I ordered you not to eat?’ 
Gen 3:12 The man answered, ‘The woman you placed beside me, she gave me fruit from the tree and I ate.’ 
Gen 3:13 The  <c>Lord</c> God said to the woman, ‘What is this that you have done?’ The woman replied, ‘The snake deceived me, and I ate.’  ¶ 
Gen 3:14 Then the  <c>Lord</c> God said to the snake: <br>	‘Because you have done this, <br>	you will be more accursed than all cattle <br>	and all the wild beasts. <br>	You will crawl on your belly <br>	and eat dust <br>	all your life. <br>	
Gen 3:15 I will establish hostility between you and the woman, <br>	between your offspring and hers, <br>	who will wound your head, <br>	and you will wound their heel.’  ¶ 
Gen 3:16 To the woman he said, <br>	‘I will greatly increase your anguished toil in pregnancy; <br>	with pain will you bear children. <br>	<br>	You will yearn for your husband, <br>	but he will rule over you.’  ¶ 
Gen 3:17 To Adam he said, <br>	‘Because you have listened to the voice of your wife, <br>	and ate from the tree <br>	about which I ordered you: <br>	’You must never eat from it’ <br>	the ground will be cursed because of you; <br>	as long as you live, you will earn a living only by anguished toil. <br><br>	
Gen 3:18 The ground will always bring forth thorns and thistles, <br>	and you will eat the plants of the field. <br>	
Gen 3:19 By the sweat of your brow you will eat bread, <br>	until you return to the ground, <br>	for from it you were taken; <br>	for dust you are, <br>	and to dust you will return!’  ¶ 
Gen 3:20 The man, Adam, named his wife Eve <sup>[ Heb Havvah, that is, Life. ]</sup>; because she was the mother of all living people. 
Gen 3:21 The  <c>Lord</c> God made clothes from animal skins for Adam and his wife and dressed them.  ¶ 
Gen 3:22 Then the  <c>Lord</c> God said: ‘The man has become like one of us, knowing good and evil. He must not reach out his hand, and take also from the tree of life, and eat, and live forever.’ 
Gen 3:23 So the  <c>Lord</c> God sent him out of the garden of Eden, to till the ground from which he had been taken. 
Gen 3:24 He drove out Adam and he placed at the east of the garden of Eden the cherubim, and the blazing whirling sword, to bar the way to the tree of life.           ¶ 
Gen 4:1 Adam lay with his wife Eve and she became pregnant and gave birth to Cain, and she said, ‘I have created a man with the help of the  <c>Lord</c>!’ 
Gen 4:2 She also gave birth to his brother Abel. Abel was a shepherd, while Cain was a farmer.  ¶ 
Gen 4:3 In the course of time Cain brought some of the ground’s produce as an offering to the  <c>Lord</c>. 
Gen 4:4 Abel too brought some of the choicest animals of his flock and sacrificed their fat pieces. The  <c>Lord</c> looked with approval on Abel and his offering 
Gen 4:5 but he could not receive Cain and his offering with approval.  ¶ Cain burned with anger and his face fell. 
Gen 4:6 So the  <c>Lord</c> said to Cain, ‘Why are you angry and why do you scowl? 
Gen 4:7 If you do what is right and good, can’t you hold your head up high? But if you do wrong, sin crouches at the door and longs to have you, but you must master it.’  ¶ 
Gen 4:8 Cain said to his brother Abel, ‘Let us go into the field.’ While they were there, Cain attacked his brother and killed him.  ¶ 
Gen 4:9 Then the  <c>Lord</c> asked Cain, ‘Where is your brother Abel?’ He answered, ‘I do not know! Am I my brother’s keeper?’  ¶ 
Gen 4:10 ‘What have you done?’ the  <c>Lord</c> replied, ‘Listen! Your brother’s blood is crying out to me from the ground. 
Gen 4:11 Even now you are cursed by the very ground that has opened to receive your brother’s blood shed by your hand. 
Gen 4:12 From now on when you till the ground, it will no longer yield its best to you. You will be a vagabond and a wandering refugee upon the earth.’  ¶ 
Gen 4:13 Then Cain said to the  <c>Lord</c>, ‘My punishment is too much for me to bear. 
Gen 4:14 Look! Today you banish me from the ground. I must hide in your presence. I will be a wandering refugee upon the earth, and whoever finds me will kill me!’  ¶ 
Gen 4:15 But the  <c>Lord</c> said to him, ‘If any one kills you, the crime shall be avenged sevenfold.’ So the  <c>Lord</c> placed a distinctive mark on Cain, to keep any one who found him from killing him. 
Gen 4:16 Cain departed from the  <c>Lord</c>’s presence and lived east of Eden in the land of Wandering.  ¶ 
Gen 4:17 Cain lay with his wife. She became pregnant, giving birth to Enoch. Cain built a city, and named it after his son Enoch. 
Gen 4:18 To Enoch was born Irad, and Irad fathered Mehujael, and Mehujael fathered Methushael, and Methushael fathered Lamech.  ¶ 
Gen 4:19 Lamech took two wives; the name of one was Adah, and the name of the other Zillah. 
Gen 4:20 Adah gave birth to Jabal, who became the ancestor of the people who live in tents and have cattle. 
Gen 4:21 His brother’s name was Jubal; he was the ancestor of the people who play the harp and flute. 
Gen 4:22 As for Zillah, she gave birth to Tubal-cain, who forged all sort of tools from copper and iron. The sister of Tubal-cain was Naamah.  ¶ 
Gen 4:23 Lamech said to his wives: <br>	‘Adah and Zillah, hear my voice; <br>		wives of Lamech, listen to my speech; <br>	because I have slain a man for wounding me, <br>		and a young man for bruising me. <br>	
Gen 4:24 If Cain is to be avenged sevenfold, <br>		then Lamech will be seventy and sevenfold.’  ¶ 
Gen 4:25 Adam lay with his wife again and she bore a son. She named him Seth: ‘because God gave me another son for Abel, who was killed by Cain.’ 
Gen 4:26 Seth too had a son. He named him Enosh. That was when people began worshipping in the name of  <c>Lord</c>.  ¶ 
Gen 5:1 This is the list of the descendants of Adam. On the day that God created human beings, he made them in his own image. 
Gen 5:2 He created them male and female created, and blessed them, and called their name Adam.  ¶ 
Gen 5:3 Adam lived for a hundred and thirty years, and had a son in his own likeness, after his image; and named him Seth. 
Gen 5:4 Adam lived for eight hundred years after he had Seth; and he had sons and daughters. 
Gen 5:5 In total, Adam lived for nine hundred and thirty years; and then he died.  ¶ 
Gen 5:6 Seth lived for a hundred and five years, and fathered Enosh. 
Gen 5:7 Seth lived a further eight hundred and seven years after he had Enosh, and had sons and daughters. 
Gen 5:8 In total, Seth lived for nine hundred and twelve years; and then he died.  ¶ 
Gen 5:9 Enosh lived for ninety years, and fathered Kenan. 
Gen 5:10 Enosh lived a further eight hundred and fifteen years after he had Kenan, and had sons and daughters. 
Gen 5:11 In total, Enosh lived for nine hundred and five years; and then he died.  ¶ 
Gen 5:12 Kenan lived for seventy years, and fathered Mahalalel. 
Gen 5:13 Kenan lived for eight hundred and forty years after he had Mahalalel, and had sons and daughters. 
Gen 5:14 In total, Kenan lived for nine hundred and ten years; and then he died.  ¶ 
Gen 5:15 Mahalalel lived for sixty and five years, and fathered Jared. 
Gen 5:16 Mahalalel lived for eight hundred and thirty years after he had Jared, and had sons and daughters. 
Gen 5:17 In total, Mahalalel lived for eight hundred ninety and five years; and then he died.  ¶ 
Gen 5:18 Jared lived for a hundred sixty and two years, and fathered Enoch. 
Gen 5:19 Jared lived for eight hundred years after he had Enoch, and had sons and daughters. 
Gen 5:20 In total, Jared lived for nine hundred sixty and two years; and then he died.  ¶ 
Gen 5:21 Enoch lived for sixty and five years, and fathered Methuselah. 
Gen 5:22 Enoch walked with God for three hundred years after he had Methuselah, and had sons and daughters. 
Gen 5:23 In total, Enoch lived for three hundred sixty and five years. 
Gen 5:24 Enoch walked with God, and then he was gone; because God took him.  ¶ 
Gen 5:25 Methuselah lived for a hundred eighty and seven years, and fathered Lamech. 
Gen 5:26 Methuselah lived for seven hundred eighty and two years after he had Lamech, and had sons and daughters. 
Gen 5:27 In total, Methuselah lived for nine hundred sixty and nine years; and then he died.  ¶ 
Gen 5:28 Lamech lived for a hundred eighty and two years, and had a son. 
Gen 5:29 He named him Noah, saying: ‘He will bring us relief from our work and the toil of our hands which comes from the ground the  <c>Lord</c> cursed.’ 
Gen 5:30 Lamech lived for five hundred ninety and five years after he had Noah, and had sons and daughters. 
Gen 5:31 In total, Lamech lived for seven hundred seventy and seven years; and then he died.  ¶ 
Gen 5:32 When Noah was five hundred years old, he fathered Shem, Ham, and Japheth.  ¶ 
Gen 6:1 When people began to multiply on the face of the earth, and daughters were born to them, 
Gen 6:2 some of the heavenly beings saw that the daughters of humans were beautiful; and they took them as wives, whoever they chose. 
Gen 6:3 But the  <c>Lord</c> said: ‘My spirit shall not abide in people forever, because they are flesh; therefore they will live for only a hundred and twenty years.’ 
Gen 6:4 The Nephilim were on the earth in those days (and later too) when the heavenly beings lay with the human daughters who had their children. These were the mighty heroes of old, men of renown.  ¶ 
Gen 6:5 When the  <c>Lord</c> saw that people’s wickedness was increasing in the world, and that the trend of their thoughts was at all times toward evil, 
Gen 6:6 he was greatly grieved and regretted that he had made people on the earth. 
Gen 6:7 Therefore the  <c>Lord</c> said, ‘I will destroy all living beings from off the ground — people, animals, creeping things, and birds — because I regret that I have made them.’ 
Gen 6:8 But Noah had won the  <c>Lord</c>’s favour.  ¶ 
Gen 6:9 This is the story of Noah. Among the people of his time, Noah was righteous and wholehearted; Noah walked with God. 
Gen 6:10 Noah had three sons, Shem, Ham, and Japheth. 
Gen 6:11 God saw that the earth was corrupt and full of violence. 
Gen 6:12 God looked at the earth and saw that it was corrupt; all living things on the earth had become corrupt in their ways.  ¶ 
Gen 6:13 So God said to Noah, ‘I have determined to put an end to all living beings, for the earth is filled with their acts of injustice; I am going to destroy them from the earth. 
Gen 6:14 Make yourself an ark of cypress wood. Construct rooms in the ark, and coat it within and without with pitch. 
Gen 6:15 This is how you shall build it: the length of the ark shall be five hundred feet, its breadth eighty feet, and its height fifty feet. 
Gen 6:16 Make a roof for it and place the door on the side. Construct it with lower, second, and third storeys. 
Gen 6:17 For I am about to bring floods of water upon the earth to destroy from under heaven every living thing in which is the breath of life; every thing that is on the earth shall die.  ¶ 
Gen 6:18 ‘But I will make a solemn agreement with you. Go into the ark with your sons, your wife and their wives, 
Gen 6:19 and take with you into the ark two of every kind living thing, a male and a female, 
Gen 6:20 birds, animals and creeping things, so that they might be kept alive. 
Gen 6:21 Take and store food for them and you.’  ¶ 
Gen 6:22 Noah did all this. He did everything that God told him to.  ¶ 
Gen 7:1 Then the  <c>Lord</c> said to Noah, ‘Enter with all your household into the ark; for I see that in this age you are living before me an upright life. 
Gen 7:2 Take seven of all the beasts that are fit for food and sacrifice, the male and the female; but of the beasts that are not fit for food and sacrifice take only two, the male and the female; 
Gen 7:3 and of the wild birds that are fit for food and sacrifice take seven, to keep the species alive on the earth. 
Gen 7:4 After seven days I will send rain on the earth forty days and forty nights; and I will destroy from the surface of the ground every living thing that I have made.’  ¶ 
Gen 7:5 Then Noah did all that the  <c>Lord</c> commanded him. 
Gen 7:6 He was six hundred years old, and when the waters of the flood came upon the earth 
Gen 7:7 he, his sons, his wife, and his sons’ wives, entered the ark because of the waters of the flood 
Gen 7:8 together with the beasts that were fit for food and sacrifice and the beasts that were not fit, and the birds, and everything that creeps upon the ground. 
Gen 7:9 Two by two, male and female, they entered the ark as God had commanded Noah.  ¶ 
Gen 7:10 After seven days, the flood waters came. 
Gen 7:11 In the six hundredth year of Noah’s life, in the second month, on the seventeenth day of the month, on that very day, all the fountains of the great deep burst open, and the windows of heaven were opened — and 
Gen 7:12 it rained for forty days and forty nights. 
Gen 7:13 That was the day that Noah, and Shem, and Ham, and Japheth, the sons of Noah, and Noah’s wife, and the three wives of his sons with them, went into the ark, and 
Gen 7:14 every type of animal, and cattle, and creeping thing that creeps on the earth, and bird 
Gen 7:15 went with Noah into the ark, two by two of every kind of living thing. 
Gen 7:16 They went in, male and female, as God had commanded Noah; and the  <c>Lord</c> shut Noah in the ark.  ¶ 
Gen 7:17 The flood continued for forty days, and the waters increased and raised up the ark, and it was lifted high above the earth. 
Gen 7:18 It floated on the surface as the waters rose higher over the land. 
Gen 7:19 Higher the waters rose over the land — until the highest mountains were covered 
Gen 7:20 by more than twenty feet.  ¶ 
Gen 7:21 All creatures on the land, bird and cattle and animals, every creature that swarms on the ground, every person, 
Gen 7:22 everything on dry land in whose nostrils was the breath of life, died. 
Gen 7:23 The  <c>Lord</c> destroyed everything that existed upon the face of the ground, both man and cattle, and creeping things, and the birds of the heavens, and Noah only was left and they who were with him in the ark.  ¶ 
Gen 7:24 The waters did not start to go down for a hundred and fifty days.  ¶ 
Gen 8:1 Then God remembered Noah and all the beasts and all the animals that were with him in the ark; and God caused a wind to blow over the earth, and the flood subsided, 
Gen 8:2 the fountains of the deed were stopped and the windows of heaven closed, and the rain from heaven ceased, 
Gen 8:3 and the waters withdrew more and more from the land for a hundred and fifty days. 
Gen 8:4 On the seventeenth day of the seventh month, the ark came to rest on the mountains of Ararat. 
Gen 8:5 The waters continued to go down until, on the first day of the tenth month, the tops of the mountains could be seen.  ¶ 
Gen 8:6 After forty days Noah opened the window of the ark, 
Gen 8:7 and sent out a raven; and it kept going to and fro until the waters were dried up from the earth. 
Gen 8:8 He also sent out a dove to see if the waters had subsided from the surface of the ground; 
Gen 8:9 but the dove found no rest for her foot, and so returned to him to the ark, for the waters covered the surface of the whole earth. So he reached out his hand and took her and brought her back into the ark.  ¶ 
Gen 8:10 Then he waited seven days longer and again sent out the dove from the ark. 
Gen 8:11 The dove came in to him at dusk and in her mouth was a freshly plucked olive-leaf. So Noah knew that the waters had subsided from the earth. 
Gen 8:12 He waited seven days more and sent out the dove; but it did not return to him again.  ¶ 
Gen 8:13 So it was that in the first day of the first month of Noah’s six hundred and first year, the waters had dried up. Noah removed the covering of the ark and looked, and saw that the surface of the ground was dry. 
Gen 8:14 It was the twenty-seventh day of the second month.  ¶ 
Gen 8:15 God said to Noah, 
Gen 8:16 ‘Leave the ark with your wife and sons and their wives. 
Gen 8:17 Bring out every living creature, every bird, cattle, and creeping thing that creeps on the earth, so that they can spread over the earth, and be fruitful and multiply.’ 
Gen 8:18 So Noah left the ark with his sons and his wife and his son’s wives, 
Gen 8:19 and every living creature, every creeping thing, every bird came out one kind after another. 
Gen 8:20 Noah built an altar to the  <c>Lord</c> and took one of every beast and bird that was fit for sacrifice and offered burnt-offerings on the altar. 
Gen 8:21 When the  <c>Lord</c> smelled the pleasing odour, he said to himself, ‘I will never again curse the ground because of people because the inclination of their heart is evil from their youth, nor will I again destroy every living thing, as I have done. 
Gen 8:22 While the earth remains, seedtime and harvest, cold and heat, summer and winter, day and night, shall not cease.’  ¶ 
Gen 9:1 Then God blessed Noah and his sons, and said to them, ‘Bear children and multiply and repopulate the earth. 
Gen 9:2 Every wild beast and bird and everything that creeps on the ground and all the fish of the sea shall fear and dread you; into your hand they are given. 
Gen 9:3 Every moving thing that lives shall be food for you; as I gave the green herbs, I give them all to you. 
Gen 9:4 Only you shall not eat flesh while the life is in it, that is, the blood.  ¶ 
Gen 9:5 ‘Moreover, your own life-blood will I require for a person’s life; from every beast will I require it, and from everyone who takes another’s life. 
Gen 9:6 Whoever sheds a person’s blood, by people shall their blood be shed; for God made people in his own image. 
Gen 9:7 But you are to bear children and repopulate the whole earth and subdue it.’  ¶ 
Gen 9:8 God also said to Noah and to his sons with him, 
Gen 9:9 ‘Now I make this solemn agreement with you and with your descendants 
Gen 9:10 and with every living creature that is with you, with the birds, the cattle, and every wild animal that is with you of all that have gone out of the ark, even with every beast of the earth. 
Gen 9:11 This is my solemn agreement: No living thing will ever again be cut off by the waters of the flood, and there will never again be a flood to destroy the earth.’  ¶ 
Gen 9:12 God said, ‘This is the symbol of the solemn agreement that I make for all time between me and you and every living creature that is with you: 
Gen 9:13 I have placed my bow in the cloud and it shall be the symbol of the solemn agreement between me and the inhabitants of the earth. 
Gen 9:14 Whenever I bring a cloud over the earth and the bow is seen in the cloud, 
Gen 9:15 I will remember the agreement which is between me and you and every living creature; and the waters shall never again become a flood to destroy all living things. 
Gen 9:16 Whenever the bow is seen in the cloud, I will see it and remember the everlasting agreement between God and every living creature on earth,’ 
Gen 9:17 God said to Noah, ‘it is the sign of the solemn agreement which I have made with everything that lives on earth.’  ¶ 
Gen 9:18 The sons of Noah, who left the ark, were Shem, and Ham, and Japheth; and Ham was the father of Canaan. 
Gen 9:19 The descendants of these three sons of Noah spread over the whole earth.  ¶ 
Gen 9:20 Now Noah, the farmer, was the first to plant a vineyard. 
Gen 9:21 When he drank the wine he became drunk, and lay uncovered in his tent. 
Gen 9:22 Then Ham, the father of Canaan, saw the nakedness of his father and told his two brothers about it. 
Gen 9:23 But Shem and Japheth took a garment and laid it upon both their shoulders and went backward to cover the nakedness of their father, their faces being turned away so that they did not see their father’s nakedness. 
Gen 9:24 When Noah awoke from his wine and learned what his youngest son had done to him, 
Gen 9:25 he said, <br>	Cursed be Canaan; <br>	may he be a slave of slaves to his brothers.  ¶ 
Gen 9:26 Also he said: <br>	Blessed of the  <c>Lord</c> be Shem; <br>		and let Canaan be a slave to him. <br>	
Gen 9:27 God enlarge Japheth <br>		and let him live in the tents of Shem. <br>	Let Canaan be a slave to him as well.  ¶ 
Gen 9:28 Noah lived after the flood three hundred and fifty years. 
Gen 9:29 All the days of Noah were nine hundred and fifty years; and he died. 
Gen 10:1 Now these are the descendants of the sons of Noah: Shem, Ham, and Japheth; and to them were sons born after the flood. 
Gen 10:2 The sons of Japheth: Gomer, and Magog, and Madai, and Javan, and Tubal, and Meshech, and Tiras. 
Gen 10:3 The sons of Gomer: Ashkenaz, and Riphath, and Togarmah. 
Gen 10:4 The sons of Javan: Elishah, and Tarshish, Kittim, and Dodanim. 
Gen 10:5 From the descendants of these were the peoples of the coasts and islands divided in their lands, every one after his tongue, after their families, in their nations. 
Gen 10:6 The sons of Ham: Cush, and Mizraim, and Put, and Canaan. 
Gen 10:7 The sons of Cush: Seba, and Havilah, and Sabtah, and Raamah, and Sabteca; and the sons of Raamah: Sheba, and Dedan. 
Gen 10:8 Cush fathered Nimrod; he began to be known as a mighty one in the earth. 
Gen 10:9 He was a mighty hunter before the  <c>Lord</c>; which is why people say: ‘Like Nimrod a mighty hunter before the  <c>Lord</c>.’ 
Gen 10:10 The beginning of his kingdom was Babel, and Erech, and Accad, and Calneh, in the land of Shinar. 
Gen 10:11 Out of that land went forth Asshur, and builded Nineveh, and Rehoboth-ir, and Calah, 
Gen 10:12 and Resen between Nineveh and Calah — which is the great city. 
Gen 10:13 Mizraim fathered Ludim, and Anamim, and Lehabim, and Naphtuhim, 
Gen 10:14 and Pathrusim, and Casluhim — from whom went forth the Philistines — and Caphtorim. 
Gen 10:15 Canaan fathered Zidon his firstborn, and Heth; 
Gen 10:16 and the Jebusite, and the Amorite, and the Girgashite; 
Gen 10:17 and the Hivite, and the Arkite, and the Sinite; 
Gen 10:18 and the Arvadite, and the Zemarite, and the Hamathite; and afterward were the families of the Canaanite spread abroad. 
Gen 10:19 The border of the Canaanite was from Zidon, as you go toward Gerar, to Gaza; as you go toward Sodom and Gomorrah and Admah and Zeboiim, to Lasha. 
Gen 10:20 These are the sons of Ham, after their families, after their tongues, in their lands, in their nations. 
Gen 10:21 To Shem, the father of all the children of Eber, the elder brother of Japheth, to him also were children born. 
Gen 10:22 The sons of Shem: Elam, and Asshur, and Arpachshad, and Lud, and Aram. 
Gen 10:23 The sons of Aram: Uz, and Hul, and Gether, and Mash. 
Gen 10:24 Arpachshad fathered Shelah; and Shelah fathered Eber. 
Gen 10:25 To Eber were born two sons; the name of the one was Peleg; for in his days was the earth divided; and his brother’s name was Joktan. 
Gen 10:26 Joktan fathered Almodad, and Sheleph, and Hazarmaveth, and Jerah; 
Gen 10:27 and Hadoram, and Uzal, and Diklah; 
Gen 10:28 and Obal, and Abimael, and Sheba; 
Gen 10:29 and Ophir, and Havilah, and Jobab; all these were the sons of Joktan. 
Gen 10:30 Their settlements were from Mesha, as you go toward Sephar, to the mountain of the east. 
Gen 10:31 These are the sons of Shem, after their families, after their tongues, in their lands, after their nations. 
Gen 10:32 These are the families of the sons of Noah, after their generations, in their nations; and of these were the nations divided in the earth after the flood.  ¶ 
Gen 11:1 All the inhabitants of the earth had one language and vocabulary; 
Gen 11:2 and as they travelled westward, they found a broad valley in the land of Shinar, and made their home there.  ¶ 
Gen 11:3 Then they said one to another, ‘Come, let us make bricks and thoroughly bake them.’ So they had bricks for stone and asphalt for mortar. 
Gen 11:4 They said, ‘Come, let us build ourselves a city, and a tower whose top will touch the heavens. We will make a landmark, so that we are not scattered over all the earth.’  ¶ 
Gen 11:5 But when the  <c>Lord</c> came down to see the city and tower that people had built, 
Gen 11:6 he said, ‘See, they are one people and all have one language. This is only the beginning of their activity, and now nothing that they propose to do will seem too difficult for them. 
Gen 11:7 Come, let us go down there and confuse their language, so that they do not understand each other’s speech.’  ¶ 
Gen 11:8 So the  <c>Lord</c> scattered them from there over all the earth; and they ceased building the city. 
Gen 11:9 That is why they named it Babel <sup>[ Confusion ]</sup>, for there the  <c>Lord</c> confused the language of all the inhabitants of earth and scattered them over the whole world.  ¶ 
Gen 11:10 These are the descendants of Shem. Shem was a hundred years old, and fathered Arpachshad two years after the flood. 
Gen 11:11 Shem lived for five hundred years after he fathered Arpachshad, and fathered sons and daughters.  ¶ 
Gen 11:12 Arpachshad lived for five and thirty years, and fathered Shelah. 
Gen 11:13 Arpachshad lived for four hundred and three years after he fathered Shelah, and fathered sons and daughters.  ¶ 
Gen 11:14 Shelah lived for thirty years, and fathered Eber. 
Gen 11:15 Shelah lived for four hundred and three years after he fathered Eber, and fathered sons and daughters.  ¶ 
Gen 11:16 Eber lived for four and thirty years, and fathered Peleg. 
Gen 11:17 Eber lived for four hundred and thirty years after he fathered Peleg, and fathered sons and daughters.  ¶ 
Gen 11:18 Peleg lived for thirty years, and fathered Reu. 
Gen 11:19 Peleg lived for two hundred and nine years after he fathered Reu, and fathered sons and daughters.  ¶ 
Gen 11:20 Reu lived for two and thirty years, and fathered Serug. 
Gen 11:21 Reu lived for two hundred and seven years after he fathered Serug, and fathered sons and daughters. 
Gen 11:22 Serug lived for thirty years, and fathered Nahor.  ¶ 
Gen 11:23 Serug lived for two hundred years after he fathered Nahor, and fathered sons and daughters.  ¶ 
Gen 11:24 Nahor lived for nine and twenty years, and fathered Terah. 
Gen 11:25 Nahor lived for a hundred and nineteen years after he fathered Terah, and fathered sons and daughters.  ¶ 
Gen 11:26 Terah lived for seventy years, and fathered Abram, Nahor, and Haran.  ¶ 
Gen 11:27 Now these are the descendants of Terah. Terah fathered Abram, Nahor, and Haran; and Haran fathered Lot. 
Gen 11:28 Haran died in the presence of his father Terah in the land of his birth, in Ur of the Chaldees. 
Gen 11:29 Abram and Nahor took wives: the name of Abram’s wife was Sarai; and the name of Nahor’s wife, Milcah, the daughter of Haran, the father of Milcah, and the father of Iscah. 
Gen 11:30 Sarai was barren; she had no child. 
Gen 11:31 Terah took Abram his son, and Lot the son of Haran, his son’s son, and Sarai his daughter-in-law, his son Abram’s wife; and they went from Ur of the Chaldees, to go to the land of Canaan; and they nt to Haran, and dwelt there. 
Gen 11:32 In total, Terah lived for two hundred and five years; and died in Haran.  ¶ 
Gen 12:1 The  <c>Lord</c> said to Abram, ‘Go from your country, your relatives and your father’s house to the land that I will show you. 
Gen 12:2 I will make of you a great nation; and I will surely bless you and make your name famous, so that you will be a blessing. 
Gen 12:3 I will bless those who bless you, and I will curse those who curse you, and all the families of the earth shall ask for themselves a blessing like your own.’  ¶ 
Gen 12:4 So Abram set out, as the  <c>Lord</c> had commanded him; and Lot went with him. Abram was seventy-five years old when he left Haran. 
Gen 12:5 He took Sarai his wife and Lot his brother’s son and all the slaves that they had acquired in Haran, and started for the land of Canaan.  ¶ 
Gen 12:6 Abram passed through the land to a place called Shechem, to the oak of Moreh. At that time the Canaanites lived there. 
Gen 12:7 The  <c>Lord</c> appeared to Abram and said, ‘To your descendants I will give this land.’ There Abram built an altar to the  <c>Lord</c> who had appeared to him. 
Gen 12:8 From there he moved on to the hill at the east of Bethel and pitched his tent with Bethel on the west and Ai on the east, and there too he built an altar to the  <c>Lord</c> and prayed to him.  ¶ 
Gen 12:9 Abram moved on, going from place to place toward the Nagreb. 
Gen 12:10 There was a famine in the land, so Abram went down to Egypt to live there; because the famine was severe in the land. 
Gen 12:11 As he was about to enter Egypt, he said to Sarai his wife, ‘You are a beautiful woman; 
Gen 12:12 so that when the Egyptians see you, they will say, “She is his wife”; and they will kill me, but let you live. 
Gen 12:13 Say you are my sister, so that everything may go well for me because of you and my life will be spared.’ 
Gen 12:14 W hen Abram arrived in Egypt, the Egyptians saw that Serai was very beautiful. 
Gen 12:15 The officials of Pharaoh, when they saw her, praised her to Pharaoh, and she was taken into Pharaoh’s household. 
Gen 12:16 He treated Abram well for her sake. He had sheep, and oxen and donkeys, and male and female slaves, and she-donkeys, and camels. 
Gen 12:17 But the  <c>Lord</c> sent great plagues to Pharaoh and his household because of Sarai, Abram’s wife. 
Gen 12:18 Pharaoh called Abram and said, ‘What is this that you have done to me? Why did you not tell me that she was your wife? 
Gen 12:19 Why did you say, “She is my sister,” so that I took her to be my wife? Here she is, take her and go.’ 
Gen 12:20 Pharaoh gave his men orders to send him on his way with his wife and all his possessions.  ¶ 
Gen 13:1 So Abram and his wife and all his possessions left Egypt and went to the Negreb and Lot went with him. 
Gen 13:2 Abram was now very rich in cattle, in silver, and in gold. 
Gen 13:3 He journeyed on from the Negreb in stages towards Bethel, to the place where he had earlier pitched his tent between Bethel and Ai 
Gen 13:4 and had set up the alter to worship the  <c>Lord</c>.  ¶ 
Gen 13:5 Lot, who went with Abram, also had so many flocks and herds and tents 
Gen 13:6 that the land was not fertile enough to support them both. They had too many animals to live in the same place. 
Gen 13:7 At that time, the Canaanites and Perizzites were living in the land. So when there was a quarrel between Lot’s herdsmen and Abram’s herdsmen, 
Gen 13:8 Abram said to Lot, ‘There should be no quarrels between me and you, or between my herdsmen and yours, because we are relatives. 
Gen 13:9 Is not the whole land before you? Let’s separate. If you go to the left, then I will go to the right; or if you go to the right, then I will go to the left.’  ¶ 
Gen 13:10 Then Lot looked about and saw that all the plain of the Jordan, as far as Zoar, was well watered everywhere, like a garden of the  <c>Lord</c>. (This was before the Lord destroyed Sodom and Gomorrah.) 
Gen 13:11 So Lot chose for himself all the valley of the Jordan and went on to the east; and they separated from one another. 
Gen 13:12 Abram lived in the land of Canaan and Lot lived in the cities of the plain and moved his tent as far as Sodom. 
Gen 13:13 (But the men of Sodom were very wicked and sinned against the  <c>Lord</c>.)  ¶ 
Gen 13:14 The  <c>Lord</c> said to Abram, after Lot had gone away from him, ‘Lift up your eyes and look from the place where you are northward, southward, eastward and westward, 
Gen 13:15 for all the land that you see I will give to you and to your descendants forever. 
Gen 13:16 I will make your descendants as many as the dust of the earth, so that if someone could count the dust of the earth, then your descendants could also be counted. 
Gen 13:17 Rise, walk through the length and breadth of the land, for I will give it to you.’  ¶ 
Gen 13:18 Then Abraham moved his tent and lived in the oak grove of Mamre, which is in Hebron, and built there an altar to the  <c>Lord</c>.  ¶ 
Gen 14:1 I n the days of Amraphel king of Shinar, Arioch king of Ellasar, Chedorlaomer king of Elam, and Tidal king of Goiim, 
Gen 14:2 they went to war with Bera king of Sodom, and with Birsha king of Gomorrah, Shinab king of Admah, and Shemeber king of Zeboiim, and the king of Bela (that is, Zoar). 
Gen 14:3 All these joined forces together in the valley of Siddim (that is, the Dead Sea).  ¶ 
Gen 14:4 For twelve years they had been subject to Chedorlaonier, but in the thirteenth year they had rebelled. 
Gen 14:5 So in the fourteenth year Chedorlaonier, and the kings that were with him, came and defeated the Rephaim in Ashteroth-Karnaim, the Zuzim in Ham, the Emim in Shaveh-Kiriathaim, 
Gen 14:6 and the Horites in their hill country of Seir, to El-Paran, which is on the edge of the wilderness. 
Gen 14:7 Then they returned and came to En-Mishpat (that is, Kadesh), and laid waste all the country of the Amalekites, and also the Amorites, who lived in Hazazon-Tamar.  ¶ 
Gen 14:8 So the king of Sodom went out together with the king of Gomorrah, the king of Admah, the king of Zeboiim, and the king of Bela (that is, Zoar); and they set themselves in battle array against them in the valley of Siddim; 
Gen 14:9 against Chedorlaomer king of Elam, Tidal king of Goiim, Amraphel king of Shinar, and Arioch king of Ellasar; four kings against the five. 
Gen 14:10 Now the valley of Siddim is full of bitumen pits; so when the kings of Sodom and Gomorrah fled, they fell into them, but those who remained fled to the mountain. 
Gen 14:11 Then they took all the goods of Sodom and Gomorrah, and all their provisions and went their way. 
Gen 14:12 They also took Lot, Abram’s brother’s son, who was living in Sodom, and his goods and departed.  ¶ 
Gen 14:13 But one who had escaped came and told Abram the Hebrew. Now he was living by the oaks of Mamre the Amorite, brother of Eshcol, and brother of Aner, and these were supporters of Abram. 
Gen 14:14 When Abram heard that his kinsman had been taken captive, he led forth his trained men, born in his house, three hundred and eighteen, and pursued as far as Dan. 
Gen 14:15 Then, dividing his band in order to attack the kings by night, he with his servants attacked them, and pursued them to Hobah, which is north of Damascus. 
Gen 14:16 So he brought back all the goods, and also his kinsman Lot, with his goods, as well as the women and the people.  ¶ 
Gen 14:17 Then the king of Sodom went out to meet him, after his return from the defeat of Chedorlaomer and the kings who were with him, at the valley of Shaveh (that is, the King’s Vale). 
Gen 14:18 Melchizedek king of Salem also brought out bread and wine; and he was priest of God Most High. 
Gen 14:19 He blessed him saying: <br>	Blessed be Abram before God Most High, <br>		possessor of heaven and earth. <br>	
Gen 14:20 Blessed be God Most High, <br>		who has delivered your foes into your power. <br> ¶ Then Abram gave him a tenth of everything.  ¶ 
Gen 14:21 The king of Sodom said to Abram, ‘Give me my people, and take the goods for yourself.’ 
Gen 14:22 But Abram said to the king of Sodom, ‘I have lifted up my hand to the  <c>Lord</c>, God Most High, Possessor of heaven and earth, 
Gen 14:23 that I would not take a thread nor a sandal-thong nor anything that is yours, so that you could not say, “I have made Abram rich.” 
Gen 14:24 By no means! Only that which the servants have eaten, and the portion of the men who went with me, Aner, Eshcol, and Mamre — let them take their portion.’  ¶ 
Gen 15:1 After these things God spoke to Abram in a vision saying, ‘Do not be afraid, Abram, I am your shield. Your reward will be exceedingly great.’ 
Gen 15:2 But Abram said, ‘Lord  <c>God</c>, what can you give me? I am childless, and the person who will be possessor of my house is Eliezer of Damascus, 
Gen 15:3 to me you have given no offspring, and, so a slave born in my house is my heir.’ 
Gen 15:4 The word of the  <c>Lord</c> came to him, ‘This man will not be your heir, but a child of your own will be your heir.’  ¶ 
Gen 15:5 Then God brought him outside and said, ‘Look now toward heaven and count the stars, if you are able to count them! So will your descendants be.’ 
Gen 15:6 Abram believed in the  <c>Lord</c>; and the  <c>Lord</c> reckoned it to him as righteousness, 
Gen 15:7 and said to him, ‘I am the  <c>Lord</c> who brought you out of Ur of the Chaldees, to give to you this land to inherit it.’  ¶ 
Gen 15:8 Abram said, ‘Lord  <c>God</c>, how will I know that I will inherit it?’  ¶ 
Gen 15:9 The  <c>Lord</c> said to him, ‘Bring me a heifer of three years old, and a she-goat of three years old, and a ram of three years old, and a turtle dove, and a young pigeon.’ 
Gen 15:10 Abram brought him all these, and divided them in the middle, and laid each half over against the other; but the birds he did not divide. 
Gen 15:11 The birds of prey came down upon the carcasses, but Abram drove them away.  ¶ 
Gen 15:12 When the sun was going down, a deep sleep fell upon Abram, and a horror of great darkness fell on him. 
Gen 15:13 The  <c>Lord</c> said to Abram, ‘Know certainly that your descendants will be foreigners in a land that is not theirs, and will be slaves there; and they will be held there for four hundred years. 
Gen 15:14 But I will judge that nation, whom they will serve, and afterward they will come out with many goods. 
Gen 15:15 But you will go to your fathers in peace; you will be buried in a good old age. 
Gen 15:16 In the fourth generation they return here again; for the iniquity of the Amorite is not yet full.’  ¶ 
Gen 15:17 When the sun had set and it was dark, there appeared a smoking furnace, and a flaming torch that passed between the pieces of the animals.  ¶ 
Gen 15:18 At that time the  <c>Lord</c> made a solemn agreement with Abram, saying, ‘To your descendants I give this land, from the river of Egypt unto the great river, the river Euphrates.’ 
Gen 15:19 (This includes the lands of the Kenite, the Kenizzite, the Kadmonite, 
Gen 15:20 the Hittite, the Perizzite, the Rephaim, 
Gen 15:21 the Amorite, the Canaanite, the Girgashite, and Jebusite).  ¶ 
Gen 16:1 Now Sarai, Abram’s wife, had borne him no children, but she had an Egyptian slave-girl whose name was Hagar. 
Gen 16:2 Sarai said to Abram, ‘the  <c>Lord</c> has denied me children; Take my slave-girl; maybe I will obtain children by her.’ Then Abram listened to her 
Gen 16:3 so she took Hagar the Egyptian, her slave-girl, after Abram had lived for ten years in the land of Canaan, and gave her to Abram her husband to be his wife 
Gen 16:4 and Abram lay with Hagar, and she conceived. When she saw that she had conceived, she looked with contempt on her mistress.  ¶ 
Gen 16:5 Sarai complained to Abram, ‘May the wrong I suffer be on you! I myself gave my slave-girl to you; and now that she sees that she has conceived, I am despised by her; may the  <c>Lord</c> judge between me and you.’ 
Gen 16:6 But Abram said to Sarai, ‘Your maid-servant is in your power, do to her whatever seems right to you.’ Then Sarai ill-treated her so that she fled from her presence.  ¶ 
Gen 16:7 The messenger of the  <c>Lord</c> found her by a spring of water in the wilderness, by the spring in the way to Shur. 
Gen 16:8 He said, ‘Hagar, Sarai’s slave-girl, where have you come from? And where are you going?’ She said, ‘I am fleeing from the presence of mistress Sarai.’ 
Gen 16:9 Then the messenger of the  <c>Lord</c> said to her, ‘Return to your mistress and submit yourself to her authority.’ 
Gen 16:10 Moreover the messenger of the  <c>Lord</c> said to her, ‘I will make your descendants so many that they can not be numbered because they are so numerous.’ 
Gen 16:11 The messenger of the  <c>Lord</c> also said to her, ‘You are pregnant, and will have a son; you must call him Ishmael God hears, because the  <c>Lord</c> has heard of your ill-treatment.’ <br>	
Gen 16:12 He shall be like a wild donkey, <br>		his hand against every man, <br>		and every man’s hand against him; <br>	and he will live at odds with all his relatives.  ¶ 
Gen 16:13 Then she called the name of the  <c>Lord</c>, who had spoken to her, El-roi (You are a God who sees me); for she said, ‘Have I seen God and am I still alive after I have looked upon him?’ 
Gen 16:14 Therefore the well is called Beer-lahai-roi <sup>[ Well of the living One who sees me ]</sup>, ( it is between Kadesh and Bered) 
Gen 16:15 Hagar bore Abram a son, and Abram named his son, whom Hagar bore, Ishmael. 
Gen 16:16 Abram was eighty-six years old, when Hagar bore Ishmael.  ¶ 
Gen 17:1 When Abram was ninety-nine years old, the  <c>Lord</c> revealed himself to Abram and said to him, ‘I am God Almighty, walk before me and be blameless 
Gen 17:2 and I will make my solemn agreement between me and you and will make your descendants exceedingly numerous.’ 
Gen 17:3 Then Abram fell on his face; and God talked with him, saying 
Gen 17:4 ‘I make this solemn promise to you: you will be the father of a multitude of nations. 
Gen 17:5 Neither will your name any longer be Abram, but your name will be Abraham; for I will make you the father of a multitude of nations. 
Gen 17:6 I will make you exceedingly fruitful, and will make nations of you, and kings shall spring from you. 
Gen 17:7 I will establish my solemn agreement between me and you and your descendants after your throughout their generations, an everlasting covenant, to be a God to you and to your descendants after you. 
Gen 17:8 I will give to you, and to your descendants after your, the land where you are now foreigners, all the land of Canaan, for an everlasting possession, and I will be their God.’  ¶ 
Gen 17:9 God also said to Abraham, ‘As for you, you must keep the requirements of my solemn agreement, you, and your descendants after you throughout their generations. 
Gen 17:10 This is my solemn agreement, which you must keep, between me and you and your descendants after you: every male among you must be circumcised. 
Gen 17:11 Whenever you are circumcised, the flesh of your foreskin shall be a sign of a solemn agreement between me and you. 
Gen 17:12 Every male when he is eight days old, must be circumcised throughout your generations, whether he is born in the house, or bought with money from any foreigner who is not of your offspring. 
Gen 17:13 The slave who is born in your house and the one who is bought with your money must be circumcised. The sign of my solemn agreement will be in your flesh — an everlasting agreement. 
Gen 17:14 As for the uncircumcised male, who is not circumcised in the flesh of his foreskin, that one will be cut off from his people; he has broken my solemn agreement.’  ¶ 
Gen 17:15 Then God said to Abraham, ‘As for Sarai your wife, do not call her name Sarai, but Sarah. 
Gen 17:16 I will bless her, and will give you a son from her: I will bless her, and she will become the mother of nations; kings of peoples will descend from her.’  ¶ 
Gen 17:17 Then Abraham fell on his face and laughed, and said to himself. ‘Will a child be born to one who is an hundred years old? Will Sarah who is ninety years old bear children?’ 
Gen 17:18 Abraham said to God, ‘If only Ishmael might live with your blessing!’  ¶ 
Gen 17:19 But God said, ‘No. But Sarah your wife is about to bear your a son; call him Isaac. I will establish my covenant with him for an everlasting covenant for his descendants after him. 
Gen 17:20 However I have heard you regarding Ishmael: I have blessed him, and will make him fruitful and his descendants exceedingly many. Twelve princes he will father, and I will make him a great nation. 
Gen 17:21 But my covenant I will establish with Isaac, whom Sarah shall bear to you at this appointed time next year.’ 
Gen 17:22 When he had finished talking with him, God left Abraham.  ¶ 
Gen 17:23 Then Abraham took Ishmael his son, and all who were born in his house, and all who were bought with his money, every male among the men of Abraham’s house, and circumcised the flesh of their foreskin that very same day, as God had said to him. 
Gen 17:24 Now Abraham was ninety-nine years old, when he was circumcised in the flesh of his foreskin. 
Gen 17:25 Ishmael his son was thirteen years old, when he was circumcised in the flesh of his foreskin. 
Gen 17:26 On this very same day was Abraham circumcised, with Ishmael his son. 
Gen 17:27 All the men of his house, those born in the house and those bought with money from foreigners, were circumcised with him.  ¶ 
Gen 18:1 The  <c>Lord</c> also appeared to Abraham by the oaks of Mamre, as he was sitting at the entrance of his tent in the heat of the day; 
Gen 18:2 and, as he looked up, three men stood there before him. As soon as he saw them, he ran from the entrance of his tent to meet them and bowed to the ground 
Gen 18:3 and said, ‘Sirs, if you are willing to do me a favour, do not, I beg of you, pass by your servant. 
Gen 18:4 Since you have come to your servant, let a little water be brought, so that you may wash your feet, and lie down under the tree. 
Gen 18:5 And let me bring some food, so that you may refresh yourselves; afterward you may go on your way.’ They replied, ‘Do as you have said.’  ¶ 
Gen 18:6 So Abraham hastened to Sarah’s tent and said, ‘Make ready quickly four measures of fine meal, knead it, and make cakes.’ 
Gen 18:7 Abraham also ran to the herd, and took a calf that was tender and good, and gave it to the servant, and he prepared it quickly. 
Gen 18:8 Then Abraham took curd and milk, with the calf that he had prepared, and served them; and he waited on them under the tree, while they ate.  ¶ 
Gen 18:9 Then they said to him, ‘Where is your wife?’ He said, ‘There, within the tent.’ 
Gen 18:10 One of them said, ‘I will surely return to you about nine months from now, and then, Sarah your wife shall have a son.’ But Sarah was listening behind the door of the tent. 
Gen 18:11 Now Sarah and Abraham were advanced in years; 
Gen 18:12 so she laughed to herself, saying, ‘After I and my husband are so old will I have pleasure?’ 
Gen 18:13 But the  <c>Lord</c> said to Abraham, ‘Why did Sarah laugh, saying, “Will I, indeed, even when I am old give birth to a child?” 
Gen 18:14 Is anything too wonderful for the  <c>Lord</c>? At the appointed time about nine months from now, I will return to you and Sarah shall have a son.’ 
Gen 18:15 Sarah was frightened and denied that she had laughed, but he said ‘Yes, you laughed.’  ¶ 
Gen 18:16 Then the men started from there and looked off in the direction of Sodom; and Abraham went along with them to start them on their way. 
Gen 18:17 the  <c>Lord</c> said, ‘Should I conceal from Abraham that which I am about to do, 
Gen 18:18 since Abraham will become a great and mighty nation and all the nations of the earth will want a blessing like his for themselves? 
Gen 18:19 For I have chosen him in order that he may teach his sons and his household after him, and that they may keep the way of the  <c>Lord</c>, by doing righteousness and justice, so that the  <c>Lord</c> may bring on Abraham that which he has promised concerning him.’  ¶ 
Gen 18:20 The  <c>Lord</c> said, ‘The complaint has come that the people of Sodom and Gomorrah have committed great and terrible sins. 
Gen 18:21 I will go down and see whether they have done exactly as the complaint comes to me; and if they have not, I will know.’  ¶ 
Gen 18:22 As the men turned from there and went toward Sodom, Abraham remained standing before the  <c>Lord</c>. 
Gen 18:23 Abraham drew near to the  <c>Lord</c> and said, ‘Will you sweep away the righteous with the wicked? 
Gen 18:24 Suppose there are within the city fifty people who are righteous. Will you sweep it away and not forgive the place for sake of the fifty righteous who are in it? 
Gen 18:25 Far be it from you to do this: to slay the righteous with the wicked! And that the righteous should be treated as the wicked, far be it from you! Should not the Judge of all the earth do what is just?’ 
Gen 18:26 The  <c>Lord</c> said, ‘If I find in the city of Sodom fifty who are righteous, I will spare the whole place for their sake.’ 
Gen 18:27 Abraham answered, ‘I have dared to speak to the  <c>Lord</c>, even though I am but dust and ashes. 
Gen 18:28 Suppose there be five lacking of the fifty righteous. Will you sweep away all the city for lack of five?’ The  <c>Lord</c> said, ‘I will not sweep it away, if I find forty-five there.’  ¶ 
Gen 18:29 Then Abraham spoke to him again, and said, ‘Suppose forty are found there?’ He replied, ‘For the sake of forty I will not do it.’ 
Gen 18:30 Then Abraham said, ‘Oh, let not the  <c>Lord</c> be angry, but let me speak. Suppose thirty are found there?’ He answered, ‘I will not do it, if I find thirty there.’ 
Gen 18:31 Then Abraham said, ‘You see that I have dared to speak to the  <c>Lord</c>. Suppose twenty are found there?’ He replied, ‘For the sake of twenty I will not destroy it.’ 
Gen 18:32 Then Abraham said, ‘Oh, let not the  <c>Lord</c> be angry, but let me speak just once more. Suppose ten are found there?’ And he said, ‘For the sake of the ten I will not destroy it.’ 
Gen 18:33 Then the  <c>Lord</c> went his way, and Abraham returned home.  ¶ 
Gen 19:1 Two messengers came to Sodom in the evening, as Lot was sitting at the gate of Sodom. When Lot saw them, he rose up to meet them, and he bowed with his face to the earth 
Gen 19:2 and said, ‘Sirs, turn aside, I beg of you, into your servant’s house and spend the night and wash your feet; then you can rise up early and go on your way.’ They said, ‘No, we will spend the night in the street.’ 
Gen 19:3 But he urged them so strongly that they went with him and entered his house. He made a feast for them and baked bread made without yeast, and they ate.  ¶ 
Gen 19:4 But before they had lain down, the people of Sodom, both young and old, all the people from every quarter, surrounded the house. 
Gen 19:5 They called out to Lot, ‘Where are the men who came in to you tonight? Bring them out to us so we can rape them.’  ¶ 
Gen 19:6 Then Lot went out to them at the entrance of his house, but he shut the door after him. 
Gen 19:7 He said, ‘I beg of you, my friends, do not do what is wrong. 
Gen 19:8 See, I have two unmarried daughters; let me bring them out to you, and do to them as you desire; only do nothing to these men, for they have come under the shadow of my roof.’ 
Gen 19:9 But they replied, ‘Stand back!’ And they added, ‘This one came in as a foreigner to live here, but now he would set himself up as a judge! We will treat you worse than them.’ They pressed hard against Lot and advanced to break the door. 
Gen 19:10 But the men reached out and drew Lot to them into the house and shut the door. 
Gen 19:11 Then they struck the men who were at the door of the house, both small and great, with blindness, so that they grew tired of searching for the door.  ¶ 
Gen 19:12 Then the men said to Lot, ‘Have you any one else here? Bring your sons-in-law, your sons, and daughters, and whoever you have in the city out of this place, 
Gen 19:13 for we are about to destroy it, because great complaint concerning the people has come to the  <c>Lord</c> and he has sent us to destroy it.’ 
Gen 19:14 So Lot went out and said to his sons-in-law, ‘Up, go out of this place, for the  <c>Lord</c> will destroy the city.’ But his sons-in-law thought he was only jesting.  ¶ 
Gen 19:15 When the dawn appeared, the messengers urged Lot, saying, ‘Get up, take your wife and your two daughters so that you may not be swept away in the punishment of the city.’ 
Gen 19:16 When he hesitated, the men grabbed him by the hand and led him and his wife and his two daughters outside the city, for the  <c>Lord</c> was merciful to him.  ¶ 
Gen 19:17 When they had brought them outside, they said, ‘Run for your life; do not look behind you nor stay anywhere in the plain. Escape to the heights, that you may not be swept away!’ 
Gen 19:18 But Lot said to them, ‘Oh, sirs, not so! 
Gen 19:19 See, your servant has found favour with you, and you have shown great mercy to me in saving my life. I cannot escape to the heights, lest some evil overtake me, and I die. 
Gen 19:20 See now, this village is near enough to run to, and it is small. Oh, let me escape there, and my life will be saved.’ 
Gen 19:21 He answered, ‘I have also granted you this favour, in that I will not destroy the village of which you have spoken. 
Gen 19:22 Make haste, escape to it, for I can do nothing until you arrive there.’ Therefore the village was called Zoar <sup>[ Little ]</sup>.  ¶ 
Gen 19:23 The sun had risen when Lot came to Zoar. 
Gen 19:24 Then the  <c>Lord</c> caused brimstone and fire from heaven to rain upon Sodom and Gomorrah, 
Gen 19:25 and he destroyed those cities and all the plain, with all the people who lived in it and all that grew on the ground. 
Gen 19:26 But Lot’s wife, who was following him, looked back, and she became a pillar of salt.  ¶ 
Gen 19:27 Early in the morning Abraham rose and went to the place where he had stood before the  <c>Lord</c>; 
Gen 19:28 and as he looked toward Sodom and Gomorrah and all the plain, he saw the smoke of the land going up as the smoke of a smelting-furnace. 
Gen 19:29 God had remembered Abraham when he destroyed the cities of the plain and rescued Lot from the destruction.  ¶ 
Gen 19:30 Then Lot went up from Zoar with his two daughters and lived in a cave on the heights, for he was afraid to stay in Zoar. 
Gen 19:31 The older daughter said to the younger, ‘Our father is old, and there is no one on the earth to come in to us after the manner of all the world. 
Gen 19:32 Come let us make our father drink wine and we will lie with him, so that we can preserve our family through our father.’ 
Gen 19:33 So they made their father drink wine that night; and the older daughter went in and lay with her father. He, however, did not know when she lay down, nor when she arose. 
Gen 19:34 Then in the morning the older daughter said to the younger, ‘Last night I lay with my father. Let us make him drink wine again tonight; and you go in and lie with him, so that we can preserve our family through our father.’ 
Gen 19:35 So they made their father drink wine that night as well. The younger arose and lay with him. He, however, did not know when she lay down nor when she arose. 
Gen 19:36 In this way both the daughters of Lot became pregnant by their father. 
Gen 19:37 Then Lot went up from Zoar with his two daughters and lived in a cave on the heights, for he was afraid to stay in Zoar. His oldest daughter bore a son, and named him Moab. He is the father of the present Moabites. 
Gen 19:38 The younger also bore a son and named him Ben-ammi. That one is the father of the present Ammonites.  ¶ 
Gen 20:1 Abraham journeyed from there toward the land of the Negreb, settling between Kadesh and Shur, and staying for a while in Gerar, 
Gen 20:2 where he said that his wife Sarah was his sister. So King Abimelech of Gerar had Sarah brought to him. 
Gen 20:3 But God came to Abimelech in a dream in the night and said to him, ‘You will die, because of the woman you have taken, for she is married. 
Gen 20:4 But Abimelech had not come near her; so he said, Lord, will you slay an innocent people? 
Gen 20:5 Did Abraham not himself say to me, “She is my sister?” And even she herself said, “He is my brother.” I acted innocently and in good faith.’ 
Gen 20:6 Then God said to him in the dream, ‘I know that you acted innocently and in good faith, and I also prevented you from sinning against me, since I did not allow you to touch her. 
Gen 20:7 Now you must restore the man’s wife — for he is a prophet and he can intercede for you, and you will live. But if you do not restore her at once, you will die, together with all your people.’ 
Gen 20:8 Abimelech rose early in the morning, and summoned all his court, and when he had told all these things in their hearing, they were greatly afraid.  ¶ 
Gen 20:9 Then Abimelech called Abraham and asked him, ‘What have you done to us? What harm have I done to you to make you bring this great sin on me and my kingdom? You have done to me something that ought not to be done.’ 
Gen 20:10 Abimelech said to Abraham, ‘What was your purpose in doing this thing?’ 
Gen 20:11 Abraham answered, ‘Because I thought, “Surely the fear of God is not in this place and they will slay me for my wife’s sake.” 
Gen 20:12 Moreover, she really is my sister, the daughter of my father, though not the daughter of my mother; and she became my wife. 
Gen 20:13 So when God caused me to wander from my father’s house, I said to her, “This is how you can show your loyalty to me: at every place to which we come, say that you are my brother.”’  ¶ 
Gen 20:14 Abimelech then took sheep and oxen, and male and female slaves and gave them to Abraham, and restored Sarah his wife to him. 
Gen 20:15 Also Abimelech said, ‘My land lies before you; live wherever you please.’ 
Gen 20:16 To Sarah he said, ‘I have given your brother a thousand pieces of silveras compensation for all that has befallen you; and in every respect you are vindicated.’ 
Gen 20:17 Then Abraham prayed to God and God healed Abimelech, and his wife, and his slave-girls, so that they could have children ( 
Gen 20:18 for the  <c>Lord</c> had made every woman in Abimelech’s household barren, because of Sarah, Abraham’s wife).  ¶ 
Gen 21:1 The  <c>Lord</c> remembered what he had told Sarah, and he did as he had promised. 
Gen 21:2 So Sarah had Abraham’s son in his old age at the fixed time of which God had told him. 
Gen 21:3 Abraham named him Isaac <sup>[ Laughter ]</sup>
Gen 21:4 and when he was eight days old he circumcised him as God had told him to. 
Gen 21:5 Abraham was a hundred years old when his son Isaac was born. 
Gen 21:6 Sarah said, ‘God has made laughter for me; everyone who hears will laugh with me.’ 
Gen 21:7 She added, ‘Who would have said to Abraham that Sarah would nurse children? Yet I have born him a son in his old age.’  ¶ 
Gen 21:8 When the child grew up, Abraham made a great feast on the day that he was weaned. 
Gen 21:9 But Sarah saw the son whom Hagar the Egyptian had borne to Abraham, playing with her son Isaac. 
Gen 21:10 S he said to Abraham, ‘Drive out this slave-girl and her son, for the son of this slave-girl shall not be heir with my son Isaac’ 
Gen 21:11 This request was very displeasing to Abraham because the boy was his son. 
Gen 21:12 But the  <c>Lord</c> said to Abraham, ‘Do not be displeased because of the boy and because of your slave-girl. Listen to all that Sarah says to you, for only through the line of Isaac will your name be perpetuated. 
Gen 21:13 But I will also make of the son of the slave-girl a great nation, because he is your son.’  ¶ 
Gen 21:14 Then Abraham got up early in the morning and took bread and a skin of water and gave it to Hagar, and he put the boy upon her shoulder and sent her away. So she departed and wandered in the wilderness of Beersheba. 
Gen 21:15 When the water in the skin was gone, she left the child under one of the desert shrubs 
Gen 21:16 and went a short distance away and sat down and said, ‘Let me not see the death of the child.’ So she sat there and wept.  ¶ 
Gen 21:17 Then the  <c>Lord</c> heard the cry of the boy, and the messenger of the  <c>Lord</c> called to Hagar from heaven and said, ‘What troubles you, Hagar? Don’t be afraid, for the  <c>Lord</c> has heard the boy’s cry. 
Gen 21:18 Rise, lift him up, and hold him fast by the hand, for I will make him a great nation.’ 
Gen 21:19 The  <c>Lord</c> opened her eyes and she saw a well of water. Then she went and filled the skin with water and gave the boy a drink.  ¶ 
Gen 21:20 The  <c>Lord</c> was with the boy, and he grew up, 
Gen 21:21 and lived in the wilderness of Paran, and became a bowman. His mother secured a wife for him from Egypt.  ¶ 
Gen 21:22 It happened at that time that Abimelech and Phicol the captain of his army spoke to Abraham, saying, ‘God is with you in all you do. 
Gen 21:23 Now therefore take an oath to me here by God that you will not be false to me, nor to my son nor to my descendants; but that you will treat me and the land you have stayed in according to the kindness which I have shown you.’ 
Gen 21:24 Abraham said, ‘I swear it.’  ¶ 
Gen 21:25 Now as often as Abraham complained to Abimelech because of the well of water which Abimelech’s servants had seized, 
Gen 21:26 Abimelech said, ‘I do not know who has done this thing, neither have you told me nor have I heard of it until today.’ 
Gen 21:27 So Abraham took sheep and oxen and gave them to Abimelech, and made an agreement with each other. 
Gen 21:28 But when Abraham set seven ewe lambs of the flock by themselves, 
Gen 21:29 Abimelech said to Abraham, ‘What is the meaning of these seven ewe lambs which you have set by themselves?’ 
Gen 21:30 Abraham answered, ‘Accept these seven ewe lambs from my hand so that you may be my witness that I dug this well.’ 
Gen 21:31 The place was called Beer-sheba, because it was there they swore their oath. 
Gen 21:32 So they made a solemn agreement at Beer-sheba, and Abimelech arose with Phicol the captain of his army, and they returned to the land of the Philistines. 
Gen 21:33 Abraham, however, planted a tamarisk tree in Beer-sheba, and called there on the name of the  <c>Lord</c>, the Everlasting God. 
Gen 21:34 Abraham stayed in the land of the Philistines many days.  ¶ 
Gen 22:1 Later the  <c>Lord</c> tested Abraham, saying to him, ‘Abraham’; and he answered, ‘Here I am.’ 
Gen 22:2 The  <c>Lord</c> said, ‘Take your son, your only son Isaac, whom you love, and go to the land of Moriah, and offer him there as a burnt-offering on one of the mountains which I will show you.’  ¶ 
Gen 22:3 So Abraham rose early in the morning and saddled his donkey and took two of his servants with him, and his son Isaac. When he had split the wood for the burnt-offering, he set out for the place of which God had told him. 
Gen 22:4 On the third day, when Abraham looked up and saw the place in the distance, 
Gen 22:5 he said to his servants, ‘Stay here with the donkey, while I and the boy go over there. When we have worshipped, we will come back to you.’  ¶ 
Gen 22:6 Then Abraham took the wood for the burnt-offering and laid it on Isaac, his son. He took the fire and the knife, and they both went on together. 
Gen 22:7 Isaac spoke to Abraham his father and said, ‘My father!’ and Abraham answered, ‘Yes, my son.’ Isaac said, ‘Here is the fire and the wood, but where is the lamb for a burnt-offering?’ 
Gen 22:8 Abraham answered, ‘My son, God will himself provide a lamb for a burnt-offering.’ So the two went on together.  ¶ 
Gen 22:9 When they came to the place of which God had told him, Abraham built the altar there and laid the wood on it and bound Isaac his son and laid him on the altar upon the wood. 
Gen 22:10 Then Abraham reached out his hand, and took the knife to kill his son. 
Gen 22:11 But the messenger of the  <c>Lord</c> called to him from heaven, saying, ‘Abraham, Abraham!’ and he answered, ‘Here am I.’ 
Gen 22:12 He said, ‘Do not put your hand upon the boy, nor do anything to him, for now I know that you love God, for you have not refused to give your son, your only son, to me.’  ¶ 
Gen 22:13 Then Abraham looked up, and he saw a ram caught in the thicket by his horns. 
Gen 22:14 So Abraham took the ram and offered him up as a burnt-offering instead of his son. 
Gen 22:15 He named the place ‘The  <c>Lord</c> will provide’ — and even today people say, ‘The  <c>Lord</c> will provide on his mountain.’  ¶ 
Gen 22:16 The messenger of the  <c>Lord</c> again called to Abraham and said, ‘The  <c>Lord</c> declares, “Because you have done this thing and have not kept back your son, your only son, 
Gen 22:17 I will surely bless you. I will make your children as many as the stars of the heavens and as the sand which is on the seashore, so that they will conquer their enemies. 
Gen 22:18 All the nations of the earth will ask for themselves a blessing like theirs, because you have obeyed my command.”’  ¶ 
Gen 22:19 So Abraham returned to his servants, and they arose and went together to Beer-sheba.  ¶ Abraham was living in Beer-sheba. 
Gen 22:20 After these things, Abraham was told, ‘Milcah has also borne children to your brother Nahor, 
Gen 22:21 Uz his first born, Buz his brother, Kemuel the father of Aram, 
Gen 22:22 Chesed, Hazo and Pildash, Jidlaph and Bethuel.’ 
Gen 22:23 (And Bethuel fathered Rebekah). These eight Mileah bore to Nahor, Abraham’s brother. 
Gen 22:24 And his concubine whose name was Reumah, also bore Tebah, Gaham, Tahash, and Maaeah.  ¶ 
Gen 23:1 Sarah lived to be a hundred and twenty-seven years old. 
Gen 23:2 When she died in Kiriath-arba (that is Hebron), in the land of Canaan, Abraham went to mourn for Sarah, and to weep for her.  ¶ 
Gen 23:3 When Abraham rose up from the presence of his dead, he said to the Hittites, 
Gen 23:4 ‘I am a stranger and a foreigner living among you; give me possession of a burying-place with you, so that I may bury my dead out of my sight.’ 
Gen 23:5 The Hittites answered Abraham, 
Gen 23:6 ‘Hear us, my lord; you are a mighty prince among us; bury your dead in the best of our burial places. None of us will withhold from you his burial place, so that you may bury your dead.’  ¶ 
Gen 23:7 Abraham rose up and bowed before the people of the land, the Hittites, 
Gen 23:8 and said to them, ‘If it is your intention that I should bury my dead out of my sight, hear me, and speak for me to Ephron the son of Zohar, 
Gen 23:9 to give me the cave of Machpelah, which he has, which is at the end of his field. Let him give to me for the full price in your presence, so that I can own it as a burying-place.’ 
Gen 23:10 Now Ephron was sitting with the other Hittites, and, in the presence of all the Hittites, all who went in and out at the gate of his city he answered Abraham, 
Gen 23:11 ‘No, my lord, hear me. I give the field to you and the cave that is in it I give to you; in the presence of the children of my people I give it to you; bury your dead.’  ¶ 
Gen 23:12 Then Abraham bowed before the people of the land, 
Gen 23:13 and spoke to Ephron in the hearing of the people of the land, saying, ‘Please, hear me — I will give the price of the field; accept it from me so that I may bury my dead there.’  ¶ 
Gen 23:14 Ephron answered Abraham by saying to him, 
Gen 23:15 ‘My lord, listen to me; a piece of land worth four hundred shekels of silver, what is that between me and you? Bury your dead.’ 
Gen 23:16 Then Abraham accepted Ephron’s terms and Abraham weighed to Ephron the silver, which he had named in the hearing of the Hittites, four hundred shekels of silver, on the standard weights used by merchants.  ¶ 
Gen 23:17 So the field of Ephron which was in Machpelah which was to the east of Mamre, the field, and the cave which was in it, with all the trees that were in the field, that were in all the border of it round about, 
Gen 23:18 were transferred to Abraham’s possession in the presence of the Hittites, before all that went in at the gate of his city.  ¶ 
Gen 23:19 After this Abraham buried Sarah his wife in the cave of the field of Machpelah to the east of Mamre (that is Hebron), in the land of Canaan. 
Gen 23:20 In this way the field and the cave that is in it were transferred by the Hittites to Abraham that he might possess a burying-place.  ¶ 
Gen 24:1 When Abraham was very old and the  <c>Lord</c> had blessed him in every way, 
Gen 24:2 Abraham said to the eldest of his household servants, who had charge of all his affairs, ‘Put your hand under my thigh, 
Gen 24:3 while I make you promise by the  <c>Lord</c>, the God of heaven and earth, that you will not let my son marry one of the daughters of the Canaanites, among whom I live, 
Gen 24:4 but that you will go to my own country and to my relatives and there get a wife for my son Isaac.’ 
Gen 24:5 The servant said to him, ‘Perhaps the woman will not be willing to follow me to this land. Must I then take your son back to the land from which you came?’ 
Gen 24:6 Abraham said to him, ‘See to it that you do not take my son back there. 
Gen 24:7 The  <c>Lord</c>, the God of heaven, who took me from my father’s house and from my native land and who solemnly promised me, “To your children I will give this land,” will send his messenger before you and there you will get a wife for my son. 
Gen 24:8 But if the woman is not willing to come with you, then you will be free from this promise to me; only never take my son back there.’ 
Gen 24:9 So the servant put his hand under Abraham’s thigh and made the promise.  ¶ 
Gen 24:10 Then the servant took ten of his master’s camels and set out with precious gifts from his master. So he went to the town of Aram-naharaim, where Nahor lived. 
Gen 24:11 He made the camels kneel down outside the town by the well in the evening, at the time when women go out to draw water. 
Gen 24:12 Then he said, ‘ <c>Lord</c>, God of my master Abraham, give me, I pray, success today, and show kindness to my master Abraham. 
Gen 24:13 Here I am standing by the spring of water, and the daughters of the men of the town are coming out to draw water. 
Gen 24:14 May that young woman to whom I shall say, “Please let down your water-jar that I may drink”; and who answers, “Drink and I will also water your camels,” may she be the one you have chosen for thy servant Isaac. By this I shall know that you have shown kindness to my master.’  ¶ 
Gen 24:15 Then even before he was through speaking, Rebekah, who was the daughter of Bethuel son of Milcah, the wife of Nahor, Abraham’s brother, came out with her water-jar upon her shoulder. 
Gen 24:16 She was very beautiful and unmarried, a virgin. She went down to the spring, filled her jar, and came up. 
Gen 24:17 Then the servant ran to meet her and said, ‘Please let me drink a little water from your jar.’ 
Gen 24:18 She answered, ‘Drink, sir,’ and quickly let down her water-jar from her shoulder upon her hand and gave him a drink.  ¶ 
Gen 24:19 When she had finished giving him a drink she said, ‘I will draw water for your camels also, until they have finished drinking.’ 
Gen 24:20 So she quickly emptied her jar into the trough and ran again to the well to draw water, and drew for all his camels. 
Gen 24:21 Meanwhile the man was silently gazing at her in order to find out whether the  <c>Lord</c> had made his journey successful or not.  ¶ 
Gen 24:22 As soon as the camels had finished drinking, the man took a gold ring, half a shekel in weight, and put it in her nose, and put on her arms two golden bracelets weighing ten shekels, 
Gen 24:23 and said, ‘Whose daughter are you? Tell me, I beg of you. Is there room in your father’s house for us to spend the night?’ 
Gen 24:24 She answered, ‘I am the daughter of Bethuel son of of Milcah and Nahor.
