Gen 24:25 We have plenty of straw and feed, and there is a place for you to spend the night.’  ¶ 
Gen 24:26 Then the man bowed his head and worshipped the  <c>Lord</c>, 
Gen 24:27 saying, ‘Blessed be the  <c>Lord</c>, the God of my master Abraham, who has continued to show his mercy and his faithfulness toward my master. As for me, the  <c>Lord</c> has led me on the way to the house of my master’s relatives.’  ¶ 
Gen 24:28 Then the young woman ran and told these things to her mother’s family. 
Gen 24:29 Now Rebekah had a brother named Laban; and Laban ran out to the man at the spring. 
Gen 24:30 When he saw the bracelets on his sister’s hands and the ring, and when he heard Rebekah say, ‘This is what the man said to me,’ he went to the man, who was still standing by the camels at the spring, 
Gen 24:31 and said, ‘Come in, you who are blessed by the  <c>Lord</c>! Why do you stand outside? For I have cleared the house and have room for the camels.’ 
Gen 24:32 So he brought the man into the house and took the packs off the camels and furnished straw and feed for them, and water to wash his feet and the feet of the men who were with him.  ¶ 
Gen 24:33 But when food was set before him to eat, he said, ‘I will not eat until I have made known my errand.’ They answered, ‘Speak.’ 
Gen 24:34 He said, ‘I am Abraham’s servant; 
Gen 24:35 and the  <c>Lord</c> has blessed my master greatly, so that he has become very rich. He has given him flocks and herds, silver and gold, servants, and camels and donkeys. 
Gen 24:36 Now Sarah, my master’s wife, had a son when she was old, and my master has given him all that he has. 
Gen 24:37 My master also made me promise, saying, “Do not let my son marry one of the daughters of the Canaanites, in whose land I live, 
Gen 24:38 but go to my father’s home and to my relatives and there find a wife for my son.”  ¶ 
Gen 24:39 ‘When I said to my master, “What if the woman will not follow me?” 
Gen 24:40 he said to me, “The  <c>Lord</c>, whom I love and serve, will send his messenger with you and make you successful, and you will find for my son a wife from among my relatives and my father’s family. 
Gen 24:41 Then you will be free from your promise to me. But if you go to my family and they do not give her to you, you shall also be free from your promise to me.” 
Gen 24:42 So I came today to the spring and said, “ <c>Lord</c>, God of my master Abraham, see, I am standing by the spring of water. If you will make the errand on which I am going successful, then let the young woman who comes to draw, to whom I say, “Please give me a little water from your jar to drink”, 
Gen 24:44 and who shall say to me, “Drink, and I will also draw for your camels”, let that one be the woman whom the  <c>Lord</c> has chosen for my master’s son.”  ¶ 
Gen 24:45 ‘Even before I was through speaking, Rebekah came out with her water-jar on her shoulder and went down to the spring and drew water. When I said to her, “Please let me drink,” 
Gen 24:46 she quickly let down her water-jar from her shoulder and answered, “Drink, and I will also water your camels.” So I drank, and she also watered the camels. 
Gen 24:47 Then I asked her, “Whose daughter are you?” She said, “The daughter of Bethuel son of Nahor and Milcah.” So I put the ring in her nose and the bracelets on her arms. 
Gen 24:48 I bowed my head and worshipped and blessed the  <c>Lord</c> God of my master Abraham who had led me on the right way to find the daughter of my master’s brother for his son. 
Gen 24:49 Tell me whether or not you will deal kindly and truly with my master, so that I shall know what to do!’  ¶ 
Gen 24:50 Then Laban and his family answered, ‘The matter is in the hands of the  <c>Lord</c>. We cannot say either “yes” or “no.” 
Gen 24:51 See, Rebekah is before you; take her and go and let her be the wife of your master’s son, as the  <c>Lord</c> has said.’  ¶ 
Gen 24:52 When Abraham’s servant heard their words, he bowed to the ground before the  <c>Lord</c>. 
Gen 24:53 Then he brought out gold and silver ornaments and clothing and gave them to Rebekah. He also gave costly gifts to her brother and to her mother. 
Gen 24:54 He and the men who were with him ate and drank and spent the night there.  ¶ When they rose in the morning, the servant said, ‘Send me away to my master.’ 
Gen 24:55 But Rebekah’s brother and mother answered, ‘Let the young woman stay with us a month or at least ten days; after that she may go.’ 
Gen 24:56 But he said to them, ‘Do not delay me, for the  <c>Lord</c> has given me success. Send me away that I may go to my master.’  ¶ 
Gen 24:57 Then they said, ‘We will call the young woman and ask her.’ 
Gen 24:58 So they called Rebekah and said to her, ‘Will you go with this man?’ She answered, ‘I will go.’ 
Gen 24:59 So they sent away their sister Rebekah and her nurse with Abraham’s servant and his men.  ¶ 
Gen 24:60 They also blessed Rebekah, saying to her, ‘Our sister! May your children and their children become thousands and thousands, may your sons conquer the cities of their enemies!’ 
Gen 24:61 Then Rebekah set out with her maids and, riding upon the camels, they followed the man. So the servant took Rebekah and went away.  ¶ 
Gen 24:62 Now Isaac had come from Beer-lahai-roi, and was settled in the Negeb. 
Gen 24:63 In the evening, when Isaac had gone out for a walk in the field, he looked up and saw camels coming. 
Gen 24:64 Rebekah too looked up, and when she saw Isaac, she quickly alighted from the camel 
Gen 24:65 and said to the servant, ‘Who is this man walking in the field to meet us?’ When the servant said, ‘It is my master,’ she took her veil and covered her face. 
Gen 24:66 Then the servant told Isaac all that he had done. 
Gen 24:67 Isaac brought Rebekah to the tent of Sarah his mother, and she became his wife; and he loved her. So Isaac was comforted after his mother’s death.  ¶ 
Gen 25:1 Abraham had taken another wife, whose name was Keturah. 
Gen 25:2 She gave him sons: Zimran, Jokshan, Medan, Midian, Ishbak, and Shuah. 
Gen 25:3 Jokshan fathered Sheba, and Dedan. T he sons of Dedan were Asshurim, Letushim, and Leummim; 
Gen 25:4 and the sons of Midian were Ephah, Epher, Hanoch, Abida, and Eldaah. All these were descendants of Keturah.  ¶ 
Gen 25:5 Abraham had left all that he had to Isaac. 
Gen 25:6 But to the sons of his concubines, Abraham had given gifts while he was still alive, and had sent them away from Isaac his son, eastward, to the east country.  ¶ 
Gen 25:7 Abraham had lived for one hundred and seventy-five years, 
Gen 25:8 when he breathed his last, dying in a good old age, old and satisfied with living, and was gathered to his forefathers.  ¶ 
Gen 25:9 Then Isaac and Ishmael his sons buried him in the cave of Machpelah, in the field of Ephron the son of Zohar the Hittite, which is east of Mamre, 
Gen 25:10 the field which Abraham purchased from the Hittites. There Abraham was buried with Sarah his wife.  ¶ 
Gen 25:11 After the death of Abraham, God blessed Isaac his son, who settled at Beer-lahai-roi.  ¶ 
Gen 25:12 This is a list of descedents of Ishmael, Abraham’s son whom Hagar the Egyptian, Sarah’s maid-servant gave to Abraham. 
Gen 25:13 These then are the names of the sons of Ishmael, named according to their order of birth: the first-born of Ishmael, Nebaioth; then Kedar, Adbeel, Mibsam, 
Gen 25:14 Mishma, Dumah, Massa, 
Gen 25:15 Hadad, Tema, Jetur, Naphish, and Kedemah. 
Gen 25:16 These are the sons of Ishmael, and these are their names, by their villages, and by their encampments, twelve princes according to their peoples.  ¶ 
Gen 25:17 Ishmael lived for one hundred and thirty-seven years; and he breathed his last, and was gathered to his people. 
Gen 25:18 They settled from Havilah to Shur that is east of Egypt, as far as Assyria; he settled down alongside all his people.  ¶ 
Gen 25:19 These are the descendants of Isaac, Abraham’s son. Abraham fathered Isaac. 
Gen 25:20 Isaac was forty years old, when he married Rebekah, the daughter of Bethuel the Aramean of Paddan-aram, the sister of Laban the Aramean.  ¶ 
Gen 25:21 Isaac prayed to the  <c>Lord</c> for his wife, because she had no children; and the  <c>Lord</c> heard his prayer, and Rebekah became pregnant with twins. 
Gen 25:22 The children struggled against each other in her womb, and she said, ‘Why is this happening to me? What does it mean?’ She went to ask the  <c>Lord</c>, 
Gen 25:23 who said to her, <br>	‘Two nations are in your womb, <br>		two peoples divided from birth, <br>	One will be stronger than the other, <br>		the elder will serve the younger.’  ¶ 
Gen 25:24 When the time came for her to give birth, she became the mother of twin boys. 
Gen 25:25 The first was from birth red, all over like a hairy mantle; so they named him Esau <sup>[ Hairy ]</sup>. 
Gen 25:26 Afterwards his brother came holding Esau’s heel with his hand; so he was named Jacob <sup>[ Supplanter ]</sup>. Isaac was sixty years old when they were born.  ¶ 
Gen 25:27 As they grew up, Esau became a skilful hunter, a man who lived out in the fields; but Jacob was a quiet man who stayed about the tents. 
Gen 25:28 Isaac loved Esau, for he had a taste for venison; but Rebekah loved Jacob.  ¶ 
Gen 25:29 Once when Jacob was preparing a stew, Esau came in from the fields, and he was very hungry; 
Gen 25:30 so he said to Jacob, ‘Let me swallow some of that red stew, for I am very hungry.’ (This is why he was called Edom.) 
Gen 25:31 But Jacob said, ‘Sell me first of all your right as the eldest.’ 
Gen 25:32 Esau replied, ‘See, I am nearly dead now! So of what use is this birthright to me?’ 
Gen 25:33 Jacob said, ‘First solemnly promise to give it to me.’ So Esau solemnly promised and sold his birthright to Jacob. 
Gen 25:34 Then Jacob gave Esau bread and stewed lentils, and when he had finished eating and drinking, he got up and went away. In this way Esau gave away his birthright.  ¶ 
Gen 26:1 Now when a famine came in the land, (not the first famine that was in the days of Abraham), Isaac went to Abimelech king of the Philistines at Gerar.  ¶ 
Gen 26:2 The  <c>Lord</c> appeared to him and said, ‘Go not down into Egypt; settle in the land of which I will tell you, 
Gen 26:3 stay in this land, and I will be with you and will bless you; for to you, and to your descendants, I will give all these lands, and will establish the oath which I swore to Abraham your father: 
Gen 26:4 I will make your descendants as many as the stars of heaven, and give to your descendants all these lands; and all the nations of the earth will invoke for themselves a blessing like that of your descendants, 
Gen 26:5 because Abraham obeyed my voice and kept my charge, my commandments, my statutes, and my laws.’ 
Gen 26:6 So Isaac settled in Gerar.  ¶ 
Gen 26:7 The men of the place asked him about his wife; and he said, ‘She is my sister’; for he was afraid to say ‘my wife’; lest the men of the place kill him for Rebekah; because she was beautiful to look at. 
Gen 26:8 But after he had been there a long time, Abimelech king of the Philistines looked out of the window, and saw Isaac just as he was caressing Rebekah his wife.  ¶ 
Gen 26:9 Then Abimelech called to Isaac, and said, ‘Surely she is your wife; why did you say “She is my sister?”’ Isaac answered him, ‘I said it, so that I might not die because of her.’ 
Gen 26:10 Abimelech said, ‘What is this you have done to us? One of the people might have lain with your wife and so you would have brought guilt upon us.’ 
Gen 26:11 Abimelech warned all the people, saying, ‘The person who touches this man or his wife will be put to death.’  ¶ 
Gen 26:12 Then Isaac sowed in that land, and reaped in the same year an increase of a hundredfold, for the  <c>Lord</c> blessed him. 
Gen 26:13 The man became rich, and grew richer and richer until he became very wealthy; for he had many flocks, and many herds, and a great household; so that the Philistines envied him.  ¶ 
Gen 26:14 Now all the wells which Isaac’s father’s servants had dug in the days of Abraham his father, the Philistines had stopped, and filled with earth. 
Gen 26:15 But Isaac dug again the wells of water, which they had dug in the days of Abraham his father — for the Philistines had stopped them after the death of Abraham and he gave them the same names as his father had given them.  ¶ 
Gen 26:16 Abimelech said to Isaac, ‘Go from us; for you are much mightier than we are.’ 
Gen 26:17 So Isaac departed, and encamped in the valley of Gerar, and settled there. 
Gen 26:18 Isaac reopened the wells which had been dug in the days of his father Abraham and stopped by the Philistines after his death. He called them by the names his father had given them. 
Gen 26:19 When Isaac’s slaves dug in the valley, they found there a well of spring water. 
Gen 26:20 The herdsmen of Gerar quarreled with Isaac’s herdsmen, saying, ‘The water is ours.’ So he called the name of the well Esek <sup>[ Contention ]</sup>, because they contended with him. 
Gen 26:21 And when they dug another well, they quarreled over that also. So he called the name of it Sitnah <sup>[ Enmity ]</sup>. 
Gen 26:22 He moved on from these and dug another well; and over that one there was no dispute. So he called it Rehoboth <sup>[ Room ]</sup>, and said, ‘For now the  <c>Lord</c> has made room for us and we shall be fruitful in the land.’  ¶ 
Gen 26:23 Isaac went up from there to Beer-sheba. 
Gen 26:24 The  <c>Lord</c> appeared to him the same night and said, ‘I am the God of Abraham your father, do not be afraid, because I am with you, and will bless you and make your descendants numerous for the sake of my servant Abraham.’ 
Gen 26:25 Isaac built an altar there, and called upon the name of the  <c>Lord</c>, and pitched his tent there. There also Isaac’s slaves dug a well.  ¶ 
Gen 26:26 Then Abimelech came to him from Gerar with Ahuzzath his friend, and Phicol the captain of his army. 
Gen 26:27 Isaac said to them, ‘Why have you come to me, since you hated me and have driven me away from you?’ 
Gen 26:28 They said, ‘We saw plainly that the  <c>Lord</c> was with you, so we said, “Let there now be a sworn treaty between us — let us make a solemn agreement with you — 
Gen 26:29 so that you will do us no harm, as we have not touched you, and as we have done to you nothing but good, and have sent you away in peace.” You are now blessed of the  <c>Lord</c>.’ 
Gen 26:30 And he made them a feast and they ate and drank. 
Gen 26:31 Then in the morning they arose early and took oaths with each other; and Isaac sent them away, and they departed from him in peace. 
Gen 26:32 That same day, Isaac’s slaves came and told him about a well which they had dug, and said to him, ‘We have found water.’ 
Gen 26:33 He called it Shebna <sup>[ Oath ]</sup>, therefore the name of the city is Beer-sheba to this day.  ¶ 
Gen 26:34 When Esau was forty years old he married Judith the daughter of Beeri the Hittite, and Basemath the daughter of Elon the Hittite, 
Gen 26:35 and they were a source of grief to Isaac and to Rebekah.  ¶ 
Gen 27:1 When Isaac was so old and so nearly blind that he could not see, he called Esau his oldest son and said to him, ‘My son.’ Esau answered, ‘Here I am.’ 
Gen 27:2 Isaac said, ‘See, I am old and do not know how soon I may die. 
Gen 27:3 T ake your quiver and your bow and go out into the fields and hunt venison for me 
Gen 27:4 and prepare for me savory food, such as I love, and bring it to me that I may eat and that I may bless you before I die.’  ¶ 
Gen 27:5 Rebekah was listening when Isaac spoke to his son Esau. So when Esau went into the fields to hunt venison, 
Gen 27:6 Rebekah said to her son Jacob, ‘I just now heard your father say to your brother Esau, 
Gen 27:7 “Bring me venison and prepare for me savory food that I may eat it and bless you before I die.” 
Gen 27:8 Now, my son, do as I tell you: 
Gen 27:9 Go to the flock and bring me from there two good young goats, and I will make of them savory food for your father, such as he loves. 
Gen 27:10 Then take it to him, so that he may eat, so that he may bless you before he dies.’ 
Gen 27:11 But Jacob said to Rebekah his mother, ‘You know that my brother Esau is a hairy man, while I am smooth. 
Gen 27:12 Perhaps my father will touch me; then I will appear to him to be a deceiver, and I will bring blame upon me and not a blessing.’ 
Gen 27:13 But his mother said to him, ‘Let the curse be on me, my son; only obey me and go, bring the goats to me.’ 
Gen 27:14 So he went and brought them to his mother, and his mother made savory food such as his father loved.  ¶ 
Gen 27:15 Rebekah also took the fine clothes of her older son Esau, which she had with her in the tent, and put them on her younger son Jacob. 
Gen 27:16 Then she put the skins of the goats upon his hands and upon the smooth part of his neck, 
Gen 27:17 and she placed the savory food and the bread which she had prepared in his hand, 
Gen 27:18 and he went to his father and said, ‘My father.’ Isaac answered, ‘Here I am; who are you, my son?’ 
Gen 27:19 Jacob said, ‘I am Esau your oldest son. I have done as you commanded me. Sit up and eat some of my venison, so that you may bless me.’ 
Gen 27:20 Isaac said to his son, ‘How very quickly you have found it, my son.’ He answered, ‘Yes, because the  <c>Lord</c> your God gave me success.’  ¶ 
Gen 27:21 Then Isaac said to Jacob, ‘Come here, my son, that I may touch you to find out whether you are really my son Esau or not.’ 
Gen 27:22 So Jacob went near to Isaac his father, and he felt him and said, ‘The voice is the voice of Jacob, but the hands are the hands of Esau. 
Gen 27:23 Are you really my son Esau?’ Jacob answered, ‘I am.’ Isaac did not recognise him, for his hands were hairy like his brother Esau’s. So he blessed him. 
Gen 27:25 Then Isaac said, ‘Bring the food to me, that I may eat some of my son’s venison and bless you.’ So he brought it to him, and he ate. Jacob also brought him wine, and he drank.  ¶ 
Gen 27:26 Then his father Isaac said to him, ‘Come near now and kiss me, my son.’ 
Gen 27:27 As he came near and kissed him, he smelled the smell of his garment, and blessed him: <br>	See, the smell of my son <br>		is as that of fields blessed by the  <c>Lord</c>. <br>	
Gen 27:28 May God give you dew from heaven, <br>		a share in the earth’s fertile places, <br>		and plenty of corn and wine. <br>	
Gen 27:29 May peoples be subject to you, <br>		and nations bow down to you. <br>	Be master over your brothers. <br>		Let your mother’s sons bow down before you, <br>	Cursed be all who curse you. <br>		and blessed be all who bless you.  ¶ 
Gen 27:30 As soon as Isaac had given Jacob his blessing, and Jacob was about to leave his father, Esau his brother came in from his hunting. 
Gen 27:31 He also had made savory food and was bringing it to his father. So he said to him, ‘Father, rise and eat of your son’s venison, that you may bless me.’ 
Gen 27:32 But Isaac his father said to him, ‘Who are you?’ He answered, ‘I am your son, your oldest, Esau.’ 
Gen 27:33 Then Isaac trembled and said, ‘Who then is he that has hunted venison and brought it to me, so that I ate plentifully before you came, and blessed him? His blessing cannot be undone!’  ¶ 
Gen 27:34 When Esau heard the words of his father, he uttered a loud and bitter cry and said to his father, ‘Father, bless me also!’  ¶ 
Gen 27:35 But Isaac said, ‘Your brother came with deceit and has taken away your blessing.’ 
Gen 27:36 Esau said, ‘He was correctly named Jacob <sup>[ means Supplanter ]</sup>. He has supplanted me these two times: he took my birthright, and now he has taken my blessing!’ Then he said, ‘Have you kept a blessing for me?’ 
Gen 27:37 Isaac answered Esau, ‘I have made him your master and I have given to him all his relatives as slaves and grain and wine as his food. What then can I do for you, my son?’ 
Gen 27:38 Esau said to his father, ‘Is that the only blessing you have, my father? Father, bless me too!’ and Esau began to weep aloud. 
Gen 27:39 Then Isaac his father answered him: <br>	‘You shall live far from earth’s fertile places, <br>		and away from the dew of heaven. <br>	
Gen 27:40 By your sword you will live, <br>		and your brother you will serve. <br>	But whenever you will break loose, <br>		you will break off his yoke from your neck.’  ¶ 
Gen 27:41 Esau hated Jacob because of the blessing that his father had given him. Esau said to himself, ‘My father will soon die; then I will kill Jacob, my brother.’  ¶ 
Gen 27:42 When the words of her older son Esau were told to Rebekah, she sent for her younger son Jacob and said to him, ‘Your brother, Esau, is going to kill you. 
Gen 27:43 Now, my son, listen to me: run away to my brother Laban at Haran 
Gen 27:44 and stay with him for a time until your brother is no longer angry 
Gen 27:45 — until he is no longer angry and he forgets what you have done to him. Then I will send and bring you back. Why should I lose both of you in one day?’  ¶ 
Gen 27:46 Rebekah said to Isaac, ‘I am disgusted with life because of the Hittite women; if Jacob marries a Hittite woman, such as these, the women of the land, I might as well die.’  ¶ 
Gen 28:1 Then Isaac called Jacob, and blessed him, and instructed him, ‘You must not marry any of the daughters of Canaan. 
Gen 28:2 Arise, go to Paddan-aram, to the house of Bethuel your mother’s father; and marry one of the daughters of Laban, your mother’s brother. 
Gen 28:3 May God Almighty bless you, and make you fruitful and numerous, so that you may become a great people, 
Gen 28:4 and may he give the blessing of Abraham to you and to your descendants with you so that you may inherit the land you have settled in, which God gave to Abraham.’  ¶ 
Gen 28:5 So Isaac sent away Jacob, and he went to Paddan-aram to Laban, the son of Bethuel the Aramean, the brother of Rebekah, Jacob and Esau’s mother. 
Gen 28:6 Now when Esau saw that Isaac had blessed Jacob and send him away to Paddan-aram, to find a wife there, and that, as he blessed him, he instructed him: ‘You must not take a wife of the daughters of Canaan’, 
Gen 28:7 and that Jacob had obeyed his father and mother, and had gone to Paddan-aram, 
Gen 28:8 and when Esau also saw that the daughters of Canaan did not please Isaac his father, 
Gen 28:9 then Esau went to Ishmael, and in addition to the wives that he had, married Mahalath the daughter of Ishmael, Abraham’s son, the sister of Nebaioth.  ¶ 
Gen 28:10 Then Jacob set out from Beersheba and went toward Haran. 
Gen 28:11 When he arrived at a certain holy place, he passed the night there, because the sun had set. He took one of the stones from its place and put it under his head and lay down to sleep. 
Gen 28:12 Then he dreamed and saw a ladder set up on the earth, and its top reached to heaven; and the messengers of God were going up and down on it.  ¶ 
Gen 28:13 The  <c>Lord</c> also stood beside him and said, ‘I am the  <c>Lord</c>, God of Abraham and God of Isaac. The land on which you lie I will give to you and to your children. 
Gen 28:14 Your descendants will be as countless as the dust of the earth and you will spread abroad to the west, and to the east, and to the north, and to the south, and all the families of the earth will wish for a blessing like yours and that of your descendants. 
Gen 28:15 See, I am with you, and will keep you wherever you go and will bring you again to this land; for I will not leave you until I have done what I have promised you.’  ¶ 
Gen 28:16 When Jacob awoke from his sleep, he said, ‘Surely the  <c>Lord</c> is in this place, and I did not know it.’ 
Gen 28:17 And he was filled with awe and said, ‘This place is the house of God, and this is the gate of heaven.’  ¶ 
Gen 28:18 So Jacob rose early in the morning and took the stone that he had put under his head and set it up as a pillar and poured oil upon the top of it. 
Gen 28:19 He named that place Bethel <sup>[ which means House of God ]</sup>. (The earlier name of the town was Luz.) 
Gen 28:20 Jacob also made this promise, ‘If God will be with me and protect me on this journey which I am making and give me bread to eat and clothing to put on, 
Gen 28:21 and if I return safe and sound to my father’s house, then the  <c>Lord</c> shall be my God, 
Gen 28:22 and this stone which I have set up as a pillar will be a house of God. And of all that you give me I will surely give a tenth to you.’  ¶ 
Gen 29:1 Jacob continued on his journey and arrived at the land of the people of the East. 
Gen 29:2 He looked and saw a well in the field, and there were three flocks of sheep lying down by it; for from that well they watered the flocks; but there was a large stone over the well. 
Gen 29:3 When all the flocks were gathered there, the shepherds used to roll away the stone and water the sheep and then put the stone back in its place over the well.  ¶ 
Gen 29:4 Jacob said to the men, ‘My friends, from where do you come?’ They said, ‘We are from Haran.’ 
Gen 29:5 Then he said to them, ‘Do you know Laban the son of Nahor?’ They said, ‘We know him.’ 
Gen 29:6 He said to them, ‘Is all well with him?’ They said, ‘All is well; indeed, this is Rachel his daughter coming with the sheep.’ 
Gen 29:7 H e said, ‘See, the sun is still high! It is not time for the cattle to be gathered together. Water the sheep and feed them.’ 
Gen 29:8 But they said, ‘We cannot until all the flocks are gathered together, and they roll away the stone from the well; then we will water the sheep.’  ¶ 
Gen 29:9 While he was still speaking with them, Rachel came with her father’s sheep; for she was a shepherdess. 
Gen 29:10 When Jacob saw Rachel the daughter of Laban, his mother’s brother, and Laban’s sheep, he went up and rolled the stone from the well and watered the flock of Laban his mother’s brother. 
Gen 29:11 Then Jacob kissed Rachel and wept aloud. 
Gen 29:12 When Jacob told Rachel that he was a relative of her father and that he was Rebekah’s son, she ran and told her father.  ¶ 
Gen 29:13 As soon as Laban heard about Jacob, his sister’s son, he ran to meet him, put his arms round him, kissed him many times, and brought him to his home. When Jacob told Laban all that had happened, 
Gen 29:14 Laban said to him, ‘Surely you are my bone and my flesh.’ So he remained with him a whole month.  ¶ 
Gen 29:15 Then Laban said to Jacob, ‘Should you serve me for nothing simply because you are related to me? Tell me what shall be your wages?’ 
Gen 29:16 Now Laban had two daughters: the name of the older was Leah, and the name of the younger was Rachel. 
Gen 29:17 Leah’s eyes were dull, but Rachel was beautiful. 
Gen 29:18 Jacob loved Rachel, and so he said, ‘I will serve you seven years for Rachel your younger daughter.’ 
Gen 29:19 Laban said, ‘It is better for me to give her to you than to give her to any other man. Stay with me.’ 
Gen 29:20 So Jacob served seven years for Rachel, and they seemed to him but a few days, because he loved her so.  ¶ 
Gen 29:21 Then Jacob said to Laban, ‘Give me my wife, for my time is up, and let me marry her.’ 
Gen 29:22 So Laban gathered all the men of the place and made a feast. 
Gen 29:23 In the evening he took Leah his daughter and brought her to Jacob, and Jacob received her as his wife. 
Gen 29:24 At the same time Laban gave his slave-girl Zilpah to his daughter Leah.  ¶ 
Gen 29:25 When in the morning Jacob found it was Leah, he said to Laban, ‘What is this you have done to me? Did I not serve you for Rachel? Why then have you deceived me?’ 
Gen 29:26 Laban said, ‘It is not the custom among us to give the younger in marriage before the older. 
Gen 29:27 Remain with this one during the marriage week, then we will give you the other also for the service which you will give me during seven more years.’ 
Gen 29:28 Jacob did so: he remained with Leah during the marriage week. Then Laban gave him Rachel his daughter to be his wife, 
Gen 29:29 and his slave-girl Bilhah to serve Rachel. 
Gen 29:30 Jacob slept with Rachel as well, and loved Rachel more than Leah. So he had to serve Laban seven years more.  ¶ 
Gen 29:31 When the  <c>Lord</c> saw that Leah was spurned, he gave her the gift of motherhood; Rachel, however, was barren. 
Gen 29:32 So Leah gave birth to a son whom she named Reuben <sup>[ Behold a son ]</sup>; for she said, ‘The  <c>Lord</c> has seen my affliction; now my husband will love me.’ 
Gen 29:33 She gave birth to another son; and said, ‘Because the  <c>Lord</c> has heard that I am spurned, he has given me this one also’; and she called his name Simeon <sup>[ Hearing ]</sup>. 
Gen 29:34 She gave birth to another son and said, ‘Now this time my husband will become attached to me because I have borne him three sons’; therefore his name was called Levi <sup>[ Attached ]</sup>. 
Gen 29:35 She gave birth to another son and said, ‘This time I will praise the  <c>Lord</c>’; therefore she called his name Judah <sup>[ Praise ]</sup> then she stopped having children.  ¶ 
Gen 30:1 When Rachel saw that she bore Jacob no children, she was jealous of her sister and said to Jacob, ‘Give me children or else I will die.’ 
Gen 30:2 But Jacob’s anger was aroused against Rachel, and he said, ‘Am I in God’s place? Who has withheld offspring from you?’ 
Gen 30:3 She said, ‘Here is my slave-girl Bilhah, go to her, so that she may bear sons who can be laid on my knees and I also may obtain children though her.’ 
Gen 30:4 So she gave him Bilhah her slave-girl for a wife, and Jacob slept with her. 
Gen 30:5 When Bilhah conceived and bore Jacob a son, 
Gen 30:6 Rachel said, ‘God has judged me and has also heard my voice and has given me a son.’ So she called his name Dan <sup>[ He judged ]</sup>.  ¶ 
Gen 30:7 Bilhah, Rachel’s slave-girl conceived again, and bore Jacob a second son. 
Gen 30:8 Rachel said, ‘With superhuman wrestlings have I wrestled with my sister, and have prevailed’; so she called his name Naphtali <sup>[ Obtained by wrestling ]</sup>.  ¶ 
Gen 30:9 When Leah saw that she had stopped having children, she took Zilpah her slave-girl, and gave her to Jacob as a wife. 
Gen 30:10 Zilpah, Leah’s slave-girl bore Jacob a son. 
Gen 30:11 Leah said, ‘Fortunate!’ and she called his name Gad. 
Gen 30:12 Zilpah bore Jacob a second son, 
Gen 30:13 and Leah said, ‘Happy am I! Now women will call me happy’, and she called his name Asher.  ¶ 
Gen 30:14 One time, during the wheat harvest, Reuben went and found mandrakes in the field and brought them to his mother Leah. Rachel asked Leah, ‘Please give me some of your son’s mandrakes.’ 
Gen 30:15 But Leah said to her, ‘Is it a small matter that you have taken away my husband, that you would also take away my son’s mandrakes?’ Rachel said, ‘In exchange for your son’s mandrakes, Jacob can sleep with you tonight.’ 
Gen 30:16 So when Jacob came from the field in the evening, Leah went out to meet him, and said, ‘You sleep with me tonight, for I have hired you with my son’s mandrakes.’ So he slept with her that night.  ¶ 
Gen 30:17 God heard Leah’s prayer, and she conceived and bore Jacob a fifth son. 
Gen 30:18 Leah said, ‘God has given me my reward, because I gave my slave-girl to my husband’; so she called his name Issachar <sup>[ There is a hire ]</sup>. 
Gen 30:19 Leah conceived again, and bore a sixth son to Jacob. 
Gen 30:20 She said, ‘God has endowed me with a good dowry; now my husband will honour me, because I have borne him six sons’; and she called him Zebulun <sup>[ Dwelling ]</sup>. 
Gen 30:21 And afterwards she had a daughter and named her Dinah.  ¶ 
Gen 30:22 Then God remembered Rachel and heard her prayer and gave her a child. 
Gen 30:23 She conceived and gave birth to a son and said, ‘God has taken away my disgrace.’ 
Gen 30:24 She called his name Joseph <sup>[ He will add ]</sup>, saying, ‘the  <c>Lord</c> will add to me another son.’  ¶ 
Gen 30:25 When Rachel had given birth to Joseph, Jacob said to Laban, ‘Send me away, so that I may go to my own place, and to my country. 
Gen 30:26 Give me my wives and my children for whom I have served you, so that I may go; for you know the service which I have rendered you.’ 
Gen 30:27 But Laban said to him, ‘If now I have found favour in your eyes — I have divined that the  <c>Lord</c> has blessed me for your sake. 
Gen 30:28 State exactly to me your wages and I will pay them.’  ¶ 
Gen 30:29 Jacob answered him, ‘You know how I have served you and what your cattle have become under my care; 
Gen 30:30 for it was little which you had before I came, but now it has greatly increased, since the  <c>Lord</c> has blessed you wherever I went. But now, when am I to provide for my own house as well?’ 
Gen 30:31 Laban said, ‘What should I give you?’  ¶ Jacob said, ‘You do not need to give me anything. If you will do this thing for me, I will again feed your flock; I will again keep it. 
Gen 30:32 If I can go through all your flock today, and remove from it every black one among the lambs and the spotted and speckled among the goats; these will be my wages. 
Gen 30:33 So my honesty will testify for me later, when you come to inspect my wages: every one that is not speckled and spotted among the goats and black among the lambs has been stolen by me.’ 
Gen 30:34 Laban said, ‘Good, let it be as you say.’ 
Gen 30:35 But he removed that day the he-goats that were striped and spotted, and all the she-goats that were striped and spotted, every one that had white on it, and all the black ones among the lambs, and gave them into the hands of his sons. 
Gen 30:36 Then he put the distance of a three days’ journey between himself and Jacob; and Jacob fed the rest of Laban’s flocks.  ¶ 
Gen 30:37 Jacob, however, took fresh rods of white poplar, and of the almond and of the plane tree, and peeled white streaks in them, exposing the white which was in the rods. 
Gen 30:38 He set the rods which he had peeled before the flocks in the watering-troughs where the flocks came to drink (and they conceived when they came to drink) 
Gen 30:39 so that the flocks conceived before the rods. Therefore the flocks brought forth striped, speckled and spotted offspring. 
Gen 30:40 Jacob separated the lambs, and he set the faces of the flocks toward the striped and the black animals in the flock of Laban and he put his own droves apart and did not put them near Laban’s flock.  ¶ 
Gen 30:41 Whenever the stronger animals of the flock conceived, Jacob laid the rods in the troughs before the eyes of the flock, so that they might conceive among the rods. 
Gen 30:42 But when the animals were weak, he did not put them in. In this way the weaker became Laban’s, and the stronger Jacobs’s.  ¶ 
Gen 30:43 So the man increased in wealth exceedingly, and had large flocks, and male and female slaves, and camels and donkeys.  ¶ 
Gen 31:1 Now Jacob heard Laban’s sons say, ‘Jacob has taken all that was our father’s, and from that which was our father’s he has acquired all these riches.’ 
Gen 31:2 Now Jacob observed that Laban was not so favorably inclined to him as formerly. 
Gen 31:3 The  <c>Lord</c> said to Jacob, ‘Return to the land of your ancestors, and to your relatives, and I will be with you.’ 
Gen 31:4 Then Jacob sent for Rachel and Leah to come to the field where his flocks were, 
Gen 31:5 and said to them, ‘I see that your father is not so favorably inclined toward me as formerly; but the God of my father has been with me. 
Gen 31:6 You know that I have served your father with all my strength. 
Gen 31:7 Your father, however, has deceived me and changed my wages ten times; but God has not allowed him to do me harm. 
Gen 31:8 If your father said, “The speckled will be your wages,” then all the flock bore speckled offspring, but if he said: “The striped will be your wages,” then all the flock have striped offspring. 
Gen 31:9 God has taken away the possessions of your father and given them to me. 
Gen 31:10 At the time when the flock breed, I looked up, and saw in a dream, that the he-goats which were mating were striped, speckled, and piebald. 
Gen 31:11 The messenger of God said to me in a dream, “Jacob!” and I said, “Here I am.” 
Gen 31:12 And he said, “Look! All the he-goats which are mating are striped, speckled, and piebald: for I have seen all that Laban has been doing to you. 
Gen 31:13 I am the God of Bethel, where you anointed a pillar of stone, where you made a vow to me. Now arise, leave this land, and return to the land where you were born.”’  ¶ 
Gen 31:14 Then Rachel and Leah answered him, ‘There is no longer any inheritance for us in our father’s house. 
Gen 31:15 Are we not considered as foreigners by him? For he has sold us and goes on to consume the money paid for us. 
Gen 31:16 Since all the riches which God has taken away from our father is ours and our children’s, do whatever God has told you to do.’  ¶ 
Gen 31:17 Then Jacob rose up and put his sons and his wives on camels, 
Gen 31:18 and drove away all his cattle and all the cattle which he had acquired in Paddan-aram, in order to go to Isaac his father, to the land of Canaan. 
Gen 31:19 And while Laban was gone to shear his sheep, Rachel stole the household gods that were her father’s. 
Gen 31:20 So Jacob deceived Laban the Aramean — he did not tell him that he was going to flee. 
Gen 31:21 So he fled with all he had; crossing the river Euphrates heading towards the hill-country of Gilead.  ¶ 
Gen 31:22 When it was reported to Laban on the third day that Jacob had fled, 
Gen 31:23 he took his tribesmen with him, and pursued him for seven days, and overtook him in the hill country of Gilead. 
Gen 31:24 But God came to Laban the Aramean in a dream at night, and said to him, ‘Take care that you do not speak to Jacob either good or bad.’ 
Gen 31:25 When Laban caught up with Jacob, Jacob had pitched his tent in the hill country; and Laban with his relatives encamped in same hill country of Gilead.  ¶ 
Gen 31:26 Laban said to Jacob, ‘What have you done? You have deceived me and carried away my daughters like captives of war! 
Gen 31:27 Why did you flee secretly, stealing away from me without telling me? I would have sent you away with mirth and with songs, with tambourine and with harp — 
Gen 31:28 but you did not allow me to kiss my sons and daughters. You have acted foolishly. 
Gen 31:29 It was in my power to do you harm, but the God of your father spoke to me last night saying, “Take care that you do not speak to Jacob, neither good nor bad.” 
Gen 31:30 But now, since you are surely going because you long so earnestly for your father’s house, why have you stolen my gods?’  ¶ 
Gen 31:31 Jacob answered Laban, ‘I was afraid, because I thought you would take your daughters from me by force. 
Gen 31:32 The one with whom you find your gods will be put to death; in the presence of our kinsmen investigate for yourself what is with me and take it.’ Jacob did not know that Rachel had stolen Laban’s gods. 
Gen 31:33 So Laban went into Jacob’s tent and into Leah’s, and into the tent of the two slave-girls, but he did not find his gods. Then he went out of Leah’s tent, and entered Rachel’s. 
Gen 31:34 Now Rachel had taken the household gods and put them in the camel’s saddle and was sitting on them, so that when Laban had searched all about the tent, he did not find them. 
Gen 31:35 She said to her father, ‘Do not be angry that I cannot rise before you, my lord, for it is that time of the month that women have.’ And though he searched thoroughly, he did not find the household gods.  ¶ 
Gen 31:36 Then Jacob became angry and challenged Laban. ‘What is my crime?’ he said, ‘What is my offense, that you have pursued hotly after me? 
Gen 31:37 Alhough you have gone through all through my things, what have you found of all your household possessions? Declare it here before my kinsmen and yours, so that they may decide which of us two is in the right. 
Gen 31:38 In all these twenty years that have I been with you, your ewes and she-goats have not miscarried their young, neither did I eat the rams of your flocks. 
Gen 31:39 I did not bring to you the animals which were killed by wild beasts; I bore the loss of it myself; from my hand you required compensation, whether stolen by day or stolen by night. 
Gen 31:40 This was how I was: in the day the heat consumed me, and by night the frost, and sleep deserted me. 
Gen 31:41 These twenty years I have been in your house; I served you fourteen years for your two daughters, and six years for your flock, and you have changed my wages ten times. 
Gen 31:42 Unless the God of my father, the God of Abraham and the Fear of Isaac, had been with me, surely by now you would have sent me away empty. But God has seen my affliction and the labour of my hands, and he rebuked you last night.’  ¶ 
Gen 31:43 Then Laban answered Jacob, ‘The daughters are my daughters, and the children are my grandchildren, and the flocks are my flocks, and all that you see is mine, but what can I do today for these my daughters, or for their children whom they have borne? 
Gen 31:44 Come, let us make a solemn agreement, I and you, and let there be a witness between me and you.’  ¶ 
Gen 31:45 So Jacob took a stone, and set it up as a pillar, 
Gen 31:46 and said to the members of his family, ‘Gather stones.’ When they had taken stones and made a heap, they ate there by the heap. 
Gen 31:47 Laban called it Jegar-sahaduthap <sup>[ Heap of witness ]</sup>; but Jacob called it Galeed <sup>[ Heap of witness ]</sup>. 
Gen 31:48 ‘This heap’, Laban said, ‘is witness between me and you today.’ This is why it was called Galeed, 
Gen 31:49 and Mizpah <sup>[ Place of watching ]</sup>, for Laban said, ‘May the  <c>Lord</c> watch between me and you when we are absent one from another, 
Gen 31:50 so that you may not maltreat my daughters nor take other wives besides my daughters. No one is with us; but beware: God is witness between me and you.’  ¶ 
Gen 31:51 Moreover, Laban said to Jacob, ‘See this heap, and the pillar which I have set up between me and you. 
Gen 31:52 This heap is a witness and the pillar is a witness that I should not pass beyond this heap to you and that you must not pass beyond this heap and this pillar to me, with hostile intent. 
Gen 31:53 The God of Abraham and the God of Nahor’ (the God of their ancestors) ‘judge between us.’ And Jacob swore by the Fear of his father Isaac.  ¶ 
Gen 31:54 Then Jacob offered a sacrifice there on the mountain and called his kinsmen to eat bread, and they ate bread and spent the night on the mountain.  ¶ 
Gen 31:55 Then early in the morning Laban arose, and, when he had kissed his grandchildren and his daughters and blessed them, he departed and returned to his home.  ¶ 
Gen 32:1 Jacob went on his way and the messengers of God met him. 
Gen 32:2 When he saw them, Jacob said, ‘This is God’s camp;’ so he named the place ‘Mahanaim <sup>[ Company ]</sup>.’  ¶ 
Gen 32:3 Jacob sent messengers before him to his brother Esau, to the land of Seir, which is the territory of the Edomites. 
Gen 32:4 He gave them this command, ‘Say to my lord Esau: “Your servant Jacob declares, I have lived with Laban and have stayed until now. 
Gen 32:5 I have oxen and donkeys, flocks and male and female slaves, and I have sent to tell my lord, in order that I may win your favour.”’ 
Gen 32:6 The messengers returned to Jacob with the report, ‘We came to your brother Esau, even as he was coming to meet you with four hundred men.’  ¶ 
Gen 32:7 Then Jacob was greatly alarmed and worried. So he divided the people that were with him and the flocks and the herds and the camels into two parts 
Gen 32:8 and said, ‘If Esau comes to the one and attacks and destroys it, then the other which is left can escape.’  ¶ 
Gen 32:9 Jacob also prayed, ‘God of my father Abraham and God of my father Isaac,  <c>Lord</c> who said to me, “Return to your country, and to your relatives, and I will do well by you,” 
Gen 32:10 I am not worthy of the least of all the mercies and all the faithfulness which you have shown to me, your servant. I passed over the Jordan river with only my staff, and now I have these two groups, 
Gen 32:11 deliver me, I pray, from the hand of my brother, from the hand of Esau, for I fear that he will come and attack me and kill the mothers and the children. 
Gen 32:12 Remember your promise to make me prosper and my descendants as many as the sand of the seashore, uncountable.’  ¶ 
Gen 32:13 After spending the night there, Jacob took from his livestock as a present for his brother Esau, 
Gen 32:14 two hundred female goats and twenty male goats, two hundred ewes and twenty rams, 
Gen 32:15 thirty milch camels and their young, forty cows and ten bulls, twenty female donkeys and ten young donkeys. 
Gen 32:16 These he put, each drove by itself, in the care of his servants and said to them, ‘Go on before me and leave a space between the droves.’  ¶ 
Gen 32:17 He gave those in front this command: ‘When my brother Esau meets you and asks you, “To whom do you belong? And where are you going? And whose are these before you?” 
Gen 32:18 then you shall say, “To your servant Jacob; it is a present sent by him to my lord Esau; and Jacob himself is just behind us.”’ 
Gen 32:19 Jacob also commanded the second, and the third, and all that followed the droves, to make the same answer, 
Gen 32:20 and to say, ‘Jacob himself is just behind us.’ For he said to himself, ‘I will please him with the present that goes before me, and then, when I meet him, perhaps he will welcome me.’ 
Gen 32:21 So he sent the present over before him; but he himself spent that night in the camp.  ¶ 
Gen 32:22 Later that night he rose up and took his two wives, his two slave-girls, and his eleven children, and sent them over the river Jabbok.  ¶ 
Gen 32:23 After he had sent them accross with all his belongings, 
Gen 32:24 Jacob was left alone, and someone wrestled with him until daybreak. 
Gen 32:25 When he saw that he did not win against Jacob, he struck the socket of his hip, and the socket of Jacob’s hip was dislocated, as he wrestled with him. 
Gen 32:26 Then he said, ‘Let me go, for the dawn is breaking.’ But Jacob replied, ‘I will not let you go unless you bless me.’ 
Gen 32:27 So he said to him, ‘What is your name?’ He answered, ‘Jacob.’ 
Gen 32:28 Then he said, ‘Your name shall be no longer Jacob, but Israel <sup>[ which means Struggler with God ]</sup>; for you have struggled with God and with mortals and have won.’ 
Gen 32:29 Jacob asked him, ‘Tell me, I pray, your name.’ He said,‘Why do you ask my name?’ So he blessed him there. 
Gen 32:30 Jacob called the place Penuel <sup>[ which means Face of God ]</sup>, for he said, ‘I have seen God face to face, and my life has been saved.’  ¶ 
Gen 32:31 The sun rose as soon as he had passed beyond Penuel, and he limped because of his hip. 
Gen 32:32 This is why to this day the Israelites do not eat the thigh muscle, which is at the socket of the hip, because he touched the socket of Jacob’s hip on the thigh muscle.  ¶ 
Gen 33:1 When Jacob looked up, he saw Esau coming with four hundred men. So he divided the children between Leah and Rachel and the two slave-girls. 
Gen 33:2 He put the slave-girls and their children in front, Leah and her children next, and Rachel and her son Joseph in the rear. 
Gen 33:3 Then Jacob himself went in front of them, and he bowed down to the ground seven times, as he drew near to his brother. 
Gen 33:4 Esau ran to meet him, threw his arms about his neck, and kissed him, and they wept.  ¶ 
Gen 33:5 When Esau looked up and saw the women and the children, he said, ‘Who are these with you?’ Jacob answered, ‘The children whom God has so kindly given me.’ 
Gen 33:6 Then the slave-girls with their children came up and bowed down to the ground. 
Gen 33:7 Leah and her children also came and bowed down, and afterward Joseph and Rachel came up and bowed down before Esau.  ¶ 
Gen 33:8 Esau asked, ‘What do you mean by all this company which I met?’ Jacob answered, ‘To win your friendship, my lord.’ 
Gen 33:9 Esau said, ‘I have enough, my brother; keep what you have.’ 
Gen 33:10 But Jacob replied, ‘No, if now I have won your favour, receive this present from me, because seeing your face when you welcomed me was like seeing the face of God. 
Gen 33:11 Take, I beg of you, the gift that I bring to you, for God has been generous to me and I have enough.’ So he urged Esau until he took it.  ¶ 
Gen 33:12 Then Esau said, ‘Let us set out on our way, and let me travel with you.’ 
Gen 33:13 But Jacob replied, ‘My lord knows that the children are delicate, and I have flocks and herds with their young; if they are overdriven one day, all the flocks will die. 
Gen 33:14 Let my lord, I beg of you, go on ahead of me, and I will proceed leisurely by stages according to the pace of the cattle which I am driving and of the children, until I come to my lord at Seir.’ 
Gen 33:15 Then Esau said, ‘Let me at least leave with you some of the people who are with me.’ But Jacob replied, ‘What need is there? Let me only enjoy the favour of my lord.’ 
Gen 33:16 So Esau turned back that day on his way to Seir.  ¶ 
Gen 33:17 But Jacob journeyed to Succoth, and built there a house for himself, and made huts for his cattle; therefore the name of the place is called Succoth <sup>[ Huts ]</sup>. 
Gen 33:18 Now Jacob came in peace to the city of Shechem in the land of Canaan, when he came from Paddan-Aram, and encamped before the city. 
Gen 33:19 He bought the piece of ground where he pitched his tent from the sons of Hamor, the father of Shechem, for four hundred shekels; 
Gen 33:20 and he erected there an altar and called it El, God of Israel.  ¶ 
Gen 34:1 Dinah the daughter of Leah and Jacob, went out to visit the women of the region. 
Gen 34:2 When Sheeham the son of Hamor the Hivite, the prince of the region, saw her, he took her and lay with her and violated her, 
Gen 34:3 but his heart was drawn to Dinah the daughter of Jacob — he loved her and spoke endearingly to her. 
Gen 34:4 Therefore Shechem said to his father Hamor, ‘Get me this girl for my wife.’  ¶ 
Gen 34:5 When Jacob heard that Shecham had defiled Dinah his daughter, his sons were with his cattle in the field, so Jacob said nothing until they came home. 
Gen 34:6 Meanwhile Hamor the father of Shechem went out to Jacob to speak with him and with his sons.  ¶ 
Gen 34:7 The sons of Jacob came in from the field, and when they heard the news, the men were indignant and became very angry, because Shechem had committed a shameful crime in raping Jacob’s daughter: such a thing ought never to be done. 
Gen 34:8 Hamor said to them, ‘My son Shechem has set his heart on your daughter. I beg you: give her to him as a wife 
Gen 34:9 and intermarry with us. Give your daughters to us and take our daughters for yourselves. 
Gen 34:10 Then you can settle with us, and the land will be open before you. Remain, go about, and settle down in it.’  ¶ 
Gen 34:11 And Shechem said to Dinah’s father and to her brothers, ‘Let me find favour in your sight, and I will give you what you ask of me. 
Gen 34:12 Demand of me an exceedingly large gift for yourselves and a dowry for the bride, and I shall give all you ask of me; only give me the girl for my wife.’  ¶ 
Gen 34:13 Then the sons of Jacob answered Shechem and Hamor his father deceitfully, declaring, (because he had defiled their sister Dinah), 
Gen 34:14 ‘We cannot do this. We cannot give our sister to someone who is uncircumcised, for that would be a disgrace to us. 
Gen 34:15 Only on this condition will we make an alliance with you: if you will be as we are, in that every male of you be circumcised. 
Gen 34:16 Then will we give our daughters to you and take your daughters to us and will live with you and we will become one people. 
Gen 34:17 But if you will not listen to us and allow yourselves to be circumcised, then we will take Dinah and be gone.’  ¶ 
Gen 34:18 Their proposal pleased Hamor and his son Shechem. 
Gen 34:19 The young man (who was honored above all the house of his father) did not hesitate to do the thing demanded, because he was smitten with Jacob’s daughter. 
Gen 34:20 Hamor and his son Shechem came to the gate of their city, and conversed with the men of their city, saying, 
Gen 34:21 ‘These men are peaceably disposed toward us, let them remain in the land and go about in it; the land is broad enough for them on every side and in every direction; let us take their daughters to us for wives, and let us give them our daughters. 
Gen 34:22 Only on this condition will these men consent to settle with us to become one people, namely, that every male among us be circumcised, as they are circumcised. 
Gen 34:23 Shouldn’t their cattle and their goods and all their beasts be ours? Let us make an alliance with them so that they will live with us.’ 
Gen 34:24 Then all who went in and out of the gate of his city agreed with Hamor and Shechem. And every male was circumcised, all who went out of the gate of his city.  ¶ 
Gen 34:25 On the third day when they were still in pain, two of the sons of Jacob, Simeon and Levi, Dinah’s brothers, took swords and came upon the city unawares, 
Gen 34:26 and put Hamor and his son Shechem to the sword, and took Dinah out of Shechem’s house and went away. 
Gen 34:27 The other sons of Jacob came on the slain, and plundered the city, because they had defiled their sister. 
Gen 34:28 They took their flocks and their herds and their donkeys and all that which was in the city and all that which was in the field. 
Gen 34:29 All their wealth, and all their children and their wives, they took captive, and made all that was in the houses their prey. 
Gen 34:30 Then Jacob said to Simeon and Levi, ‘You have brought me into trouble, in that you have made me odious to the inhabitants of the land, among the Canaanites and the Perizzites. Since I have only a few people, if they gather themselves together against me they will attack me — and I and my house will be destroyed.’ 
Gen 34:31 But they replied, ‘Should he have treated our sister like a whore?’  ¶ 
Gen 35:1 Then God said to Jacob, ‘Arise, go up to Bethel, and live there. Make an altar there to God, who appeared to you when you fled from your brother Esau.’ 
Gen 35:2 So Jacob said to his household, and to everyone who was with him, ‘Put away the foreign gods that are among you, and purify yourselves, and change your garments. 
Gen 35:3 Let us arise and go up to Bethel. I will make there an altar to God, who answered me in the day of my distress, and was with me on the journey which I was making.’ 
Gen 35:4 So they gave to Jacob all the foreign gods which were in their possession, and the rings which were in their ears, and Jacob hid them under the oak which was by Shechem. 
Gen 35:5 They set out on their journey, and a terror of God was upon the cities that were round about them, and they did not pursue after the sons of Jacob. 
Gen 35:6 Then Jacob came to Luz, which is in the land of Canaan (that is, Bethel). He and all the people that were with him came to Bethel. 
Gen 35:7 He built there an altar, and named the place El-Bethel <sup>[ The God of the house of God ]</sup>; because there God revealed himself to him, when he fled from the presence of his brother. 
Gen 35:8 Then Deborah, Rebekah’s nurse, died, and was buried below Bethel under the oak. Therefore its name was called Allon-bacuth <sup>[ Oak of Weeping ]</sup>.  ¶ 
Gen 35:9 God appeared again to Jacob when he came from Paddanaram, and blessed him. 
Gen 35:10 God said to him, ‘Now your name is Jacob: but your name will no longer be Jacob, but Israel.’ So he called his name Israel. 
Gen 35:11 God said to him, ‘I am God Almighty; be fruitful and become numerous; a nation and a multitude of nations will come from you, and kings will descend from you; 
Gen 35:12 and the land which I gave to Abraham and Isaac, I will give to you, and to your descendants after you.’ 
Gen 35:13 God went up from him at that place where he spoke with him. 
Gen 35:14 Jacob set up at the place where God had spoken with him, a pillar of stone, and poured a drink-offering and oil on it. 
Gen 35:15 Jacob called the name of the place where God spoke with him, Bethel.  ¶ 
Gen 35:16 Then they set out from Bethel, and when they were still some distance from Ephrath, Rachel went into a hard and painful labour. 
Gen 35:17 At the hardest, the midwife said to her, ‘Do not be afraid; for now you will have another son.’ 
Gen 35:18 And, as her life was departing (for she was dying), she called his name Ben-oni <sup>[ Son of my Sorrow ]</sup>; but his father called him Benjamin <sup>[ Son of the right hand ]</sup>. 
Gen 35:19 So Rachel died, and was buried on the way to Ephrath (that is, Bethlehem), 
Gen 35:20 and Jacob set up a pillar on her grave: that is the Pillar of Rachel’s Grave, which stands until this day.  ¶ 
Gen 35:21 Then Israel journeyed, and pitched his tent beyond Migdal-Eder <sup>[ Tower of the Flock ]</sup>. 
Gen 35:22 While Israel was living in that land, Reuben went and lay with his father’s concubine Bilhah and Israel heard of it.  ¶ Now the sons of Jacob were twelve: 
Gen 35:23 The sons of Leah: Reuben, Jacob’s firstborn, and Simeon, and Levi, and Judah, and Issachar, and Zebulun; 
Gen 35:24 the sons of Rachel: Joseph and Benjamin; 
Gen 35:25 and the sons of Bilhah, Rachel’s slave-girl: Dan and Naphtali; 
Gen 35:26 and the sons of Zilpah, Leah’s slave-girl: Gad and Asher (these are the sons of Jacob, that were born to him in Paddan-aram).  ¶ 
Gen 35:27 Then Jacob came to Isaac his father, to Mamre, near Kiriath-arba (that is, Hebron), where Abraham and Isaac had stayed. 
Gen 35:28 The length of Isaac’s life was a one hundred and eighty years. 
Gen 35:29 Isaac beathed his last, and was gathered to his father’s kin, old and satisfied with life; and Esau and Jacob his sons buried him.  ¶ 
Gen 36:1 Now these are the descendants of Esau (that is, Edom). 
Gen 36:2 Esau took his wives from the Canaanites: Adah the daughter of Elon the Hittite, and Oholibamah the daughter of Anah, the daughter of Zibeon the Hivite, 
Gen 36:3 and Basemath Ishmael’s daughter, sister of Nebaioth. 
Gen 36:4 Adah bore Eliphaz to Esau; and Basemath bore Reuel; 
Gen 36:5 and Oholibamah bore Jeush, and Jalam, and Korah. These were the sons of Esau that were born to him in the land of Canaan.  ¶ 
Gen 36:6 Esau took his wives, and his sons, and his daughters, and all the members of his household and his cattle and all his beasts and all his possessionse which he had gathered in the land of Canaan and went into a land away from his brother Jacob. 
Gen 36:7 For their possessions were too many for them to live together; and the land where they sojourned could not support them because of their cattle. 
Gen 36:8 So Esau dwelt in Mount Seir (Esau is Edom).  ¶ 
Gen 36:9 These are the descendants of Esau the father of the Edomites in Mount Seir: 
Gen 36:10 these are the names of Esau’s sons: Eliphaz the son of Esau’s wife Adah, Reuel the son of Esau’s wife Basemath. 
Gen 36:11 The sons of Eliphaz were Teman, Omar, Zepho, and Gatam, and Kenaz. 
Gen 36:12 Timna was the concubine of Esau’s son Eliphaz; and she bore Amalek to him. These are the sons of Esau’s wife Adah. 
Gen 36:13 These are the sons of Reuel: Nahath, and Zerah, Shammah, and Mizzah. These were the sons of Basemath, Esau’s wife. 
Gen 36:14 These were the sons of Oholibamah the daughter of Anah, the daughter of Esau’s wife Zibeon she bore Jeush to Esau, and Jalam, and Korah.  ¶ 
Gen 36:15 These are the chiefs descended from Esau. The sons of Eliphaz the firstborn of Esau: chief Teman, chief Omar, chief Zepho, chief Kenaz, 
Gen 36:16 chief Korah, chief Gatam, chief Amalek. These are the chiefs descended from Eliphaz in the land of Edom. These are the sons of Adah. 
Gen 36:17 These are the sons of Reuel, Esau’s son: chief Nahath, chief Zerah, chief Shammah, chief Mizzah. These are the chiefs descended from Reuel in the land of Edom. These are the sons of Basemath, Esau’s wife. 
Gen 36:18 These are the sons of Oholibamah, Esau’s wife: chief Jeush, chief Jalam, chief Korah. These are the chiefs that came of Oholibamah the daughter of Anah, Esau’s wife. 
Gen 36:19 These are the sons of Esau (that is, Edom), and these are their chiefs.  ¶ 
Gen 36:20 These are the sons of Seir the Horite, the original inhabitants of the land: Lotan and Shobal and Zibeon and Anah, 
Gen 36:21 and Dishon and Ezer and Dishan. These are the chiefs that came of the Horites, the children of Seir in the land of Edom. 
Gen 36:22 The sons of Lotan were Hori and Heman. Lotan’s sister was Timna. 
Gen 36:23 These are the sons of Shobal: Alvan and Manahath and Ebal, Shepho and Onam. 
Gen 36:24 These are the sons of Zibeon: Aiah and Anah; this is Anah who found the hot springs in the wilderness, as he fed the donkeys of his father Zibeon. 
Gen 36:25 These are the children of Anah: Dishon and Oholibamah the daughter of Anah. 
Gen 36:26 These are the children of Dishon: Hemdan and Eshban and Ithran and Cheran. 
Gen 36:27 These are the children of Ezer: Bilhan and Zaavan and Akan. 
Gen 36:28 These are the children of Dishan: Uz and Aran. 
Gen 36:29 These are the chiefs descended from the Horites: chief Lotan, chief Shobal, chief Zibeon, chief Anah, 
Gen 36:30 chief Dishon, chief Ezer, chief Dishan. These are the chiefs that came of the Horites, according to their chiefs in the land of Seir.  ¶ 
Gen 36:31 These are the kings that reigned in the land of Edom, before there reigned any king over the Israelites. 
Gen 36:32 Bela the son of Beor reigned in Edom; and the name of his city was Dinhabah. 
Gen 36:33 Bela died, and Jobab the son of Zerah of Bozrah reigned in his stead. 
Gen 36:34 Jobab died, and Husham of the land of the Temanites reigned in his stead. 
Gen 36:35 Husham died, and Hadad the son of Bedad, who defeated Midian in the field of Moab, reigned in his stead. The name of his city was Avith. 
Gen 36:36 Hadad died, and Samlah of Masrekah reigned in his stead. 
Gen 36:37 Samlah died, and Shaul of Rehoboth by the River reigned in his stead. 
Gen 36:38 Shaul died, and Baal-hanan the son of Achbor reigned in his stead. 
Gen 36:39 Baal-hanan the son of Achbor died, and Hadar reigned in his stead: and the name of his city was Pau; and his wife’s name was Mehetabel, the daughter of Matred, the daughter of Me-zahab.  ¶ 
Gen 36:40 These are the names of the chiefs decended from Esau, according to their families, after their places, by their names: chief Timna, chief Alvah, chief Jetheth, 
Gen 36:41 chief Oholibamah, chief Elah, chief Pinon, 
Gen 36:42 chief Kenaz, chief Teman, chief Mibzar, 
Gen 36:43 chief Magdiel, chief Iram. These are the chiefs of Edom, according to their settlements in the land they possessed. This was Esau, the father of the Edomites.  ¶ 
Gen 37:1 Jacob made his home in the land of Canaan, where his father had lived as a resident foreigner. 
Gen 37:2 Joseph at the age of seventeen was a shepherd with his brothers, the sons of Bilhah and the sons of Zilpah, his father’s slave wives. He brought a bad report about them to their father. 
Gen 37:3 Now Jacob loved his son Joseph, who was born in his old age; and he made him a long robe with sleeves. 
Gen 37:4 When his brothers saw that their father loved Joseph more than all his other sons, they hated him and could not speak to him in a friendly manner.  ¶ 
Gen 37:5 Joseph also had a dream and told it to his brothers, and they hated him still more. 
Gen 37:6 This is what he said to them, ‘Hear, if you will, this dream which I have had; 
Gen 37:7 for as we were binding sheaves in the field, my sheaf rose up and remained standing, while your sheaves came round and bowed down to my sheaf.’ 
Gen 37:8 His brothers said to him, ‘Do you think you will be king over us? And rule us?’ So they hated him still more because of his dreams and his words.  ¶ 
Gen 37:9 Then he had another dream and told it to his brothers, saying, ‘I have had another dream, and it seemed to me that the sun and the moon and eleven stars bowed down to me.’ 
Gen 37:10 But when he told it to his father and his brothers, his father reproved him and said, ‘What is this dream that you have dreamed? Am I and your mother and your brothers supposed to bow down to the earth before you?’ 
Gen 37:11 Therefore his brothers envied him; but his father kept the matter in mind.  ¶ 
Gen 37:12 When his brothers went to pasture his father’s flocks in Shechem, 
Gen 37:13 Israel said to Joseph, ‘Are not your brothers pasturing the flocks in Shechem? Come now, I will send you to them.’ Joseph replied, ‘I am ready.’ 
Gen 37:14 So his father said to him, ‘Go, see whether all goes well with your brothers and with the flock, and bring me back word.’ So he sent him out from the valley of Hebron, and he came to Shechem. 
Gen 37:15 There a man found him, as he was wandering in the field, and the man asked him, ‘What are you seeking?’ 
Gen 37:16 He said, ‘I am looking for my brothers; tell me, please, where they are pasturing the flock.’ 
Gen 37:17 The man said, ‘They have gone away, for I heard them say, “Let us go to Dothan.”’ So Joseph went after his brothers and found them in Dothan.  ¶ 
Gen 37:18 When they saw him in the distance, before he came to them, they conspired against him to kill him. 
Gen 37:19 They said one to another, ‘See, here comes that master-dreamer. 
Gen 37:20 Come on, let us kill him, and throw him into one of the pits, and then we will say, “A fierce beast has devoured him”; and we shall see what will become of his dreams!’ 
Gen 37:21 Rueben, however, when he heard it, saved him from their hands by saying, ‘Let us not take his life.’ 
Gen 37:22 Reuben also said to them, ‘Do not shed blood; throw him into this pit, that is in the wilderness; but do not harm him,’ He planned to save him from their hands in order to restore him to his father. 
Gen 37:23 Nevertheless, when Joseph came to his brothers, they stripped him of his long robe, the robe with sleeves; 
Gen 37:24 and they took him and threw him into the pit. But the pit was empty, there being no water in it.  ¶ 
Gen 37:25 Then they sat down to eat bread, and when they looked up they saw a caravan of Ishmaelites coming from Gilead, and their camels were loaded with spices, balm and myrrh on their way to carry it down to Egypt. 
Gen 37:26 Judah said to his brothers, ‘What do we gain if we kill our brother and conceal his blood? 
Gen 37:27 Come, let us sell him to the Ishmaelites, and let us do him no violence, for he is our brother, our own flesh and blood.’ So his brothers listened to him; 
Gen 37:28 and when the Midianite merchants passed by, pulled Joseph up from the pit and sold him for twenty pieces of silver to the Ishmaelites, who brought him to Egypt.  ¶ 
Gen 37:29 When Reuben returned to the pit and found Joseph gone, he tore his clothes in sorrow. 
Gen 37:30 He went back to his brothers and said, ‘The boy is gone! What am I going to do?’  ¶ 
Gen 37:31 Then his brothers took Joseph’s robe, killed a he-goat, dipped the long-sleeved robe in the blood, 
Gen 37:32 tore it and sent it to their father, saying, ‘We found this; see whether it is your son’s robe or not.’ 
Gen 37:33 He recognised it and said, ‘It is my son’s robe! A wild beast has devoured him! Joseph without doubt is torn in pieces.’ 
Gen 37:34 Then Jacob tore his clothes, put sackcloth about his waist, and mourned for his son many days. 
Gen 37:35 All his sons and his daughters tried to comfort him, but he refused to be comforted, saying, ‘I shall go down to the grave mourning for my son.’ So Joseph’s father wept for him.  ¶ 
Gen 37:36 Meanwhile, the Midianites had sold Joseph in Egypt to one of Pharaoh’s court officials, Potiphar, the captain of the guard.  ¶ 
Gen 38:1 About that time Judah left his kinsmen, and settled near a certain Adullamite, whose name was Hirah. 
Gen 38:2 Judah saw there a daughter of a Canaanite whose name was Shua, and he married her. He lay with her, 
Gen 38:3 and she conceived, and bore a son, and he named him Er. 
Gen 38:4 Then she conceived again, and bore a son and named him Onan. 
Gen 38:5 She bore still another son, and named him Shelah: and it was at Chezib that she bore him.  ¶ 
Gen 38:6 Now Judah found a wife for Er his eldest son, and her name was Tamar. 
Gen 38:7 But Er, Judah’s eldest son, was wicked in the sight of the  <c>Lord</c>, and the  <c>Lord</c> took his life. 
Gen 38:8 Then Judah said to Onan, ‘Go and lie with your brother’s wife, and perform the duty of a husband’s brother to her, and raise up offspring for your brother.’ 
Gen 38:9 But Onan knew that the child would not be his; so whenever he lay with his brother’s wife, he spilled his semen on the ground, in order not to raise up offspring for his brother. 
Gen 38:10 What he did was evil in the sight of the  <c>Lord</c>: therefore he took his life also.  ¶ 
Gen 38:11 Then said Judah to Tamar his daughter-in-law, ‘Remain a widow in your father’s house, until Shelah my son is grown up’; for he said to himself, ‘I will not let him marry her, he must not die like his brothers.’ So Tamar went and lived in her father’s house.  ¶ 
Gen 38:12 After many days had passed, Shua’s daughter, the wife of Judah, died. When Judah had finished mourning, he went up to see about his sheep-shearers at Timnah, with his friend Hirah the Adullamite. 
Gen 38:13 Someone told Tamar, saying, ‘Behold, your father-in-law is going up to Timnah to shear his sheep.’ 
Gen 38:14 She took off the garments of her widowhood, and covered herself with her veil. She sat, veiled, in the gate of Enaim, which is by the way to Timnah; for she saw that Shelah had grown up without her being given to him as wife. 
Gen 38:15 When Judah saw her, he thought her to be a prostitute; because she had veiled her face. 
Gen 38:16 So he turned aside to her by the roadside, and said, ‘Permit me, I pray you, to lie with you.’ For he did not know that she was his daughter-in-law. And she said, ‘What will you give me to lie with me?’ 
Gen 38:17 He said, ‘I will send you a young goat from the flock.’ She said, ‘Will you give me a pledge, until you send it?’ 
Gen 38:18 He said, ‘What pledge should I give you?’ And she said, ‘Your seal-ring and your chain and your staff that is in your hand.’ So he gave them to her, and lay with her, and she became pregnant. 
Gen 38:19 And she got up, and went away, and took off her veil, and put on the garments of her widowhood.  ¶ 
Gen 38:20 Now when Judah sent the young goat by the hand of his friend the Adullamite, to receive the pledge from the woman’s hand, he could not find her. 
Gen 38:21 He asked the men of her place, saying, ‘Where is the sacred prostitute, who was at Enaim by the wayside?’ They replied, ‘There has been no sacred prostitute here.’ 
Gen 38:22 So he returned to Judah, and said, ‘I have not found her; and the men of the place said, “There has been no sacred prostitute here.”’ 
Gen 38:23 Judah said, ‘Let her keep the pledge, otherwise we will be put to shame. I have sent this goat, and you have not found her.’  ¶ 
Gen 38:24 Now after about three months, Judah was told, ‘Tamar your daughter-in-law has been acting like a whore and is pregnant.’ Judah said, ‘Bring her forth and let her be burnt.’ 
Gen 38:25 But when she was brought forth, she sent to her father-in-law, saying, ‘By the man to whom these things belong, I am with child.’ She also said, ‘Look at them and see if you know whose these are, the seal-ring and the chain and the staff.’ 
Gen 38:26 When Judah recognised them, he said, ‘She is more in the right than I, because I did not give her to Shelah my son.’ But he did not lie with her again.  ¶ 
Gen 38:27 When her time came to give birth, it was found that twins were in her womb. 
Gen 38:28 While she was in labour, one put out a hand and the midwife took and bound on his hand a bright red thread, saying, ‘This one came out first.’ 
Gen 38:29 But he drew back his hand, and his brother came out, and she said, ‘What a breach you have made for yourself!’ Therefore he was named Perez <sup>[ Breach ]</sup>. 
Gen 38:30 Afterward his brother came out, who had the bright red thread on his hand; therefore he was named Zerah <sup>[ Red ]</sup>.  ¶ 
Gen 39:1 Joseph was taken down to Egypt, and Potiphar, one of Pharaoh’s officers, the captain of the guard, an Egyptian, bought him from the Ishmaelites who had taken him there.  ¶ 
Gen 39:2 Now the  <c>Lord</c> was with Joseph, so that he prospered; and he remained in the house of his master the Egyptian. 
Gen 39:3 When his master saw that the  <c>Lord</c> was with him and made everything that he undertook prosper, 
Gen 39:4 Joseph won his confidence and became his personal attendant. He also made him overseer of his household and placed all that he had in his care. 
Gen 39:5 From the time that he made him overseer in his house and over all that he had, the  <c>Lord</c> blessed the Egyptian’s household for Joseph’s sake, and the blessing of the  <c>Lord</c> was upon all that he had in the house and in the field. 
Gen 39:6 Leaving all that he had in Joseph’s charge, he knew nothing about his affairs except about the food which he ate. Also Joseph was handsome and attractive.  ¶ 
Gen 39:7 After these honors had come to Joseph, his master’s wife directed her glances toward him and tried to tempt him. 
Gen 39:8 But he refused, saying to her, ‘See, my master knows nothing about what I do in the house, and he has put all that he has in my charge. 
Gen 39:9 No one has greater authority in this house than I, and he has kept back nothing from me but you, because you are his wife. How then can I do this great wrong and sin against God?’ 
Gen 39:10 Day after day she tempted Joseph, but he did not listen to her nor accept her advances. 
Gen 39:11 One day, however, when he went into the house to do his work and when none of the men of the household were at home, 
Gen 39:12 she caught hold of his garment and tried to seduce him; but he left his garment in her hand and fled out of the house.  ¶ 
Gen 39:13 When she saw that he had left his garment in her hand and had fled, 
Gen 39:14 she called to her household servants and said to them, ‘See, the master has brought a Hebrew in to insult us. He came to me to rape me, and I screamed loudly; 
Gen 39:15 and when he heard me scream, he left his garment with me and ran out of the house.’ 
Gen 39:16 She kept his garment by her until his master came home; 
Gen 39:17 then she told him the same story, saying, ‘The Hebrew slave whom you have brought to us came to me to insult me; 
Gen 39:18 and when I screamed he left his garment with me and fled.’  ¶ 
Gen 39:19 When Joseph’s master heard the statements which his wife made to him, his anger was aroused; 
Gen 39:20 and he took Joseph and put him into the prison, in the place where the king’s prisoners were confined. So he was left there in prison. 
Gen 39:21 But the  <c>Lord</c> was with Joseph and showed kindness to him and enabled him to win the favour of the keeper of the prison, 
Gen 39:22 so that he placed all the prisoners in Joseph’s charge and made him responsible for whatever they did there. 
Gen 39:23 The keeper did not have to concern himself about anything Joseph was responsible for, because the  <c>Lord</c> was with him and gave him success in everything he did.  ¶ 
Gen 40:1 Some time after these things the cupbearer of the king of Egypt and his baker offended their master the king of Egypt, 
Gen 40:2 so that Pharaoh was angry with these two officers and imprisoned them in the house of the captain of the guard, in the same prison where Joseph was confined. 
Gen 40:3 The captain of the guard assigned Joseph to them, and he waited on them; 
Gen 40:4 and they remained in confinement for some time.  ¶ 
Gen 40:5 Meanwhile the king of Egypt’s cupbearer and baker, who were confined in the prison, both had dreams the same night, each with a particular meaning. 
Gen 40:6 When Joseph came in to them in the morning, he saw plainly that they were sad. 
Gen 40:7 So he asked Pharaoh’s officers, ‘Why do you look so sad today?’ 
Gen 40:8 They answered. ‘We have had a dream and there is no one who can interpret it.’ Then Joseph said to them, ‘Do not the interpretations of dreams belong to God? Tell them to me.’  ¶ 
Gen 40:9 Then the chief cupbearer told his dream to Joseph and said to him, ‘In my dream I saw a vine before me, 
Gen 40:10 and on the vine were three branches, and as if budding it put out blossoms and its clusters brought forth ripe grapes. 
Gen 40:11 Pharaoh’s cup was in my hand, and I took the grapes and pressed them into his cup and gave the cup to Pharaoh.’  ¶ 
Gen 40:12 Then Joseph said to him, ‘This is its interpretation: the three branches are three days; 
Gen 40:13 within three days Pharaoh will release you from prison and restore you to your office, and you will give Pharaoh’s cup into his hand as you used to do when you were his cupbearer. 
Gen 40:14 But when all goes well with you, remember me, show kindness to me and speak in my behalf to Pharaoh and bring me out of this house; 
Gen 40:15 for I was unjustly stolen from the land of the Hebrews, and here also I have done nothing that they should put me in the dungeon.’  ¶ 
Gen 40:16 When the chief baker saw that the interpretation was favorable, he said to Joseph, ‘I also saw something in my dream: there were three baskets of white bread on my head, 
Gen 40:17 and in the uppermost basket there were all kinds of baked food for Pharaoh, and the birds were eating them out of the basket on my head.’ 
Gen 40:18 Joseph answered, ‘This is its interpretation: the three baskets are three days; 
Gen 40:19 within three days Pharaoh will take off your head and hang you on a tree, and the birds shall eat your flesh.’  ¶ 
Gen 40:20 Now on the third day, which was Pharaoh’s birthday, he made a feast for all his officials. Then he released the chief cupbearer and the chief baker. 
Gen 40:21 He restored the chief butler to his office, so that he again gave the cup into Pharaoh’s hand, 
Gen 40:22 but the chief baker he hanged, as Joseph had interpreted to them. 
Gen 40:23 Yet the chief cupbearer did not remember Joseph, but forgot him.  ¶ 
Gen 41:1 Two years later Pharaoh had a dream: as he stood by the Nile, 
Gen 41:2 he saw coming up from the Nile seven cows, good-looking and fat, and they had been feeding in the river grass. 
Gen 41:3 Then seven other cows came up after them out of the Nile, bad-looking and lean, and they stood by the other cows on the bank of the Nile. 
Gen 41:4 The bad-looking cows ate up the seven good-looking, fat cows. Then Pharaoh awoke.  ¶ 
Gen 41:5 Afterward he slept and had a second dream and saw seven ears, plump and good, growing up on one stalk. 
Gen 41:6 Also seven ears, thin and blasted by the east wind, sprang up after them. 
Gen 41:7 The thin ears swallowed up the seven plump, full ears. Then Pharaoh awoke, and realised that it was a dream.  ¶ 
Gen 41:8 In the morning Pharaoh’s mind was disturbed; so he sent and called all the magicians and wise men of Egypt and told them his dreams, but no one could interpret them to him.  ¶ 
Gen 41:9 Then the chief cupbearer said to Pharaoh, ‘I now must remind you of my offenses: 
Gen 41:10 Pharaoh was very angry with his servants and imprisoned me and the chief baker in the house of the captain of the guard. 
Gen 41:11 We both had dreams the same night, each with a special meaning. 
Gen 41:12 There was also with us a young Hebrew, a slave of the captain of the guard; and we told him and he interpreted our dreams to us, to each of us according to his dream. 
Gen 41:13 Our dreams came true exactly as he interpreted them to us: I was restored to my office, but the other man was hanged.’  ¶ 
Gen 41:14 Then Pharaoh sent for Joseph, and they brought him hastily out of the dungeon; and he shaved his face and changed his clothes and came to Pharaoh.
