Ruth 3:9 ‘Who are you?’ he said. ‘I am Ruth your servant,’ she answered, ‘Spread your cloak over your servant, for you are a near relative.’ 
Ruth 3:10 He said, ‘May you be blest by the  <c>Lord</c>, my daughter. You have shown me greater favour now than at first, for you have not followed young men, whether poor or rich. 
Ruth 3:11 My daughter, have no fear. I will do for you all that you ask, for the whole town knows that you are a virtuous woman. 
Ruth 3:12 Now it is true that I am a near relative, but there is another man nearer than I. 
Ruth 3:13 Stay here tonight, and then in the morning, if he will perform for you the duty of a kinsman, well, let him do it. But if he will not perform for you the duty of a kinsman, then as surely as the  <c>Lord</c> lives, I will do it for you. Lie down until morning.’  ¶ 
Ruth 3:14 So she lay at his feet until morning, but rose before anyone could recognise her, for Boaz said, ‘No one must know that a woman came to the threshing-floor.’ 
Ruth 3:15 He also said, ‘Bring the cloak which you have on and hold it.’ So she held it while he poured into it six measures of barley and laid it on her shoulders. Then he went into the city.  ¶ 
Ruth 3:16 When Ruth came to her mother-in-law, Naomi asked, ‘Is it you, my daughter?’ Then Ruth told Naomi all that the man had done for her. 
Ruth 3:17 ‘He gave me these six measures of barley,’ she said, ‘for he said I should not go to my mother-in-law empty-handed.’  ¶ 
Ruth 3:18 ‘Wait quietly, my daughter.’ Naomi said, ‘Until you know how the affair will turn out, for the man will not rest unless he settles it all today.’  ¶ 
Ruth 4:1 Then Boaz went up to the gate and sat down. Just then the near kinsman of whom Boaz had spoken came along. Boaz said, ‘Hello, So-and-so (calling him by name), come here and sit down.’ So he stopped and sat down. 
Ruth 4:2 Boaz also took ten of the town elders and said, ‘Sit down here.’ So they sat down.  ¶ 
Ruth 4:3 Then he said to the near relative, ‘Naomi, who has come back from the country of Moab, is offering for sale the piece of land which belonged to our relative Elimelech, 
Ruth 4:4 and I thought that I would lay the matter before you, suggesting that you buy it in the presence of these men who sit here and of the elders of my people. If you will buy it and so keep it in the possession of the family, do so; but if not; then tell me, so that I may know; for no one but you has the right to buy it, and I am next to you.’  ¶ ‘I will buy it,’ he said.  ¶ 
Ruth 4:5 Then Boaz said, ‘On the day you buy the field from Naomi, you must also marry Ruth the Moabite, the widow of the dead, in order to preserve the name of the dead in connection with his inheritance.’  ¶ 
Ruth 4:6 ‘I cannot buy it for myself without spoiling my own inheritance,’ the near relative said. ‘You take my right of buying it as a relative, because I cannot do so.’  ¶ 
Ruth 4:7 Now this used to be the custom in Israel: to make valid anything relating to a matter of redemption or exchange, a man drew off his sandal and gave it to the other man; and this was the way contracts were attested in Israel. 
Ruth 4:8 So when the near relative said to Boaz, ‘Buy it for yourself,’ Boaz drew off the man’s sandal.  ¶ 
Ruth 4:9 Then Boaz said to the elders and to all the people, ‘You are witnesses at this time that I have bought all that was Elimelech’s and all that was Chilion’s and Mahlon’s from Naomi. 
Ruth 4:10 Moreover I have secured Ruth the Moabite, the wife of Mahlon, to be my wife, in order to perpetuate the name of the dead in connection with his inheritance, so that his name will not disappear from among his relatives and from the household where he lived. You are witnesses this day.’  ¶ 
Ruth 4:11 Then all the people who were at the gate and the elders said, ‘We are witnesses. May the  <c>Lord</c> make the woman who is coming into your house like Rachel and Leah, who together built the house of Israel. May you do well in Ephrata, and become famous in Bethlehem. 
Ruth 4:12 From the children whom the  <c>Lord</c> will give you by this young woman may your household become like the household of Perez, whom Tamar bore to Judah.’  ¶ 
Ruth 4:13 So Boaz married Ruth, and she became his wife; and the  <c>Lord</c> gave to her a son. 
Ruth 4:14 Then the women said to Naomi, ‘Blessed be the  <c>Lord</c> who has not left you at this time without a near relative, and may his name be famous in Israel. 
Ruth 4:15 This child will restore your vigor and nourish you in your old age; for your daughter-in-law who loves you, who is worth more to you than seven sons, has borne a son to Boaz!’  ¶ 
Ruth 4:16 So Naomi took the child in her arms and cared for him as if he was her own. 
Ruth 4:17 The women of the neighbourhood gave him a name, saying, ‘A son is born to Naomi!’ They named him Obed. He became the father of Jesse, who was the father of David.  ¶ 
Ruth 4:18 This is the genealogy of Perez: <br>	Perez was the father of Hezron, <br>	
Ruth 4:19 Hezron of Ram, <br>	Ram of Amminadab, <br>	
Ruth 4:20 Amminidab of Nashon, <br>	Nashon of Salmon, <br>	
Ruth 4:21 Salmon of Boaz, <br>	Boaz of Obed, <br>	
Ruth 4:22 Obed of Jesse, <br>	Jesse of David.  ¶ 
1Sam 1:1 Now there was a certain man of Ramah, a Zuphite of the hill country of Ephraim, and his name was Elkanah the son of Jeroham, the son of Elihu, the son of Tohu, the son of Zuph, an Ephraimite. 
1Sam 1:2 He had two wives: the name of the one was Hannah, and the name of the other Peninnah. Peninnah had children, but Hannah had none. 
1Sam 1:3 This man used to go up from his city year by year to worship and to sacrifice to the  <c>Lord</c> of armies in Shiloh. Eli and his two sons, Hophni and Phinehas, were priests to the  <c>Lord</c> there. 
1Sam 1:4 It came to pass on one occasion that Elkanah sacrificed. Now he used to give portions to Peninnah his wife and to all her sons and daughters, 
1Sam 1:5 but to Hannah he used to give a double portion because he loved her. But the  <c>Lord</c> had shut up her womb. 
1Sam 1:6 Her rival used to vex her bitterly in order to make her angry, because the  <c>Lord</c> had shut up her womb. 
1Sam 1:7 This happened year after year, as often as she went up to the house of the  <c>Lord</c>, she used to vex her; therefore she wept and would not eat. 
1Sam 1:8 But Elkanah her husband said to her, ‘Hannah, why do you weep and not eat, and why is your heart sad? Am not I better to you than ten sons?’  ¶ 
1Sam 1:9 So Hannah rose up, after they had eaten in Shiloh, and stood before the  <c>Lord</c>. Now Eli the priest was sitting at his seat at the door-posts of the temple of the  <c>Lord</c>. 
1Sam 1:10 She was greatly distressed and prayed fervently to the  <c>Lord</c> and wept bitterly. 
1Sam 1:11 She vowed a vow, saying, <br>	‘O  <c>Lord</c> of armies! <br>	If you will indeed look on the affliction of your maid-servant, <br>	remember me and not forget your maid-servant, <br>	but will give to your maid-servant a boy <br>	then I will give him to the  <c>Lord</c> all the days of his life. <br>	A razor will not come upon his head.’ <br> ¶ 
1Sam 1:12 While she continued praying before the  <c>Lord</c>, Eli observed her mouth. 
1Sam 1:13 Now Hannah was speaking to herself. Only her lips moved, but her voice was not heard; therefore Eli took her for a drunken woman. 
1Sam 1:14 So Eli said to her, ‘How long will you act like a drunken woman? Put away the effects of your wine and go from the presence of the  <c>Lord</c>.’  ¶ 
1Sam 1:15 ‘No, my lord,’ Hannah answered, ‘I am an unfortunate woman! I have drunk neither wine nor intoxicating drink, but I have been pouring out my heart before the  <c>Lord</c>. 
1Sam 1:16 Do not take your maid-servant to be a vile woman, for because of the greatness of my grief and vexation have I continued speaking until now.’  ¶ 
1Sam 1:17 Then Eli answered, ‘Go in peace, and the God of Israel grant your petition that you have asked of him.’  ¶ 
1Sam 1:18 She said, ‘Let your maid-servant find favour in your sight.’ So the woman went her way and ate, and her countenance was no more sad.  ¶ 
1Sam 1:19 They rose up in the morning early, and worshipped before the  <c>Lord</c>, and returned and came to their house at Ramah. And Elkanah knew Hannah his wife; and the  <c>Lord</c> remembered her.  ¶ 
1Sam 1:20 And Hannah conceived, and it came to pass at the coming around of the new year that she bore a son, and named him Samuel <sup>[    Heb: Asked of God ]</sup>, saying, ‘For I have asked him of the  <c>Lord</c>.’  ¶ 
1Sam 1:21 The man Elkanah and all his household went up to offer to the  <c>Lord</c> the yearly sacrifice and his vow. 
1Sam 1:22 But Hannah did not go up; for she said to her husband, ‘When the child is weaned then I will bring him and he will appear in the presence of the  <c>Lord</c> and will live there forever.’  ¶ 
1Sam 1:23 Elkanah her husband said to her, ‘Do what seems good to you: wait until you have weaned him; only may the  <c>Lord</c> establish your word.’  ¶ So the woman waited and nursed her son until she weaned him. 
1Sam 1:24 When she had weaned him, she took him up with her, together with a three-year-old bullock and a bushel of flour and a skin of wine, and brought him to the house of the  <c>Lord</c> in Shiloh. 
1Sam 1:25 They slew the bullock and Hannah brought the lad to Eli. 
1Sam 1:26 She said, ‘Oh, sir, by your life, I am the woman who stood near you here, praying fervently to the  <c>Lord</c>. 
1Sam 1:27 This is the lad regarding whom I was fervently praying, and the  <c>Lord</c> has granted me my petition which I asked of him. 
1Sam 1:28 Now, I on my part have given him to the  <c>Lord</c>; as long as he lives he is given to the  <c>Lord</c>.’ So she left him there before the  <c>Lord</c>.  ¶ 
1Sam 2:1 And Hannah prayed: <br>	My heart exults in the  <c>Lord</c>, <br>	my strength is exalted in the  <c>Lord</c>; <br>	my mouth laughs at my enemies; <br>	because I rejoice in your salvation. <br><br>	
1Sam 2:2 There is none holy as the  <c>Lord</c>, <br>	there is none like you; <br>	there is no rock like our God. <br><br>	
1Sam 2:3 Do not talk so proudly, <br>	let not arrogance come out of your mouth, <br>	for the  <c>Lord</c> is a God of knowledge, <br>	and by him actions are weighed. <br><br>	
1Sam 2:4 The bows of the mighty men are broken, <br>	and they that stumbled are girded with strength. <br>	
1Sam 2:5 They that were full have hired out themselves for bread, <br>	and they that were hungry have ceased; <br>	while the barren has borne seven, <br>	she who had many children has languished. <br><br>	
1Sam 2:6 The  <c>Lord</c> kills, and makes alive; <br>	he brings down to the grave, and brings up. <br>	
1Sam 2:7 The  <c>Lord</c> makes poor, and makes rich; <br>	he brings low, he also lifts up. <br>	
1Sam 2:8 He raises up the poor out of the dust, <br>	he lifts up the needy from the garbage heap <br>	to make them sit with princes, <br>	and inherit the throne of glory. <br>	For the pillars of the earth are the  <c>Lord</c>”S, <br>	and he has set the world upon them. <br><br>	
1Sam 2:9 He will guard the feet of his holy ones, <br>	but the wicked will be put to silence in darkness; <br>	for not by strength will humans prevail. <br>	
1Sam 2:10 They who strive with the  <c>Lord</c> will be broken to pieces; <br>	against them will he thunder in heaven. <br>	The  <c>Lord</c> will judge the ends of the earth, <br>	he will give strength to his king <br>	and exalt the power of his anointed.  ¶ 
1Sam 2:11 So Elkanah went to Ramah. But the lad was ministering to the  <c>Lord</c> in the presence of Eli the priest. 
1Sam 2:12 Now the sons of Eli were base scoundrels; they had no regard for the  <c>Lord</c>, 
1Sam 2:13 nor for what was justly due to the priest from the people. Whenever a man offered a sacrifice, the priest’s servant would come, while the meat was boiling, with a three-pronged fork in his hand, 
1Sam 2:14 and would strike into the pot or the kettle or the basin or the dish. All that the fork brought up the priest would take for himself. So they did to all the Israelites who came to sacrifice to the  <c>Lord</c> in Shiloh. 
1Sam 2:15 Moreover before they burned the fat, the priest’s servant used to come and say to the man who was making the offering, ‘Give me meat to roast for the priest; for he will not take from you boiled flesh, but raw.’ 
1Sam 2:16 Should the man, however, say to him, ‘First you should burn the fat, then take as much as you desire,’ he would reply, ‘No, you must give it at once or else I will take it by force.’ 
1Sam 2:17 The sin of the young men was very great before the  <c>Lord</c>, for the men had contempt for the offering of the  <c>Lord</c>. 
1Sam 2:18 And Samuel continued ministering before the  <c>Lord</c> – a lad girded with a linen ephod. 
1Sam 2:19 His mother used to make him a little robe and bring it to him from year to year, when she came up with her husband to offer the yearly sacrifice. 
1Sam 2:20 And Eli would bless Elkanah and his wife and say, ‘The  <c>Lord</c> repay you with offspring from this woman for the gift which she gave to the  <c>Lord</c>.’ Then they would return to their own home. 
1Sam 2:21 And the  <c>Lord</c> visited Hannah so that she conceived and bore three sons and two daughters. The child Samuel grew up before the  <c>Lord</c>.  ¶ 
1Sam 2:22 Now Eli was very old; and whenver he heard what his sons were doing to all Israel, how they lay with the women who did service at the door of the tent of meeting, 
1Sam 2:23 he said to them, ‘Why do you do such things as these, which I hear from the mouth of all the people. 
1Sam 2:24 No, my sons; for it is no good report that I hear the people of the  <c>Lord</c> spreading abroad. 
1Sam 2:25 If one man sin against another, God will mediate for him; but if a man sin against the  <c>Lord</c>, who could act as mediator for him?’ Notwithstanding they did not listen to the voice of their father, because the  <c>Lord</c> desired to slay them. 
1Sam 2:26 But the lad Samuel kept on growing larger and better in the estimation both of the  <c>Lord</c> and of men.  ¶ 
1Sam 2:27 There came a man of God to Eli and said to him, ‘This is the  <c>Lord</c>’s message: I revealed myself to your father’s house, when they were in Egypt servants to Pharaoh’s house, 
1Sam 2:28 and I chose him from all the tribes of Israel to be my priest to go up to my altar to burn sacrifices, to bear an ephod before me, and I gave to your father’s house for food all the offerings of the Israelites made by fire. 
1Sam 2:29 Why do you look with envious eyes on my sacrifices and offerings, and honour your sons above me in fattening yourselves with the first-fruits of all the offerings which the Israelites bring me?” 
1Sam 2:30 Therefore the  <c>Lord</c> the God of Israel says, “I had indeed thought that your house and the house of your father would walk before me forever,” but now the  <c>Lord</c> says, “Far be it from me, for them who honour me I will honour, and they who despise me will be lightly esteemed. 
1Sam 2:31 The days are quickly coming when I Will cut off your arm and the arm of your father’s house. 
1Sam 2:32 You will look in affliction and enviously on all the prosperity which I will give Israel, and there will not be an old man in your house forever. 
1Sam 2:33 The only one of you whom I do not cut off from my altar will be spared to weep out his eyes and to wear out his body, and all of your household will die by the sword of men. 
1Sam 2:34 This will be the sign to you that will come upon your two sons, Hophni and Phinehas: on the same day both will die. 
1Sam 2:35 And I will raise up for myself a faithful priest who will do according to that which is in my heart and in my desire, and I will build him an enduring house, and he will walk before my anointed forever. 
1Sam 2:36 Anyone who is left in your house will come to do him obeisance for a piece of money or a loaf of bread, and will beg to be given in one of the priests’ offices so that they may eat a morsel of bread.”’  ¶ 
1Sam 3:1 The child Samuel continued ministering before the  <c>Lord</c> in the presence of Eli. The word of the  <c>Lord</c> was rare in those days; there were no frequent visions. 
1Sam 3:2 Once at that time, when Eli was lying in his Samuel place – his eyes had begun to grow dim, so that he could not see – 
1Sam 3:3 and while the lamp of God was still burning, and Samuel was lying in the temple of the  <c>Lord</c> where the ark of God was, 
1Sam 3:4 the  <c>Lord</c> called, ‘Samuel! Samuel!’ He said, ‘Here I am.’ 
1Sam 3:5 He ran to Eli, and said, ‘Here I am; you called me.’ But he said, ‘I didn’t call, lie down again.’ So he went and lay down. 
1Sam 3:6 Then the  <c>Lord</c> called yet again, ‘Samuel! Samuel!’ And Samuel arose and went to Eli and said, ‘Here I am; you called me.’ But he answered, ‘I didn’t call, my son. Lie down again.’ 
1Sam 3:7 Now Samuel did not yet know the  <c>Lord</c> neither had the word of the  <c>Lord</c> yet been revealed to him. 
1Sam 3:8 So when the  <c>Lord</c> called Samuel again the third time, he arose and went to Eli, and said, ‘Here I am; for you called me.’ Then Eli realized that the  <c>Lord</c> was calling the child. 
1Sam 3:9 So Eli said to Samuel, ‘Go, lie down; and if you are called, say, “Speak,  <c>Lord</c>, for your servant is listening.’” So Samuel went and lay down in his place. 
1Sam 3:10 Then the  <c>Lord</c> came, and stood there, and called as at other times, ‘Samuel! Samuel!’ And Samuel said, ‘Speak; for your servant is listening.’ 
1Sam 3:11 And the  <c>Lord</c> said to Samuel, ‘See, I am about to do such a thing in Israel, that the ears of everyone who hears it will ring. 
1Sam 3:12 In that day I will perform toward Eli all that I have spoken against his house from beginning to end. 
1Sam 3:13 For I have told him that I will judge his house forever, for the guilt which he knew, in that his sons were blaspheming God and he did not restrain them. 
1Sam 3:14 Therefore I have sworn to the house of Eli that the guilt of Eli’s house will not be expiated with sacrifice nor offering forever.’  ¶ 
1Sam 3:15 And Samuel lay there until the morning. Then he rose early in the morning and opened the doors of the house of the  <c>Lord</c>. Samuel was afraid to make the known the vision to Eli. 
1Sam 3:16 But Eli called Samuel and said, ‘Samuel, my son.’ He said, ‘I am here.’ 
1Sam 3:17 He said, ‘What is the thing that the  <c>Lord</c> has spoken to you? Hide nothing from me. May God do to you whatever he will, if you conceal from me a word of all that he spoke to you.’ 
1Sam 3:18 So Samuel told him everything; and hid nothing from him. And Eli said, ‘It is the  <c>Lord</c>; let him do what seems good to him.’  ¶ 
1Sam 3:19 And Samuel grew, and the  <c>Lord</c> was with him and let none of his words fall to the ground. 
1Sam 3:20 All Israel from Dan even to Beersheba knew that Samuel was established as a prophet of the  <c>Lord</c>. 
1Sam 3:21 And the  <c>Lord</c> again appeared in Shiloh, for the  <c>Lord</c> revealed himself to Samuel, 
1Sam 4:1 and the word of Samuel came to all Israel.  ¶ Now in those days the Philistines assembled to make war against Israel. Israel went out against the Philistines to battle, and encamped at Ebenezer; and the Philistines encamped in Aphek. 
1Sam 4:2 The Philistines put themselves in array against Israel, and Israel was smitten before the Philistines, and the battle was hard fought and they slew in the ranks on the field about four thousand men. 
1Sam 4:3 But when the people returned to the camp, the elders of Israel said, ‘Why has the  <c>Lord</c> smitten us today before the Philistines? Let us bring to us the ark of our God out of Shiloh, that it may come among us and save us from the hand of our enemies.’ 
1Sam 4:4 So they sent to Shiloh; and took from there the ark of the  <c>Lord</c> of armies who sits enthroned above the cherubim. The two sons of Eli, Hophni and Phinehas, were there with the ark of God. 
1Sam 4:5 When the ark of God the  <c>Lord</c> came to the camp, all Israel shouted such a great shout that the earth rang.  ¶ 
1Sam 4:6 When the Philistines heard the noise of the shout, they said, ‘What does this great shouting in the Hebrew’s camp mean?’ When they learned that the ark of the  <c>Lord</c> had come to the camp, 
1Sam 4:7 they were afraid, and said, ‘These are their gods. They have come to them to the camp. 
1Sam 4:8 Woe to Woe to us! Nothin like this has happened to us before! Who can deliver us out of the hand of these mighty gods? These are the gods who smote the Egyptians with every sort of plague and pesilence. 
1Sam 4:9 Be strong, and be men, O Philistines, so that you will not become slaves to the Hebrews, as they have been slaves to you.’  ¶ 
1Sam 4:10 So the Philistines fought and there was great slaughter. Israel was defeated and each fled to his home. There fell of Israel thirty thousand footmen. 
1Sam 4:11 The ark of God was taken, and the two sons of Eli, Hophni and Phinehas, perished.  ¶ 
1Sam 4:12 A Benjamite ran from the ranks and came to Shiloh the same day with his garments torn and with earth on his head. 
1Sam 4:13 Just as he came, Eli was sitting upon his seat beside the gate watching the road, for his heart was trembling for the ark of God. When the man came to the city to inform it, all the city cried out. 
1Sam 4:14 When Eli heard the noise of the crying he said, ‘What is this tumultuous noise?’ The man came quickly and told Eli. 
1Sam 4:15 (Now Eli was ninety-eight years old, and his eyes were set, so that he could not see). 
1Sam 4:16 The man said to Eli, ‘I have come from the battle, for I fled today from the ranks.’ He said, ‘How went the matter, my son?’ 
1Sam 4:17 He that brought the tidings answered, ‘Israel fled before the Philistines, and there was also a great slaughter among the people, and your two sons also, Hophni and Phinehas, are dead, and the ark of God has been captured.’ 
1Sam 4:18 When he mentioned the ark of God, Eli fell from his seat backward by the side of the gate; and his neck was broken and he died, for he was old and heavy. He had judged Israel forty years.  ¶ 
1Sam 4:19 His daughter-in-law, Phinehas’s wife, was pregnant and near her time. When she heard the report regarding the capture of the ark of God, and that her father-in-law and her husband were dead, she went into labor and crouched down and gave birth to a child. 
1Sam 4:20 As she lay dying, the women who stood by her said to her, ‘Do not fear, for you have given birth to a son.’ But she neither answered nor heeded. 
1Sam 4:21 She named the child Ichabod, saying, ‘The glory is taken away from Israel,’ meaning the capture of the ark of God, and the deaths of her father-in-law and her husband. 
1Sam 4:22 ‘Glory has left Israel,’ she said, ‘because the ark of God is taken.’  ¶ 
1Sam 5:1 The Philistines took the ark of God and brought it from Ebenezer to Ashdod. 
1Sam 5:2 Then the Philistines took the ark of the  <c>Lord</c> and brought it to the house of Dagon and set it up by the side of Dagon. 
1Sam 5:3 When the Ashdodites arose early the next day, there was Dagon fallen upon his face to the ground before the ark of the  <c>Lord</c>. They raised up Dagon and set him in his place again. 
1Sam 5:4 But when they arose early on the following morning, behold there was Dagon fallen upon his face to the ground before the ark of the  <c>Lord</c>. The head of Dagon and both his hands were cut off upon the threshold, and only the body of Dagon was left. 
1Sam 5:5 This is why the priests of Dagon and all who enter the house of Dagon do not tread on the threshold of Dagon in Ashdod to this day, but step over it. 
1Sam 5:6 The hand of the  <c>Lord</c> was heavy upon the Ashdodites, and he destroyed them, and struck them with tumors, both in Ashdod and its borders. 
1Sam 5:7 When the men of Ashdod saw that it was so, they said, ‘The ark of the God of Israel must not remain with us, for his hand is severe on us and on Dagon our god.’ 
1Sam 5:8 So they sent and gathered together all the lords of the Philistines, and said, ‘What should we do with the ark of the God of Israel?’ They answered, ‘Let the ark of the God of Israel be brought around to Gath.’ So they moved the ark of the God of Israel to Gath. 
1Sam 5:9 But after they had brought it to Gath, the hand of the  <c>Lord</c> was against the city – there was a very great panic – and he struck the men of the city, both young and old, so that tomors broke out on them. 
1Sam 5:10 So they sent the ark of God to Ekron. But when the ark of God came to Ekron, the Ekronites cried out, ‘They have brought around the ark of the God of Israel to us, to slay us and our people.’ 
1Sam 5:11 They sent therefore and gathered together all the lords of the Philistines and said, ‘Send away the ark of the God of Israel, let it go back to its own place and not kill us and our people.’ For a deadly panic had seized the entire city. The hand of God was very heavy there. 
1Sam 5:12 The men who did not die were stricken with the tumors, and the cry of lamentation from the city went up to heaven.  ¶ 
1Sam 6:1 The ark of the  <c>Lord</c> was in the country of the Philistines for seven months. 
1Sam 6:2 Then the Philistines summoned the priests and the diviners, and said, ‘What should we do with the ark of the  <c>Lord</c>? Show us how we should send it to its place.’ 
1Sam 6:3 They said, ‘If you are sending the ark of the God of Israel, you must not send it away empty. You must return to him a guilt offering. Then you will be healed and it will be made known to you why his hand is not removed from you.’ 
1Sam 6:4 Then they were asked, ‘What should the guilt offering be which we should return to him?’ and they said, ‘Five golden tumors, and five golden rats, corresponding to the number of the lords of the Philistines; for one plague was upon you as well as upon your lords. 
1Sam 6:5 Therefore you should make images of your tumors, and images of your rats that ravage the land, and you should give glory to the God of Israel. Perhaps he will lighten his hand from on you and your gods and your land. 
1Sam 6:6 Why be stubborn, as the Egyptians and Pharaoh were stubborn? Remember how he made sport of them until they let Israel go?  ¶ 
1Sam 6:7 So take and prepare a new cart, and two milch cows which have never been yoked, and fasten the cows to the cart. But leave their calves behind them at home. 
1Sam 6:8 Take the ark of the  <c>Lord</c> and place it on the cart and put the golden objects which you are returning to him as a guilt offering in a box at its side. Then send it on its way. 
1Sam 6:9 Watch; if it goes on the way to its own land, to Beth-shemesh, then it was the  <c>Lord</c> was did us this great harm, but if not, then we will know that it was not his hand that stuck us but it was an accident that happened to us.’  ¶ 
1Sam 6:10 The men did all this. They took two mulch cows and fastened them to the cart, and shut up their calves at home. 
1Sam 6:11 They placed the ark of the  <c>Lord</c> on the cart, and the box with the golden rats and the images of their tumors. 
1Sam 6:12 The cows took a straight course in the direction of Beth-shemesh. They went along the highway, lowing as they went, and did not turn left nor right. The lords of the Philistines went after them to the border of Beth-shemesh. 
1Sam 6:13 The inhabitants of Beth-shemesh were harvesting their wheat in the valley. They lifted up their eyes and saw the ark, and came rejoicing to meet it. 
1Sam 6:14 When the cart came into the field of Joshua of Beth-shemesh, it stood still there, near a great stone. So they chopped up the wood of the cart and offered the cows as a burnt offering to the  <c>Lord</c>. 
1Sam 6:15 The Levites took down the ark of the  <c>Lord</c> and the box that was with it, in which were the golden objects, and placed them on the great stone. The men of Beth-shemesh offered to the  <c>Lord</c> on that day burnt offerings and ordinary sacrifices. 
1Sam 6:16 When the five lords of the Philistines saw it, they returned to Ekron on that day.  ¶ 
1Sam 6:17 These are the golden tumors which the Philistines returned as a guilt offering to the  <c>Lord</c>: one for Ashdod, one for Gaza, one for Ashkelon, one for Gath, and one for Ekron. 
1Sam 6:18 The golden rats correspond to the number of all the cities of the Philistines belonging to the five lords, both of fortified cities and of country villages. A witness is the great stone, by which they set down the ark of the  <c>Lord</c>. To this day it is in the field of Joshua of Beth-shemesh.  ¶ 
1Sam 6:19 The descendents of Jechoniah, however, did not rejoice with the men of Beth-shemesh, when they welcomed the ark of the  <c>Lord</c>. So he killed seventy of them, and the people mourned because the  <c>Lord</c> had struck the people with such a great slaughter. 
1Sam 6:20 The people of Beth-shemesh said, ‘Who is able to stand before the  <c>Lord</c>, this holy God? To whom can we send him to be rid of him?’ 
1Sam 6:21 So they sent messengers to the inhabitants of Kiriath-jearim, saying, ‘The Philistines have brought back the ark of the  <c>Lord</c>. Come and take it back with you.’  ¶ 
1Sam 7:1 So the people of Kiriath-jearim came, and took the ark of the  <c>Lord</c>, and carried it into the house of Abinadab on the hill, and consecrated Eleazar, his son, to guard the ark of the  <c>Lord</c>.  ¶ 
1Sam 7:2 Many years passed from the time the ark began to abide in Kiriath-jearim – twenty years. All the nation of Israel turned to the  <c>Lord</c>, 
1Sam 7:3 and Samuel spoke to all the nation Israel, saying, ‘If with all your heart you are returning to the  <c>Lord</c>, then put away the foreign gods and the Astartes from among you and direct your hearts towards the  <c>Lord</c> and serve him alone, so that he will deliver you out of the hand of the Philistines.’ 
1Sam 7:4 So the Israelites put away the Baals and the Astartes, and served the  <c>Lord</c> only. 
1Sam 7:5 Then Samuel said, ‘Assemble all Israel at Mizpah and I will intercede for you with the  <c>Lord</c>.’ 
1Sam 7:6 So they assembled at Mizpah, and drew water and poured it out before the  <c>Lord</c>, and fasted all day and confessed, ‘We have sinned against the  <c>Lord</c>.’ And Samuel judged the Israelites in Mizpah.  ¶ 
1Sam 7:7 When the Philistines heard that the Israelites had assembled at Mizpah, the lords of the Philistines marched against Israel. When the Israelites heard of it, they were afraid of the Philistines 
1Sam 7:8 and said to Samuel, ‘Don’t cease to cry to the  <c>Lord</c> our God for us, so that he will save us out of the power of the Philistines.’ 
1Sam 7:9 Samuel took a sucking lamb, and offered it as a whole burnt offering to the  <c>Lord</c>, and cried to the  <c>Lord</c> on behalf of Israel, and the  <c>Lord</c> answered him. 
1Sam 7:10 While Samuel was offering the burnt offering, the Philistines drew near to fight against Israel. But the  <c>Lord</c> thundered with a mighty voice on that day against the Philistines, and threw them into confusion, and they were defeated before Israel. 
1Sam 7:11 The men of Israel went forth from Mizpah and pursued the Philistines and struck them until they were below Beth-car.  ¶ 
1Sam 7:12 Then Samuel took a stone and set it between Mizpah and Jeshanah and named it Ebenezer, saying, ‘This is how far the  <c>Lord</c> has helped us.’ 
1Sam 7:13 So the Philistines were subdued and came no more within the border of Israel. The hand of the  <c>Lord</c> was against the Philistines as long as Samuel lived. 
1Sam 7:14 The cities which the Philistines had taken from Israel were restored to Israel from Ekron to Gath. Israel recovered their territory from the power of the Philistines. There was peace between Israel and the Amorites.  ¶ 
1Sam 7:15 Samuel judged Israel all the days of his life. 
1Sam 7:16 He used to go around from year to year in succession to Bethel, Gilgal, and Mizpah, and he used to judge Israel in all those places. 
1Sam 7:17 But he always returned to Ramah, for there was his home, and there he judged Israel. There he built an altar to the  <c>Lord</c>.  ¶ 
1Sam 8:1 When Samuel grew old he appointed his sons judges over Israel. 
1Sam 8:2 The eldest was called Joel, and his second was called Abijah. They were judges in Beer-sheba. 
1Sam 8:3 However his sons did not follow his ways, but turned aside after unjust gain and took bribes and perverted justice. 
1Sam 8:4 So all the elders of Israel assembled and came to Samuel at Ramah, 
1Sam 8:5 and they said to him, ‘You have become old and your sons don’t follow your ways. Appoint for us a king to rule us like all the other nations.’ 
1Sam 8:6 But the statement displeased Samuel, when they said, ‘Give us a king to judge us.’ And Samuel prayed to the  <c>Lord</c>. 
1Sam 8:7 The  <c>Lord</c> said to Samuel, ‘Listen to the voice of the people and all that they say to you. For they have not rejected you, but they have rejected me from being king over them. 
1Sam 8:8 Like all the deeds which they have done to me since the day that I brought them up out of Egypt, even to this day, in that they have forsaken me and served other gods, so also are they doing to you. 
1Sam 8:9 Listen to what they have to say, but solemnly warn them, and show them the ways of the king who will reign over them.’  ¶ 
1Sam 8:10 Samuel told all the words of the  <c>Lord</c> to the people who were asking him to appoint a king. 
1Sam 8:11 He said, ‘This will be the way of the king who will reign over you: he will take your sons and appoint them to his chariots and cavalry. They will run before his chariots, 
1Sam 8:12 and he will appoint for himself commanders of thousands and commanders of fifties, and some to plow his ground and to reap his harvest and to make his implements of war and the equipment for his chariots. 
1Sam 8:13 He will take your daughters to be perfumers and to be cooks and to be bakers. 
1Sam 8:14 Of your fields and your vineyards and your oliveyards, he will take the best and give them to his servants. 
1Sam 8:15 He will take a tenth of your grain fields and of your vineyards and give to his eunuchs and to his servants. 
1Sam 8:16 He will take your male and female slaves, and the best of your cattle and your donkeys, and use them for his work. 
1Sam 8:17 He will take a tenth of your flocks, and you will become his slaves. 
1Sam 8:18 Then you will cry out in that day against your king whom you chose for yourselves, but the  <c>Lord</c> will not answer you in that day.’ 
1Sam 8:19 But the people refused to listen to the voice of Samuel, and said, ‘No, we must have a king over us, 
1Sam 8:20 so that we will like all other the nations, and so that our king can rule us and go out before us and fight our battles.’ 
1Sam 8:21 And Samuel heard all the words of the people and repeated them to the  <c>Lord</c>. 
1Sam 8:22 And the  <c>Lord</c> said to Samuel, ‘Listen to their voice and make them a king.’ And Samuel said to the people of Israel, ‘Each of your return to your city.’  ¶ 
1Sam 9:1 Now there was a man of Benjamin, whose name was Kish the son of Abiel, the son of Zeror, the son of Becorath, the son of Aphiah, a Benjamite, a man of wealth. 
1Sam 9:2 He had a son whose name was Saul, a man in the prime of life and handsome. There was no one among the Israelites more handsome than he was. He was a head taller than any of the people.  ¶ 
1Sam 9:3 Now the donkeys of Kish, Saul’s father, had strayed. Kish said to Saul his son, ‘Take one of the servants with you and go out and find the donkeys.’ 
1Sam 9:4 They passed through the hill country of Ephraim, and the land of Shalishah, but did not find them. Then they passed through the land of Shaalim, but they were not there. They passed through the land of the Benjamites but did not find them.  ¶ 
1Sam 9:5 When they reached the land of Zuph, Saul said to his servant who was with him, ‘Come, let us return, or my father will stop thinking of the donkeys and become anxious for us.’ 
1Sam 9:6 But the servant answered, ‘There is in this city a man of God, and the man is held in honour. All that he says is sure to come true. Let us go there now, and perhaps he can give us information about the mission on which we are going.’ 
1Sam 9:7 Saul said to the boy, ‘But, suppose we go, what should we take to the man? For the bread is gone from our sacks, and there is no present to take to the man of God. What do we have?’ 
1Sam 9:8 The servant answered Saul again, ‘See I have with me a quarter shekel of silver, and I will give it to the man of God so that he may give us information regarding our mission.’ 
1Sam 9:9 (Formerly in Israel, when someone went to inquire of God, they said, ‘Come let us go to the seer;’ because what is nowadays called a prophet was previously called a seer). 
1Sam 9:10 Then Saul said to his servant, ‘Your advice is good. Come, let us go.’ So they went to the city where the man of God was.  ¶ 
1Sam 9:11 As they were going up the ascent to the city, they met some young girls going out to draw water and said to them, ‘Is the seer here?’ 
1Sam 9:12 They answered, ‘Yes, he is there ahead of you. Hurry, he has come today to the city because the people have a sacrifice today on the high place. 
1Sam 9:13 As soon as you come to the city, you will at once find him before he goes up to the high place to eat. The people will not eat until he comes, because he is needed to bless the sacrifice before the guests eat. Now go up, and at this time you will meet him.’ 
1Sam 9:14 So they went up to the city. When they came within the city gate, Samuel was just coming out toward them, to go up to the high place.  ¶ 
1Sam 9:15 Now the  <c>Lord</c> had given to Samuel, a day before Saul came, the following revelation: 
1Sam 9:16 ‘At this time tomorrow I will send you a man out of the land of Benjamin and you must anoint him to be a prince over my people Israel. He will save my people out of the hand of the Philistines, because I have seen the suffering of my people, and their cry has reached me.’ 
1Sam 9:17 When Samuel saw Saul, the  <c>Lord</c> indicated to him, ‘This is the man of whom I spoke to you! He is the one who will rule over my people.’ 
1Sam 9:18 Then Saul drew near to Samuel in the gate, and said, ‘Tell me, please, where the seer’s house is.’ 
1Sam 9:19 And Samuel answered Saul, ‘I am the seer. Go up before me to the high place, for you will eat with me today. In the morning I will let you go, and will tell you all that is in your heart. 
1Sam 9:20 As for your donkeys that were lost three days ago, do not trouble yourself about them. They have been found. To whom does all that is desirable in Israel belong? Does it not belong to you, and to your ancestral house? 
1Sam 9:21 Saul answered, ‘But I am a Benjamite, from the smallest of the tribes of Israel, and my family is the least of all the families of the tribe of Benjamin! Why do you speak like this to me?’  ¶ 
1Sam 9:22 Samuel took Saul and his servant and brought them into the hall and made them sit at the head of the guests (who were about thirty persons). 
1Sam 9:23 And he said to the cook, ‘Bring the portion I gave you, which I told you to put aside.’ 
1Sam 9:24 The cook took up the leg and placed it before Saul. And Samuel said, ‘See, the meat is served! Eat! It was kept for you until the appointed time, so that you might eat with those whom I have invited.’  ¶ So Saul ate with Samuel that day. 
1Sam 9:25 After they came down from the high place into the city, they spread a bed for Saul on the roof, and he lay down for the night. 
1Sam 9:26 At daybreak Samuel called to Saul on the roof, ‘Get up, so that I can send you on your way.’ So Saul arose, and he and Samuel went out into the street.  ¶ 
1Sam 9:27 As they were going down at the outskirts of the city, Samuel said to Saul, ‘Tell your servant to go on ahead of us, but you stay here so that I can make known to you the word of God.’  ¶ 
1Sam 10:1 Then Samuel took a vial of oil, and poured it on his head, and kissed him and said, ‘The  <c>Lord</c> has anointed you to be a ruler over his people Israel. You will reign over the people of the  <c>Lord</c> and save them from the power of their enemies all around. This will be the sign that the  <c>Lord</c> has anointed you to be a ruler over his heritage: 
1Sam 10:2 when you go from me today you will find two men at Rachel’s tomb, in the boundary of Benjamin at Zelzah. They will say to you, “The donkeys you went to seek are found, and now your father has dismissed the matter of the donkeys and is anxious for you, asking, ‘What should I do about my son?’” 
1Sam 10:3 Then you will go on from there and come to the oak of Tabor. There three men going up to God to Bethel will meet you, one carrying three kids, and another carrying three loaves of bread, and another carrying a skin of wine. 
1Sam 10:4 They will greet you and give you two loaves of bread which you will take from their hand. 
1Sam 10:5 After that you will come to Gibeah-elohim, where the garrison of the Philistines is. When you come to the city, you will meet a band of prophets coming down from the high place with a lyre, a tambourine, a flute, and a harp before them, and they will be prophesying. 
1Sam 10:6 The spirit of the  <c>Lord</c> will rush upon you, and you will prophesy with them and will be turned into another man. 
1Sam 10:7 When these signs come to you, you will do as the occasion offers, for God is with you. 
1Sam 10:8 You must go down before me to Gilgal, and then I will come down to you, to offer burnt offerings. Wait seven days until I come to you and show you what to do.’  ¶ 
1Sam 10:9 As Saul turned his back to go from Samuel, God gave him a change of heart, and all those signs came to pass that day. 
1Sam 10:10 On his way to Gibeah, a band of prophets met him, and the spirit of God possessed him, and he prophesied among them. 
1Sam 10:11 When everyone who knew him saw him in the act of prophesying with the prophets, the people said to one another, ‘What has come over the son of Kish? Is Saul also among the prophets?’ 
1Sam 10:12 One of the bystanders answered, ‘Who is their father?’ Therefore it became a proverb, ‘Is Saul also among the prophets?’ 
1Sam 10:13 When he had finished prophesying, he went to the high place. 
1Sam 10:14 Saul’s uncle said to him and to his servant, ‘Where did you go?’ He said, ‘To find the donkeys, and when we saw that they were not found, we went to Samuel.’ 
1Sam 10:15 And Saul’s uncle said, ‘Tell me what Samuel said to you.’ 
1Sam 10:16 And Saul said to his uncle, ‘He told us that the donkeys were found.’ But about the matter of the kingdom of which Samuel had spoken, he told him nothing.  ¶ 
1Sam 10:17 Samuel called the people together to Mizpah, 
1Sam 10:18 and said to the Israelites, ‘This is what the  <c>Lord</c> the God of Israel says: I brought up Israel out of Egypt, and I delivered you out of the hand of the Egyptians, and out of the hand of all the kingdoms that were oppressing you. 
1Sam 10:19 But today you rejected your God, who has been saving you from all your calamities and your distresses. You have said to him, “No! You must set a king over us.” Now therefore present yourselves before the  <c>Lord</c> by your tribes and by your clans.’  ¶ 
1Sam 10:20 So Samuel brought all the tribes of Israel near, and the tribe of Benjamin was picked by lot. 
1Sam 10:21 He brought the tribe of Benjamin near by their clans, and the clan of the Matrites was picked by lot. He brought near the clan of Matri man by man and Saul the son of Kish was picked, but when they searched for him, him he could not be found. 
1Sam 10:22 So they asked of the  <c>Lord</c> further, ‘Did the man come here?’ And the  <c>Lord</c> answered ‘See, he has hid himself among the baggage.’ 
1Sam 10:23 Someone ran and brought him from there. When he stood among the people, he was taller than any of the people by a head. 
1Sam 10:24 Said Samuel to the people, ‘Have you seen this man whom the  <c>Lord</c> has chosen? For there is no one like him among all the people.’ All the people shouted loudly, ‘Long live the king!’  ¶ 
1Sam 10:25 In this way Samuel revealed to the people the manner of the kingdom, and wrote it in a book, and laid it up before the  <c>Lord</c>. Then Samuel sent all the people away, each to their home. 
1Sam 10:26 And Saul also went to his home at Gibeah; and with him went the warriors whose hearts God had touched. 
1Sam 10:27 But there were some scoundrels who said, ‘How can this man save us?’ They despised him, and brought him no presents.  ¶ 
1Sam 11:1 About a month later Nahash the Ammonite came up and besieged Jabesh-gilead. All the men of Jabesh said to Nahash, ‘Make terms with us and we will serve you.’ 
1Sam 11:2 But Nahash the Ammonite said to them, ‘On this condition will I make terms with you: that I gouge out the right eye of each of you and by this bring disgrace on all Israel.’ 
1Sam 11:3 The elders of Jabesh said to him, ‘Give us seven days respite, so that we can send messengers through all the territory of Israel. Then if there be no one to save us we will surrender to you.’ 
1Sam 11:4 So the messengers came to Gibeah of Saul and recounted the facts in the hearing of the people, and all the people wept aloud.  ¶ 
1Sam 11:5 Saul was just coming from the field, driving the oxen. He said, ‘What is the trouble with the people? Why are they weeping?’ Then they told him the words of the men of Jabesh. 
1Sam 11:6 The spirit of the  <c>Lord</c> rushed upon Saul when he heard these words, and his anger was greatly aroused. 
1Sam 11:7 He took a yoke of oxen, and cut them in pieces, and sent them throughout all the territory of Israel by the hand of messengers, saying, ‘Whoever does not come out after Saul and after Samuel, so will it be done to his oxen!’ Then a terror from the  <c>Lord</c> fell upon the people, and they rallied as one man.  ¶ 
1Sam 11:8 He mustered them in Bezek. The Israelites were three hundred thousand, and the men of Judah thirty thousand. 
1Sam 11:9 They said to the messengers who came, ‘Say this to the men of Jabesh-gilead: Tomorrow, by the time the sun becomes hot, deliverance will have come to you.’ So the messengers came and told the men of Jabesh. They rejoiced, 
1Sam 11:10 and said to Nahash, ‘Tomorrow we will surrender to you, and you can do to us whatever you please.’ 
1Sam 11:11 On the following day, Saul divided the people into three divisions. They came into the midst of the camp in the morning watch, and massacred the Ammonites, until the heat of the day. The survivors scattered, so that no two of them were left together.  ¶ 
1Sam 11:12 The people said to Samuel, ‘Who is he who said, “Saul will not reign over us?” Bring the men that we may put them to death!’ 
1Sam 11:13 But Saul said, ‘Today no one will be put to death, because today the  <c>Lord</c> has brought deliverance to Israel.’  ¶ 
1Sam 11:14 Then Samuel said to the people, ‘Come, and let us go to Gilgal, and renew the kingdom there.’ 
1Sam 11:15 All the people went to Gilgal. There they made Saul king before the  <c>Lord</c> in Gilgal, and sacrificed peace offerings before the  <c>Lord</c>, and there Saul and all the men of Israel held a great celebration.  ¶ 
1Sam 12:1 Samuel said to all Israel, ‘See, I have listened to you in all that you have said to me and have appointed a king over you. 
1Sam 12:2 From now on, behold the king who will lead you. As for me, I am old and grey, but my sons are with you. I have led you from my youth to this day. 
1Sam 12:3 Here I am! Testify against me before the  <c>Lord</c>, and before his annointed. Whose ox have I taken? Whose donkey have I taken? Whom have I oppressed? Whom have I defrauded? From whose hand have I taken a bribe to turn a blind eye? Testify and I will restore it to you.’ 
1Sam 12:4 They said, ‘You have not oppressed us, nor defrauded us, nor have you taken anything from anyone’s hand.’ 
1Sam 12:5 So he said to them, ‘The  <c>Lord</c> is witness against you, and his anointed is witness this day, that you have not found anything in my hand.’ They said, ‘He is witness.’  ¶ 
1Sam 12:6 Then Samuel said to the people, ‘The  <c>Lord</c> is witness, who appointed Moses and Aaron and who brought your ancestors up out of the land of Egypt. 
1Sam 12:7 Now therefore take your stand so that I may declare to you before the  <c>Lord</c> all the righteous acts of the  <c>Lord</c>, which he did to you and to your ancestors. 
1Sam 12:8 When Jacob came to Egypt, and your ancestors cried to the  <c>Lord</c>, then the  <c>Lord</c> sent Moses and Aaron to bring your ancestors out of Egypt, and settled them in this place. 
1Sam 12:9 But they forgot the  <c>Lord</c> their God, and he sold them into the hand of Sisera, commander of the army of King Jabin of Hazor, and into the hand of the Philistines and into the hand of the king of Moab. They fought against them, 
1Sam 12:10 and cried to the  <c>Lord</c> and said, ‘We have sinned because we have forsaken the  <c>Lord</c> and served the Baals and the Astartes. Deliver us out of the hand of our enemies, and we will serve you.’ 
1Sam 12:11 And the  <c>Lord</c> sent Jerubbaal, and Barak, and Jephthah, and Samson, and delivered you out of the hand of your enemies surrounding you so that you lived in safety. 
1Sam 12:12 But when you saw that Nahash the king of the Ammonites came against you, you said to me, “No, but a king must reign over us,” although the  <c>Lord</c> your God was your king. 
1Sam 12:13 Now therefore see the king whom you have chosen, for the  <c>Lord</c> has now set a king over you. 
1Sam 12:14 If you will fear the  <c>Lord</c> and serve him and listen to his voice, and not rebel against the commandment of the  <c>Lord</c>, and both you and the king who reigns over you follow the  <c>Lord</c> your God, then it will be well. 
1Sam 12:15 But if you will not listen to the voice of the  <c>Lord</c>, but rebel against the commandment of the  <c>Lord</c>, then will the hand of the  <c>Lord</c> be against you and your king. 
1Sam 12:16 Now therefore take your stand and see this great thing that the  <c>Lord</c> is about to do before your eyes. 
1Sam 12:17 Is it not wheat harvest today? I will call upon the  <c>Lord</c> to send thunder and rain. You will know and see that your wickedness is great, which you have done in the sight of the  <c>Lord</c> in asking for a king.’ 
1Sam 12:18 So Samuel called upon the  <c>Lord</c>, and the  <c>Lord</c> sent thunder and rain that day. All the people were greatly afraid of the  <c>Lord</c> and Samuel.  ¶ 
1Sam 12:19 Then all the people said to Samuel, ‘Intercede with the  <c>Lord</c> your God in behalf of your servants so that we do not die, because we have added to all our sins the crime of asking for a king.’ 
1Sam 12:20 But Samuel said to the people, ‘Don’t be afraid, you have indeed done all this evil, but do not turn aside from following the  <c>Lord</c>. Serve the  <c>Lord</c> with all your heart, 
1Sam 12:21 and do not turn aside after useless things which cannot profit or deliver, for they are useless. 
1Sam 12:22 For the  <c>Lord</c> because of his great name will not cast away his people, for the  <c>Lord</c> has undertaken to make you his own people. 
1Sam 12:23 Moreover, as for me, far be it from me that I should sin against the  <c>Lord</c> in ceasing to pray for you, and I will instruct you in the good and the right way. 
1Sam 12:24 Only fear the  <c>Lord</c> and serve him in truth with all your heart, for you see the great things he has done for you. 
1Sam 12:25 But if you persist in doing wrong, both you and your king will be swept away. 
1Sam 13:1 Saul was … years old when he began to reign, and he reigned … and two years over Israel. <sup>[    The numbers are missing from the text. ]</sup> ¶ 
1Sam 13:2 Saul chose three thousand men of Israel. Two thousand were with Saul in Michmash and on the mountain of Bethel and a thousand were with Jonathan in Gibeah of Benjamin. The rest of the people he sent to their homes. 
1Sam 13:3 Jonathan defeated the garrison of the Philistines that was in Geba, and the news reached the Philistines that the Hebrews were in revolt. But Saul had in the meantime caused the trumpet to be blown throughout all the land, 
1Sam 13:4 and all Israel heard the news that Saul had defeated the garrison of the Philistines, and also that Israel had brought itself into ill odor with the Philistines. The people were called out to join Saul at Gilgal.  ¶ 
1Sam 13:5 The Philistines were gathered together to fight with Israel – thirty thousand chariots and six thousand horsemen and fighters as numerous as the sand on the seashore. They came up and encamped in Michmash, east of Beth-aven. 
1Sam 13:6 When the Israelites saw that they were in a strait (for the fighters were hard pressed), they hid themselves in caves, in holes, in rocks, in tombs, and in pits. 
1Sam 13:7 Also many people went over the Jordan to the land of Gad and Gilead. But Saul was still in Gilgal, and all the people followed him trembling.  ¶ 
1Sam 13:8 He waited seven days for the appointed time which Samuel had set, but Samuel did not come to Gilgal, and the people scattered away from him. 
1Sam 13:9 So Saul said, ‘Bring here to me the burnt-offering and the peace-offerings.’ He offered the burnt-offering. 
1Sam 13:10 Just as he had finished offering the burnt-offering, Samuel came, and Saul went out to greet him. 
1Sam 13:11 Samuel said, ‘What have you done?’ And Saul said, ‘Because I saw that the people were scattering away from me and you did not come within the appointed time, and the Philistines were gathering together at Michmash, 
1Sam 13:12 I said, “Now the Philistines will come down to me at Gilgal, and I will not have appeased the  <c>Lord</c>.” So I felt compelled to offer the burnt-offering.’ 
1Sam 13:13 Samuel said to Saul, ‘You have acted foolishly. If you had kept the command of the  <c>Lord</c> your God, which he commanded you, then would the  <c>Lord</c> have established your kingdom over Israel forever. 
1Sam 13:14 But now your kingdom will not continue. The  <c>Lord</c> has sought out a man after his own heart, and the  <c>Lord</c> has appointed him a leader over his people, because you have not kept that which the  <c>Lord</c> commanded you.’ 
1Sam 13:15 Then Samuel arose and left Gilgal. The rest of the people followed Saul, going from Gilgal towards Gibeah of Benjamin.  ¶ Saul counted the people who were with him, about six hundred men. 
1Sam 13:16 Saul and Jonathan his son, together with the people who were with them, were staying in Gibeah of Benjamin, while the Philistines encamped in Michmash. 
1Sam 13:17 Raiding parties came out of the camp of the Philistines in three divisions: one division turned in the direction of Ophrah in the land of Shual, 
1Sam 13:18 and another division turned in the direction of Beth-horon, and another division turned in the direction of the hill that looks down over the valley of Zeboim toward the wilderness.  ¶ 
1Sam 13:19 Now there was no smith found throughout all the land of Israel, for the Philistines said, ‘The Hebrews must not make swords or spears,’ 
1Sam 13:20 so all the Israelites went down to the Philistines to sharpen each his plowshare and his sickle and his ax and his mattock. 
1Sam 13:21 The charge was two thirds of a shekel for ploughshares and mattocks, and one third of a shekel for sharpening the axes and setting the ox goads. 
1Sam 13:22 So on the day of the battle, none of the people with Saul and Jonathan had a sword or spear; but Saul and Jonathan his son had them.  ¶ 
1Sam 13:23 A garrison of the Philistines had gone out to the pass of Michmash, 
1Sam 14:1 and one day Jonathan the son of Saul said to the young man who bore his armour, ‘Come – let’s go over to the Philistines’ garrison that is on the other side.’ But he did not tell his father. 
1Sam 14:2 Saul was sitting in the outskirts of Gibeah under the pomegranate tree at Mignon, and with him were about six hundred men. 
1Sam 14:3 Ahijah the son of Ahitub, Ichabod’s brother, the son of Phinehas, the son of Eli, the priest of the  <c>Lord</c> at Shiloh, was in charge of an ephod. The people did not know that Jonathan had gone. 
1Sam 14:4 Between the passes by which Jonathan sought to go over to the Philistines’ garrison there was a rocky crag on the one side, and a rocky crag on the other side; and the name of the one was Bozez, and the name of the other Seneh. 
1Sam 14:5 One crag rose up on the north in front of Michmash, and the other on the south in front of Geba.  ¶ 
1Sam 14:6 Jonathan said to the young man who bore his armour, ‘Come, let’s go over to the garrison of these uncircumcised Philistines. Perhaps the  <c>Lord</c> will act for us, for there is nothing that can prevent the  <c>Lord</c> from saving by many or by few.’ 
1Sam 14:7 His armour-bearer said to him, ‘Do whatever your judgment dictates. I am with you, your wish is mine.’ 
1Sam 14:8 Then Jonathan said, ‘We will pass over to the men and show ourselves to them. 
1Sam 14:9 If they say to us, “Stand still until we can reach you,” then we will stand still in our place, and will not go up to them. 
1Sam 14:10 But if they say, “Come up to us,” then we will go up; for the  <c>Lord</c> has given them into our hand, and this will be the sign to us.’ 
1Sam 14:11 When both of them showed themselves to the garrison of the Philistines, the Philistines said, ‘There are Hebrews coming out of the holes where they have hidden themselves.’ 
1Sam 14:12 The men of the garrison cried out to Jonathan and his armour-bearer, ‘Come up to us so that we can tell you something.’ Then Jonathan said to his armour-bearer, ‘Come up after me, for the  <c>Lord</c> has given them into the hand of Israel.’ 
1Sam 14:13 And Jonathan climbed up on his hands and feet, and his armour-bearer after him. The Philistines fell before Jonathan, and his armour-bearer kept despatching them after him. 
1Sam 14:14 In the first attack Jonathan and his armour-bearer slew about twenty men in an area of about half an acre. 
1Sam 14:15 There was panic in the camp, in the field, and among all the people. The garrison, and even the raiders trembled and the earth quaked so that it produced a great panic.  ¶ 
1Sam 14:16 The watchmen of Saul in Gibeah of Benjamin looked, and saw the army surging hither and thither. 
1Sam 14:17 Saul said to the people who were with him, ‘Investigate now and see who is gone from us.’ When they had investigated they found that Jonathan and his armour-bearer were not there. 
1Sam 14:18 And Saul said to Ahijah, ‘Bring the ephod here,’ for at that time he had charge of the ephod before Israel. 
1Sam 14:19 While Saul was speaking to the priest, the tumult in the camp of the Philistines kept on increasing. So Saul said to the priest, ‘Draw back your hand.’ 
1Sam 14:20 And Saul and all the people that were with him responded to the call, and came to the battle, and every man’s sword was turned upon his fellow and there was very great confusion. 
1Sam 14:21 The Hebrews who had gone over to the Philistines and joined their the camp, turned to be with the Israelites who were with Saul and Jonathan. 
1Sam 14:22 Likewise all the Israelites who were in hiding in the hill-country of Ephraim, when they heard that the Philistines were fleeing, pursued close after them in the battle. 
1Sam 14:23 So the  <c>Lord</c> saved Israel that day, and the battle passed on beyond Beth-aven.  ¶ 
1Sam 14:24 Then Saul committed a great act of folly that day, for he laid an oath on the people, saying, ‘Cursed is the man who eats any food until evening and until I avenge myself on my enemies.’ So none of the people tasted food. 
1Sam 14:25 Now there was honeycomb in that country, 
1Sam 14:26 and when the people came to the honeycomb, the bees had just flown away, but no one put his hand to his mouth, for the people feared the oath. 
1Sam 14:27 But Jonathan had not heard when his father charged the people. He put forth the end of the rod that was in his hand and dipped it in the honeycomb and put his hand to his mouth, and his eyes were lightened. 
1Sam 14:28 Then one of the fighters spoke up, ‘Your father charged the people saying, “Cursed be the man who eats food this day.” So the men are exhausted.’ 
1Sam 14:29 Then said Jonathan, ‘My father has brought disaster on the land. See how I have been refreshed, because I tasted a little of this honey. 
1Sam 14:30 If only the people had eaten freely today of the spoil of their enemies which they found, how much greater would have been the slaughter of the Philistines!’  ¶ 
1Sam 14:31 But they struck at the Philistines that day from Michmash to Aijalon, and the people were very faint, 
1Sam 14:32 and they rushed upon the spoil and took sheep and oxen and calves and slaughtered them on the ground, and the people ate them with the blood. 
1Sam 14:33 When Saul was told that the people were sinning against the  <c>Lord</c> in eating with the blood, he said to those who told him, ‘Treason! Roll a great stone to me.’ 
1Sam 14:34 And Saul said, ‘Go out among the people and say to them, “Let each man bring to me his ox and his sheep, and slay it here and eat; but do not sin against the  <c>Lord</c> in eating the flesh together with the blood.”’ All the people brought their oxen that night and slew them there. 
1Sam 14:35 So Saul built an altar to the  <c>Lord</c>. That was the first altar that he built to the  <c>Lord</c>.  ¶ 
1Sam 14:36 Then Saul said, ‘Let us go down after the Philistines by night and plunder among them until daybreak, and let us not spare a single man.’ They said, ‘Do whatever you think best,’ but the priest said, ‘Let us first consut God.’ 
1Sam 14:37 So Saul asked of God, ‘Should I go down after the Philistines? Will you deliver them into the hand of Israel?’ But there was no answer that day. 
1Sam 14:38 And Saul said, ‘Come here, all you chiefs of the people and know and see in whom is this guilt today. 
1Sam 14:39 For as the  <c>Lord</c> lives, who delivered Israel, even if it be in Jonathan my son, that man will surely die.’ But no one of all the people answered him. 
1Sam 14:40 Then he said to all Israel, ‘You will on one side, and I and Jonathan my son will be on the other side.’ The people said to Saul, ‘Do what seems good to you.’ 
1Sam 14:41 Therefore Saul asked the  <c>Lord</c>, God of Israel, ‘Why have you not answered your servant this day? If the guilt is in me or in Jonathan my son, the  <c>Lord</c>, God of Israel, give Urim, but if the guilt is in your people Israel, give Thummim.’ And the lot indicated Jonathan and Saul, and the people were cleared. 
1Sam 14:42 And Saul said, ‘Cast the lot between me and Jonathan my son. He whom the  <c>Lord</c> indicates, must die.’ The people said to Saul, ‘It must not be so!’ But Saul overruled the people and they cast the lot between him and Jonathan his son. And Jonathan was indicated.  ¶ 
1Sam 14:43 Then Saul said to Jonathan, ‘Tell me what you have done.’ And Jonathan told him, saying, ‘I did indeed taste a little honey with the end of the staff that was in my hand, and here I am! I am ready to die.’ 
1Sam 14:44 And Saul said, ‘May God do to me whatever he pleases, you must surely die, Jonathan!’ 
1Sam 14:45 But the people said to Saul, ‘Should Jonathan die who has wrought this great victory in Israel? Far from it! As the  <c>Lord</c> lives, not one hair of his head will fall to the ground, for he has worked with God this day.’ So the people redeemed Jonathan, so that he did not die. 
1Sam 14:46 Then Saul broke off from pursuing the Philistines and the Philistines went to their own country.  ¶ 
1Sam 14:47 When Saul had taken the kingdom over Israel, he fought against all his enemies on every side: against Moab and the Ammonites and Edom and the kings of Zobah, and the Philistines. Wherever he turned he was victorious. 
1Sam 14:48 He did mighty deeds and struck the Amalekites and delivered Israel out of the hands of its plunderers.  ¶ 
1Sam 14:49 Now the sons of Saul were: Jonathan, Ishvi, and Malchishua. The names of his two daughters were: the eldest, Merab, the youngest, Michal. 
1Sam 14:50 The name of Saul’s wife was Ahinoam the daughter of Ahimaaz. The name of the commander of his army was Abner the son Saul’s uncle Ner. 
1Sam 14:51 Kish the father of Saul and Ner the father of Abner were sons of Abiel.  ¶ 
1Sam 14:52 The war against the Philistines was severe all the days of Saul. Whenever Saul saw any valiant or efficient man, he would take him into his service.  ¶ 
1Sam 15:1 Samuel said to Saul, ‘The  <c>Lord</c> sent me to anoint you to be king over his people Israel. Now listen to the words of the  <c>Lord</c>. 
1Sam 15:2 This says the  <c>Lord</c> of armies: “I have determined to punish the Amalekites for wha they did to Israel, in opposing them as they came up out of Egypt. 
1Sam 15:3 Now go and attack Amalek and utterly destroy all that they have. Spare no one but slay both man and woman, child and infant, ox and sheep, camel and donkey.”’  ¶ 
1Sam 15:4 So Saul summoned the people and mustered them in Telaim, two hundred thousand foot soldiers and ten thousand from Judah. 
1Sam 15:5 When Saul came to the city of Amalek, he lay in wait in the valley. 
1Sam 15:6 Saul said to the Kenites, ‘Go away, withdraw from among the Amalekites, or I will destroy you with them, for you showed kindness to all the Israelites when they came up from Egypt.’ So the Kenites departed from among the Amalekites. 
1Sam 15:7 And Saul struck the Amalekites from Havilah as far as Shur, which is east of Egypt. 
1Sam 15:8 He took Agag the king of Amalek alive and completely destroyed all the people with the sword. 
1Sam 15:9 But Saul and his army spared Agag and the best of the sheep, the oxen, the fat beasts, the lambs, and all that was good, and would not completely destroy them. But everything that was worthless and despised they completely destroyed.  ¶ 
1Sam 15:10 Then the word of the  <c>Lord</c> came to Samuel saying, 
1Sam 15:11 ‘I repent of making Saul king, because he has turned from following me and has not carried out my commands.’ And Samuel was angry and cried to the  <c>Lord</c> all night. 
1Sam 15:12 Early in the morning Samuel rose to meet Saul. Then Samuel was told, ‘Saul came to Carmel and has just set up a monument to himself and has turned and passed on and gone down to Gilgal.’ 
1Sam 15:13 When Samuel came to Saul, Saul said to him, ‘Blessed be you of the  <c>Lord</c>! I have fulfilled the command of the  <c>Lord</c>.’ 
1Sam 15:14 And Samuel said, ‘What then is this bleating of the sheep in my ears and the lowing of the cattle which I hear?’ 
1Sam 15:15 And Saul said, ‘They have brought them from the Amalekites, for the people spared the best off the sheep and of the oxen to sacrifice to the  <c>Lord</c> your God, and the rest we have completely destroyed.’ 
1Sam 15:16 Then Samuel said to ‘Saul, Stop! and let me tell you what the  <c>Lord</c> has said to me this night.’ He said to him, ‘Speak.’  ¶ 
1Sam 15:17 Samuel said, ‘Though you are little in your own sight, are you not the head of the tribes of Israel? And the  <c>Lord</c> anointed you king over Israel, 
1Sam 15:18 and the  <c>Lord</c> sent you on an expedition and said, “Go, and completely destroy the sinners of Amalek and fight against them until they are consumed.” 
1Sam 15:19 Why then did you not obey the voice of the  <c>Lord</c> and why did you swoop upon the spoil and displease the  <c>Lord</c>?’ 
1Sam 15:20 And Saul said to Samuel, ‘I have obeyed the voice of the  <c>Lord</c> and have gone on the expedition which the  <c>Lord</c> sent me on and have brought back Agag the king of the Amalekites and have completely destroyed the Amalekites. 
1Sam 15:21 But the people took of the spoil, sheep and oxen, the best of the things which were placed under the ban, to sacrifice to the  <c>Lord</c> your God in Gilgal.’ 
1Sam 15:22 And Samuel said, ‘Does the  <c>Lord</c> delight in burnt-offerings and sacrifices as in obedience to the voice of the  <c>Lord</c>? Behold to obey is better than sacrifice, and to listen than the fat of rams. 
1Sam 15:23 For rebellion is as bad as the sin of divination, and obstinacy as idolatry. Because you have rejected the word of the  <c>Lord</c>, he has rejected you from being king.’ 
1Sam 15:24 And Saul said to Samuel, ‘I have sinned, for I have transgressed the command of the  <c>Lord</c> and your words because I feared the people and listened to their voice. 
1Sam 15:25 Now therefore pardon for my sin and turn back with me, that I may worship the  <c>Lord</c>.’ 
1Sam 15:26 But Samuel said to Saul, ‘I will not turn back with you, for you have rejected the word of the  <c>Lord</c> and the  <c>Lord</c> has rejected you from being king over Israel.’ 
1Sam 15:27 As Samuel turned to go away, Saul seized the skirt of his robe, but it tore. 
1Sam 15:28 Then Samuel said to him, ‘The  <c>Lord</c> has today torn the kingdom of Israel from you and has given it to your neighbor who is better than you. 
1Sam 15:29 Moreover the Glory of Israel will not lie nor repent, for he is not a mortal that he should change his mind.’ 
1Sam 15:30 Then Saul said, ‘I have sinned, yet honour me now at least before the elders of my people and before Israel, and turn back with me, so that I may worship the  <c>Lord</c> your God.’ 
1Sam 15:31 So Samuel turned back and followed Saul, while Saul worshipped the  <c>Lord</c>.  ¶ 
1Sam 15:32 Then Samuel said, ‘Bring here to me Agag the king of the Amalekites.’ And Agag came to him trembling and said, ‘Surely death is bitter.’ 
1Sam 15:33 Samuel said, ‘As your sword has bereaved women, so will your mother be the most bereaved of women.’ Then Samuel hewed Agag in pieces before the  <c>Lord</c> in Gilgal.  ¶ 
1Sam 15:34 Then Samuel went to Ramah, but Saul went up to his house to Gibeah of Saul. 
1Sam 15:35 And Samuel did not see Saul again until the day of his death, for Samuel grieved over Saul. Now the  <c>Lord</c> repented that he had made Saul king over Israel.  ¶ 
1Sam 16:1 The  <c>Lord</c> said to Samuel, ‘How long will you grieve over Saul, when I have rejected him from being king over Israel? Fill your horn with oil and go. I will send you to Jesse the Bethlehemite, for I have chosen for myself a king among his sons.’ 
1Sam 16:2 And Samuel said, ‘How can I go, since Saul will hear of it and kill me?’ But the  <c>Lord</c> said, ‘Take a calf with you and say you have come to sacrifice to the  <c>Lord</c>. 
1Sam 16:3 Invite Jesse to the sacrifice, and I will show you what to do, and anoint the man whom I name.’ 
1Sam 16:4 So Samuel did that which the  <c>Lord</c> had commanded. When he came to Bethlehem, the elders of the city came trembling to meet him and said, ‘Do you come in peace?’ 
1Sam 16:5 He said ‘Yes, I have come to sacrifice to the  <c>Lord</c>. Purify yourselves and rejoiced with me in the sacrifice.’ He purified Jesse and his sons and invited them to the sacrifice.  ¶ 
1Sam 16:6 When they came and he saw Eliab, he said, ‘Surely the  <c>Lord</c>’s annointed is now in presence.’ 
1Sam 16:7 But the  <c>Lord</c> said to Samuel, ‘Pay no attention to his appearance or to the height of his stature, because I have rejected him. The  <c>Lord</c> does not see as humans see, for they look on the outward appearance, but the  <c>Lord</c> looks at the heart.’ 
1Sam 16:8 Then Jesse called Abinadab, and brought him before Samuel. But he said, ‘Neither has the  <c>Lord</c> chosen this one.’ 
1Sam 16:9 Then Jesse brought forward Shammah. But he said, Neither hath the  <c>Lord</c> chosen this one. 
1Sam 16:10 Then Jesse brought his seven sons before Samuel. But Samuel said to Jesse, ‘The  <c>Lord</c> has not chosen these.’ 
1Sam 16:11 And Samuel said to Jesse, ‘Are these all your sons?’ He said, ‘There is still the youngest, but he is a shepherd with the flock.’ So Samuel said to Jesse, ‘Send and bring him, for we will not sit down until he is brought here.’ 
1Sam 16:12 So he sent and brought him in. Now he was handsome, a youth with beautiful eyes and ruddy cheeks. And the  <c>Lord</c> said, ‘Get up, anoint him, for this is the man.’ 
1Sam 16:13 Then Samuel took the horn of oil and anointed him in the midst of his brothers. The spirit of the  <c>Lord</c> came with power upon David from that day forward. And Samuel arose and went to Ramah.  ¶ 
1Sam 16:14 Now the spirit of the  <c>Lord</c> had departed from Saul and an evil spirit from the  <c>Lord</c> tormented him. 
1Sam 16:15 And Saul’s servants said to him, ‘See now, an evil spirit from God is tormenting you. 
1Sam 16:16 Command your servants who are before and they will seek for our lord a man skilful in playing the lyre. Then whenever the evil spirit comes upon you he will play with his hand, and you will be better.’ 
1Sam 16:17 So Saul said to his servants, ‘Provide me now someone who plays well, and bring him to me.’ 
1Sam 16:18 One of the young men answered, ‘I have seen a son of Jesse the Bethlehemite who is skilful in playing and a valiant man, a good fighter, judicious in speech, a man of good appearance, and the  <c>Lord</c> is with him.’ 
1Sam 16:19 So Saul sent messengers to Jesse and said, ‘Send me David your son, who is with the flock.’ 
1Sam 16:20 And Jesse took ten loaves of bread, and a skin of wine, and a kid, and sent them to Saul with David his son. 
1Sam 16:21 So David came to Saul and entered his service. Saul loved him so much that he became one of his armour-bearers, 
1Sam 16:22 and sent a message to Jesse, saying, ‘Let David enter my service, for he has found favour in my sight.’ 
1Sam 16:23 Whenever the evil spirit from God came upon Saul, David would take the lyre and play with his hand and Saul would breathe freely and would feel better and the evil spirit would depart from him.  ¶ 
1Sam 17:1 Now the Philistines mustered together their forces for war. They were gathered together at Socoh, which belongs to Judah, and encamped between Socoh and Azekah, in Ephes-dammim. 
1Sam 17:2 Saul and the men of Israel were gathered together and encamped in the valley of Elah, and they drew up in battle-array against the Philistines. 
1Sam 17:3 The Philistines were standing on the mountain on the one side, and the Israelites were standing on the mountain on the other side, and the valley was between them. 
1Sam 17:4 A champion came out from the camp of the Philistines. His name was Goliath of Gath and he was over nine feet in height. 
1Sam 17:5 He had a helmet of bronze on his head, and he was clad with a bronze breastplate of scales, the weight of which was about two hundred pounds. 
1Sam 17:6 He had greaves of bronze on his legs and a javelin of bronze slung between his shoulders. 
1Sam 17:7 The shaft of his spear was like a weaver’s beam, and the head of his iron spear weighed twenty-four pounds. His shield-bearer went before him. 
1Sam 17:8 He stood and cried out to the ranks of Israel, ‘Why have you come out to draw up the line of battle? Am not I a Philistine and you Saul’s servants? Choose a man for yourselves and let him come down to me. 
1Sam 17:9 If he is able to fight with me and kill me, then we will be your servants. But if I prevail against him and kill him, then you will be our servants and serve us.’ 
1Sam 17:10 The Philistine said, ‘I have insulted the ranks of Israel today! Give me a man that we may fight together.’ 
1Sam 17:11 When Saul and all Israel heard these words of the Philistine, they were terrified and greatly afraid.  ¶ 
1Sam 17:12 Now David was the son of an Ephrathite of Bethlehem in Judah, whose name was Jesse. Jesse had eight sons. The man was old in the days of Saul, advanced in years among men. 
1Sam 17:13 The three eldest sons of Jesse had gone after Saul to the war. Their names were Eliab, the eldest, his second Abinadab, and the third Shammah. 
1Sam 17:14 David was the youngest. The three eldest had followed Saul, 
1Sam 17:15 while David went to and fro from Saul to feed his father’s sheep at Bethlehem.  ¶ 
1Sam 17:16 The Philistine drew near morning and evening and took his stand for forty days. 
1Sam 17:17 One day Jesse said to David his son, ‘Take now for your brothers a bushel of this parched grain and these ten loaves and carry them quickly to the camp to your brothers. 
1Sam 17:18 But bring these ten cheeses to the commander of their thousand and look after your brothers’ welfare and bring back some token of assurance from them.  ¶ 
1Sam 17:19 They are with Saul and all the men of Israel in the valley of Elah fighting with the Philistines.’  ¶ 
1Sam 17:20 So David rose up early in the morning and left the flock with a keeper and went, as Jesse had commanded him. He came to the encampments just as the army was going forth to the battle-array, shouting the war cry. 
1Sam 17:21 Israel and the Philistines drew up the line of battle, army confronting army. 
1Sam 17:22 David left his vessels in the charge of the keeper of the baggage and ran to the line of battle and came and asked for the welfare of his brothers. 
1Sam 17:23 Just as he was talking with them, the champion, the Philistine of Gath, Goliath by name, came up out of the ranks of the Philistines and spoke the same words as before, and David heard them.  ¶ 
1Sam 17:24 All the men of Israel, when they saw the man, fled from him and were greatly afraid. 
1Sam 17:25 ‘Have you seen this man who has come up?’ they said, ‘Surely he has come up to insult Israel. Whoever kills him, the king will greatly enrich and will give him his daughter and will make his father’s house free in Israel.’ 
1Sam 17:26 Then David spoke to the men who stood by him, ‘What should be done for the man who strikes that Philistine and takes away the reproach from Israel? For who is this uncircumcised Philistine, that he has dared to insult the armies of the living God?’ 
1Sam 17:27 The people answered him in the words just given, ‘This is what will be done to the man who kills him.’  ¶ 
1Sam 17:28 Eliab his eldest brother heard when he spoke to the men. Eliab’s anger was kindled against David, and he said, ‘Why have you come down? With whom have you left those few sheep in the wilderness? I know you well and the wickedness of your heart. You have come down to see the battle.’ 
1Sam 17:29 David said, ‘What have I done now? It was only a question.’ 
1Sam 17:30 Turning away from him to another, he spoke as before, and the people answered him again as at the first time.  ¶ 
1Sam 17:31 When the words were heard which David spoke, they reported them to Saul. They took him and brought him before Saul. 
1Sam 17:32 David said to Saul, ‘Let not my lord’s courage fail him. Your servant will go and fight with this Philistine.’ 
1Sam 17:33 Saul answered, ‘You are not able to go against this Philistine to fight with him. You are only a youth and he has been a warrior from his youth.’ 
1Sam 17:34 But David said to Saul, ‘Your servant was a shepherd with his father’s flock, and when a lion or a bear would come and take a lamb out of the flock, 
1Sam 17:35 I would go out after him and kill him and rescue the lamb from his mouth. If he rose up against me, I would seize him by his jaw and slay him with a blow. 
1Sam 17:36 Your servant has killed both lion and bear. Now this uncircumcised Philistine will be like one of them, since he has insulted the armies of the living God. 
1Sam 17:37 The  <c>Lord</c> who delivered me from the paw of the lion, and from the paw of the bear, will deliver me from the hand of this Philistine.’ So Saul said to David, ‘Go, and may the  <c>Lord</c> be with you.’  ¶ 
1Sam 17:38 Saul clothed David with his armour, and put a helmet of bronze on his head and clad him with a coat of mail. 
1Sam 17:39 David girded his sword over his coat and made a vain attempt to go, for he had not tried them. Then David said to Saul, I cannot go with these because I am not used to them. And he took them off.
