Esth 7:5 Then King Ahasuerus said to Queen Esther, ‘Who is he and where is he whose heart has impelled him to do this?’  ¶ 
Esth 7:6 ‘A foe, an enemy: this wicked Haman.’ Esther answered. Haman shrank in terror before the king and the queen. 
Esth 7:7 In his wrath the king rose from the place where he was drinking wine and went into the palace garden. Haman stayed to beg Queen Esther for his life, for he saw that the king was fully determined to bring calamity upon him. 
Esth 7:8 As the king returned from the palace garden to the banquet hall, Haman had flung himself on Esther’s couch. The king cried, ‘Is he going to rape my queen while I am present in my own house?’  ¶ As the king spoke these words, the attendants covered Haman’s face 
Esth 7:9 and Harbonah, one of those who waited on the king, said, ‘There are the gallows, seventy-five feet high, which Hainan erected for Mordecai, who spoke a good word in behalf of the king, standing in the house of Haman!’ The king said ‘Hang him on them.’ 
Esth 7:10 So they hanged Haman on the gallows that he had prepared for Mordecai. Then the wrath of the king was pacified.  ¶ 
Esth 8:1 At that time King Ahasuerus gave the property of Haman the Jews’ enemy to Queen Esther. Mordecai was made one of the king’s personal advisers, for Esther had disclosed his relationship to her. 
Esth 8:2 The king also drew off his signet ring, which he had taken from Haman. He gave it to Mordecai, and Esther placed Mordecai in charge of Haman’s property.  ¶ 
Esth 8:3 Then Esther sought another audience with the king and fell at his feet and with tears begged him to avert the evil planned by Haman the Agagite and to frustrate his designs against the Jews. 
Esth 8:4 The king held out to her the golden sceptre, and she arose and stood before him. 
Esth 8:5 ‘If it seems best to the king,’ she said, ‘and if I have won his favour and he thinks it right, and if I please him, let written orders be given to revoke the dispatches devised by Haman son of Hammedatha the Agagite, which he wrote ordering the destruction of the Jews who are in all the king’s provinces. 
Esth 8:6 For how can I bear to look upon the evil that will come to my people? How can I bear to see their destruction?’ 
Esth 8:7 Then King Ahasuerus said to Queen Esther and to Mordecai the Jew, ‘See, I have given Esther the property of Haman, and they have hanged him on the gallows, because he laid hands upon the Jews. 
Esth 8:8 Now you write on behalf of the Jews, as seems best to you, in the king’s name and seal it with the king’s signet ring. For a document that is written in the king’s name and sealed with the king’s signet ring cannot be revoked.’  ¶ 
Esth 8:9 On the twenty-third day of the third month (that is the month of Sivan), the king’s secretaries were summoned and as Mordecai instructed an edict was issued to the Jews, to the satraps and provincial governors and the rulers of each of the one hundred twenty-seven provinces from India to Ethiopia in their own script and their own language, and to the Jews in their own script and language.  ¶ 
Esth 8:10 Mordecai wrote in the name of King Ahasuerus. He sealed it with the king’s signet ring. Dispatches were sent by mounted couriers who rode the swift, noble steeds, bred of the royal studs. 
Esth 8:11 In this way the king permitted the Jews who were in every city to gather together and make a stand for their life, to destroy, to kill, and annihilate all the armed forces of any people or province that might be hostile to them, including their children and women, and to take their goods as plunder 
Esth 8:12 throughout all the provinces of King Ahasuerus on that thirteenth day of the twelfth month (which is called Adar). 
Esth 8:13 A copy of the edict was to be published as a decree in every province – publicly displayed so that the Jews might be ready for that day and avenge themselves. 
Esth 8:14 So the couriers who rode the swift, noble steeds went out, hastened and impelled by the king’s commands!  ¶ Meantime the decree had been given out in the royal palace at Susa; 
Esth 8:15 and Mordecai had gone out from the presence of the king in royal garments of violet and white and with a great crown of gold and with a robe of fine linen and purple. The people of Susa shouted and were glad. 
Esth 8:16 To the Jews there came light and gladness and joy and honour. 
Esth 8:17 And in every province and city, wherever the king’s command and decree came, there was gladness and joy among the Jews and a holiday. Many of the peoples of the earth professed to be Jews, for fear of the Jews took possession of them.  ¶ 
Esth 9:1 Now in the twelfth month (that is the month of Adar), on the thirteenth day, when the king’s command and his decree was about to put into execution, on the day that the enemies of the Jews hoped to gain the mastery over them, then the tables were turned so that the Jews had the mastery over those who hated them. 
Esth 9:2 The Jews gathered together in the cities throughout all the provinces of King Ahasuerus, to attack anyone who tried to harm them. No one could withstand them, for the fear of them had fallen on all the peoples. 
Esth 9:3 All the princes of the provinces and the satraps and the governors and they who attended to the king’s business, helped the Jews, because the fear of Mordecai had fallen on them. 
Esth 9:4 For Mordecai was great in the king’s palace, and as his power increased his fame spread throughout all the provinces. 
Esth 9:5 The Jews put all their enemies to the sword and, with slaughter and destruction, they did what they wanted to those who hated them. 
Esth 9:6 In Susa the capital the Jews killed five hundred people. 
Esth 9:7 They killed Parshandatha, Dalphon, Aspatha, 
Esth 9:8 Poratha, Adalia, Aridatha, 
Esth 9:9 Parmashta, Arisia, Aridai, and Vaizatha, 
Esth 9:10 the ten sons of Haman the son of Hammedatha, the Jews’ enemy; but they did not take any plunder.  ¶ 
Esth 9:11 On that day the number of those who were slain in Susa was brought before the king, 
Esth 9:12 and the king said to Queen Esther, ‘The Jews have slain five hundred people in Susa, and the ten sons of Haman. What then have they done in the rest of the king’s provinces! Now what is your petition? It will be granted to you. What is your request? It will be done.’  ¶ 
Esth 9:13 ‘If it please the king,’ Esther said, ‘let it be granted to the Jews who are in Susa to do tomorrow also according to this day’s decree. Let the bodies of Haman’s ten sons be hanged on the gallows.’ 
Esth 9:14 And the king commanded it to be done. A decree was given out in Susa and they hung the bodies of Haman’s ten sons on the gallows. 
Esth 9:15 The Jews who were in Susa gathered themselves together again on the fourteenth day of the month of Adar. They killed three hundred people in Susa. But they did not take any plunder. 
Esth 9:16 And the other Jews who were in the king’s provinces gathered themselves together and fought for their lives and overcame their enemies. They killed seventy-five thousand who hated them. But they did not take any plunder. 
Esth 9:17 This was on the thirteenth day of Adar. <br> ¶ On the fourteenth day of the month Adar the Jews rested and made it a day of feasting and rejoicing. 
Esth 9:18 (But the Jews in Susa gathered on both the thirteenth and fourteenth day – and rested on the fifteenth day of the same month and made it a day of feasting and rejoicing.)  ¶ 
Esth 9:19 This is why the Jews who live in the country villages keep the fourteenth day of the month of Adar as a day of rejoicing and feasting and a holiday, and a day in which they send gifts of food to each other.  ¶ 
Esth 9:20 Mordecai had these things recorded. He sent letters to all the Jews who were in all the provinces of the King Ahasuerus, both near and far. 
Esth 9:21 He told them to keep the fourteenth day of the month of Adar and also the fifteenth day every year, 
Esth 9:22 as the days on which the Jews had rest from their enemies, and the month which was turned from sorrow to gladness and from mourning into a feast day. They should make them days of feasting and gladness and of sending gifts of food to each other and of gifts to the poor.  ¶ 
Esth 9:23 So what the Jews had begun to do they adopted as a custom, just as Mordecai had written to them. 
Esth 9:24 For Haman the son of Hammedatha, the Agagite, the enemy of all the Jews, had plotted to destroy them. He had cast “Pur”, that is the lot, intending to consume them and to destroy them. 
Esth 9:25 But when the matter came before the king, he gave written orders that his wicked plot, which he had planned against the Jews, should come upon his own head, and that he and his sons should be hanged on the gallows. 
Esth 9:26 This is why these days are called Purim, after the word Pur. Therefore because of all the words of this letter, as well as all they had seen, and all they had experienced, 
Esth 9:27 the Jews established and made it a custom for them, for their descendants, and for all who should join them, so that it might not be repealed, that they should continue to observe these two days as feasts each year, 
Esth 9:28 and that these days should be remembered and kept throughout every generation, every family, every province, and every city. And these days of Purim should not pass away from among the Jews nor the remembrance of them disappear among their descendants.  ¶ 
Esth 9:29 Queen Esther, the daughter of Abihail, gave Mordecai the Jew all authority in writing to confirm this second letter of Purim. 
Esth 9:30 He sent letters to all the Jews, to the hundred and twenty-seven provinces of the kingdom of Ahasuerus, wishing them peace and security, 
Esth 9:31 to confirm these days of Purim in their proper times, to be observed as Mordecai the Jew and Queen Esther had directed and as the Jews had proscribed for themselves and their descendants, in the matter of the fastings and their cry of lamentation. 
Esth 9:32 And the commands of Esther confirmed these matters of Purim; and it was written in the records. <br> ¶ 
Esth 10:1 King Ahasuerus imposed a tribute on the land and the coasts. 
Esth 10:2 All the acts of his power and of his might, and the full account of the greatness of Mordecai to which the king advanced him, are they not recorded in the book of the chronicles of the kings of Media and Persia? 
Esth 10:3 For Mordecai the Jew was next in rank to King Ahasuerus, and great among the Jews, and loved by them all. He sought the good of his people and promoted the welfare of their descendants.  ¶ 
Job 1:1 In the land of Uz there was a man called Job– a man blameless and upright, who feared God and 
Job 1:2 shunned evil. He had a family of seven sons and 
Job 1:3 three daughters: and he owned seven thousand sheep, three thousand camels, five hundred yoke of oxen, five hundred she-asses, and a vast train of servants, so that he was the richest man in all the 
Job 1:4 East. Now his sons used to hold feast day about, and they would send and invite their three sisters 
Job 1:5 to eat and drink with them; and when the cycle of feasts was over, Job used to send for them and prepare them for worship, rising early and offering burnt offerings for them all: for – said Job– <br>		Perchance my children have sinned <br>		And cursed God in their heart. And this Job never failed to do.  ¶ 
Job 1:6 Now on a certain day the heavenly Beings came to present themselves before Jehovah, and 
Job 1:7 among them came Satan. Then Jehovah asked Satan where he had come from, and Satan answered Jehovah thus, "From ranging the earth and from 
Job 1:8 walking up and down it." Then Jehovah said to Satan: <br>	"Hast thou noted my servant Job, <br>		That on earth there is none like him– <br>	A man blameless and upright, <br>		Who fears God and shuns evil?" <br>	
Job 1:9 To this Satan made answer: <br>	But is it for nothing that Job fears God? <br>	
Job 1:10 Hast Thou not Thyself fenced him and his house, <br>		And all he possesses on every side? <br>	The work of his hands Thou hast blessed, <br>		And his substance abounds in the land. <br>	
Job 1:11 But put forth Thy hand and touch all he possesses, <br>		And assuredly then to Thy face he will curse Thee." <br>	
Job 1:12 Whereat Jehovah said to Satan: <br>	"See! all he possesses is in thy power, <br>		But lay not thy hand on the man himself." <br>	Then forth Satan went from the presence of Jehovah. 
Job 1:13 Now on a certain day, as his sons and daughters Were eating and drinking wine in the house of their 
Job 1:14 eldest brother, suddenly a messenger appeared before Job with the tidings: <br>	"The oxen were hard at the plough; <br>		And the asses were feeding beside them, <br>	
Job 1:15 When sabeans fell upon them and seized them; <br>		The servants they slew with the sword– <br>		Only I alone am escaped to tell thee." <br>	
Job 1:16 While he was still speaking, another came and said: <br>		"The fire of God has fallen from heaven, <br>		And burnt to a cinder the sheep and the servants– <br>		Only I alone am escaped to tell thee." <br>	
Job 1:17 While he was still speaking, another came and said: <br>	"Chaldeans, formed into three bands, <br>		Made a raid on the camels and seized them. <br>	The servants they slew with the sword– <br>		Only I alone am escaped to tell thee." <br>	
Job 1:18 While he was still speaking, another came and said: <br>	"Thy sons and thy daughters were eating and drinking <br>		In the house of their eldest brother: <br>	
Job 1:19 On a sudden a mighty wind <br>		From the other side of the desert <br>	came and smote and four sides of the house, <br>		That it fell on the young folk and killed them– <br>		Only I alone am escaped to tell thee." <br>	
Job 1:20 Then Job rose and rent his robe; and, after shaving <br>	his head, he threw himself with these words pros- <br>	trate upon the ground: <br>	
Job 1:21 "Naked came I from my mother’s womb, <br>		And naked thither must I return. <br>	Jehovah hath given, Jehovah hath taken: <br>		The name of Jehovah be blessed." <br>	
Job 1:22 In all this Job committed no sin, nor did he charge <br>	God with unseemly dealing.  ¶ 
Job 2:1 Now on a certain day the heavenly Beings came to present themselves before Jehovah, and among them came Satan to present himself before Jehovah. 
Job 2:2 Then Jehovah asked Satan where he had come from, and satan answered Jehovah thus, "From ranging the earth and from walking up and down it." 
Job 2:3 Then Jehovah said to Satan: <br>	"Hast thou noted my servant Job, <br>		That on earth there is none like him– <br>	A man blameless and upright, <br>		Who fears God and shuns evil? <br>	And still he clings to his honour– <br>		In vain hast thou set me on to destroy him." <br>	
Job 2:4 To this Satan made answer: <br>		"Skin for skin; <br>		All a man’s goods will he give for his life. <br>	
Job 2:5 But put forth Thy hand, touch his bone and his flesh <br>		And assuredly then to Thy face he will curse Thee." <br>	
Job 2:6 Whereat Jehovah said to Satan: <br>		"See! he is on thy power, <br>		But take heed that thou spare his life." <br>	
Job 2:7 Then forth Satan went from the presence of Jehovah.  ¶ And he smote Job from the sole of his foot to the 
Job 2:8 crown of his head with boils so grievous that he took a potsherd to scratch with; and, as he was 
Job 2:9 sitting among the ashes, his wife said to him: <br>	"Art thou clinging still to thine honour? <br>		Curse God and die." <br>	
Job 2:10 But Job said to her: <br>		"Must thou too speak <br>		As a foolish women speak? <br>	We accept from God what is good: <br>		Shall we not accept what is evil?" <br>	In all this Job was guilty of no sin of speech.  ¶ 
Job 2:11 When Job’s three friends heard of all the misery that had come upon him, they travelled each man from his own place – Eliphaz the Temabite, Bildad the Shuhite, and Zophar the Naamathite; for they had made a tyrst together to come to condole with 
Job 2:12 him and comfort him. But when they caught a glimpse of him at a distance they did not recognize him. Then every man of them wept aloud and tore his robe and scattered dust heavenwards upon 
Job 2:13 his head. Then they sat down beside him upon the ground seven days and nights, and no one said a word to him; for they saw that his pain was very great.  ¶ 
Job 3:1 Thereafter Job opened his mouth to curse his 
Job 3:2 day, and thus he began: <br>	
Job 3:3 Perished the day wherein I was born, <br>		And the night which announced that a man-child had come. <br>
